(a)  No exclusive franchise or privilege shall be granted. No franchise or privilege shall begin at any time after six months subsequent to the taking effect of the ordinance granting the same. No franchise or privilege shall be extended directly or indirectly beyond the term originally fixed by the ordinance granting same. 
(b)  An application for the renewal of a franchise or the granting of a new one may be considered and acted upon prior to the expiration date of the current franchise so that the new franchise may take effect upon the expiration date of the other; provided, however, that the procedure prescribed herein for the original granting of such franchise is followed in all particulars. 
(Code 1982, § 27.202; Code 1995, § 27.202) 
Sec. 2-339. - Powers of city over franchise holders. 
(a)  The city shall have the right and power, acting through the council, to determine, fix, and regulate the charges, fares, or rates of any person enjoying or that may enjoy a franchise or exercise any other public privilege in the city and to prescribe the kind of service to be furnished by such person and the manner in which it shall be rendered. From time to time the city may alter or change such rules, regulations, and compensation. 
(b)  The city shall have the power and authority to require extensions, betterments, and improvements of the service that may be rendered by the holder of a franchise and shall likewise have the power to prevent the making of unnecessary or unprofitable extensions. 
(Code 1982, § 27.203; Code 1995, § 27.203) 
Sec. 2-340. - Conditions of franchises. 
    Each franchise granted by the council shall provide: 
(1)  Compensation to be paid to the city for the use and occupancy of the public property, which the compensation may be a fixed fee, or may be measured by gross receipts, or some other method mutually agreeable to the parties. Such compensation may be changed from time to time by mutual consent. 
(2)  The length of time that such franchise shall continue in effect; provided, however, that no franchise shall be granted for a period longer than 25 years. 
(3)  A method of accounting applicable to the particular business conducted by the grantee. 
(4)  Provisions for the maintenance of sufficient depreciation reserves so that the integrity of the property used and useful in rendering the public service may be maintained. Each franchise shall specify the purposes for which the depreciation reserves may be used. In determining the amount and character of reserves required it shall be proper to resort to current common practices applicable to the particular utility concern. 
(5)  Recapture provisions whereby the city shall have the right to cancel the franchise and purchase the property of the franchise holder at a price to be determined according to the formula or method agreed upon in the franchise when granted. 
(6)  That the procedure to be followed in ordering the making of extensions, betterments, or permanent improvements of the service by the city or considering applications by the grantee for permission to make extensions enlargement or betterments, be prescribed. 
(7)  That no rate of return shall exceed a fair return upon the fair value of the property used and useful in rendering the public service. 
(8)  That the grantee may be required, at grantee's expense, to conform its installations in the streets, alleys, and public ways to any changes of grade made by the city. 
(9)  That no franchise shall be assigned without the written consent of the council, which shall be evidenced by a resolution or an ordinance. 
(Code 1982, § 27.204; Code 1995, § 27.204) 
Sec. 2-341. - Investigations and public hearings. 
(a)  The council shall have full power to examine or cause to be examined at any time, and at all times, the books, papers, and records of franchise holders; to take testimony and compel the attendance of witnesses and the production of books, papers, and records and to examine witnesses under oath and under such rules and regulations as it may adopt. 
(b)  Should any franchise holder refuse to permit the inspection of such books, papers, or records by the council or by any one designated by it to make such inspection, or fail to produce the same when notified to do so by the council, or should any officer, agent, or employee of such franchise holder refuse to give testimony before the council, the council shall have the power by ordinance to declare the franchise or privilege enjoyed by such person in default, and terminated. 
(c)  The council shall have the power to call a public hearing, giving reasonable notice to the holder of a franchise, to determine whether or not an application to increase rates shall be granted or to determine whether or not the rates currently charged by any holder of a franchise for the service rendered are excessive. In that connection, the council shall have full power to examine the book, papers, and records of the franchise holder, and to compel the attendance of all witnesses deemed necessary for the ascertainment of the facts in connection with the inquiry. Failure to obey and subpoena to appear as a witness shall be punishable by the council for contempt by any appropriate proceedings permitted by law. 
(Code 1982, § 27.205; Code 1995, § 27.205) 
Chapter 4 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Alcoholic beverages, V.T.C.A., Alcoholic Beverage Code § 1.01 et seq.; alcoholic beverage permit and license fees authorized, V.T.C.A., Alcoholic Beverage Code §§ 11.38, 61.36; location restrictions for sale of beer and wine authorized, V.T.C.A., Alcoholic Beverage Code § 109.31 et seq.; local option provisions, V.T.C.A., Alcoholic Beverage Code § 251.71 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 4-1. - Penalty. 
    Each violation of this chapter shall be punishable by fine of not less than $10.00 or more than $500.00, and each day making a separate offense. 
(Code 1995, § 15.302; Ord. No. 676, 9-9-1990) 
Sec. 4-2. - Distance restriction for sale or consumption of alcohol. 
    The sale or consumption of alcoholic beverages within 300 feet of a church, public school, or public hospital is prohibited. 
(Code 1995, § 15.202; Ord. No. 676, 9-9-1990) 
Sec. 4-3. - Zoning limitations. 
    The sale of alcoholic beverages is to be limited to certain specific zoned areas as set forth in chapter 50. 
(Code 1995, § 15.203; Ord. No. 676, 9-9-1990) 
Secs. 4-4-4-24. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PERMITS AND LICENSES 

Sec. 4-25. - Required. 
    No person shall sell within the city an alcoholic beverage without having first obtained a permit or license as required by this article. 
(Code 1995, § 15.301; Ord. No. 676, 9-9-1990) 
Sec. 4-26. - Package stores and wine and beer retailers permits. 
    An annual permit fee equal to an amount of exactly one-half of that levied by the state is levied upon all package stores and all wine and beer retailers located within the city unless excepted by state law. This permit fee shall be levied on all package stores whether they sell all or any part of the classifications of intoxicating beverages. These fees are levied pursuant to the provisions of V.T.C.A., Alcoholic Beverage Code § 11.38. 
(Code 1995, § 15.101; Ord. No. 676, 9-9-1990) 
Sec. 4-27. - Mixed beverage on-premises permits. 
    An annual permit fee equal to an amount of exactly one-half of that levied by the state is levied upon all mixed beverage permits (which includes the sale of wine, beer, ale, and malt liquor for consumption on the licensed premises). The fee levied pursuant to this section shall apply after the three-year exemption period (following the issuance of the applicant's state permit) established by V.T.C.A., Alcoholic Beverage Code § 11.38. 
(Code 1995, § 15.102; Ord. No. 676, 9-9-1990) 
Sec. 4-28. - Manufacture, distribution, or sale of beer licenses. 
    An annual license fee in an amount of exactly one-half of that levied by the state is levied upon all licensed by the state to manufacture, distribute, or sell beer, (except a temporary or agent's beer license) within the city. These fees are levied pursuant to the provisions of V.T.C.A., Alcoholic Beverage Code § 61.36. 
(Code 1995, § 15.103; Ord. No. 676, 9-9-1990) 
Sec. 4-29. - Place and time of fee payment. 
    All original permit fees and license fees shall be paid to the city manager at city hall. All renewal fees shall be due to the city manager at city hall on, or before, the expiration of the anniversary date of its issuance. 
(Code 1995, § 15.104; Ord. No. 676, 9-9-1990) 
Chapter 6 - ANIMALS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Local Public Health Reorganization Act, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 121.001 et seq.; treatment of animals, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 821.001 et seq.; dangerous dogs, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 822.001 et seq.; Rabies Control Act of 1981, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.001 et seq.; animal health, V.T.C.A., Occupations Code § 801.001 et seq.; cruelty to livestock animals, V.T.C.A., Penal Code § 42.09; livestock, V.T.C.A., Agriculture Code § 141.001 et seq.; registration of dogs and cats, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.031; protection of birds, nests, and eggs, V.T.C.A., Parks and Wildlife Code § 64.002 et seq.; vaccination of dogs and cats, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.021; restraint of dogs and cats, impoundment, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.033; quarantine of animals, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.042 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 6-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Abandoned animal means any animal that has been deprived of any of the necessities of life including air, food, water, medical care, exercise, or shelter. The term "abandoned animal" also means those animals left unclaimed at the city animal control facility 72 hours after the owners have been notified and admitted ownership and then failed to retrieve the animal. 
    Adult dog or cat is a dog or cat more than four months old. 
    Animal means any living vertebrate or invertebrate, domesticated or wild, not including man. 
    Animal care facility means the facility operated by the city for the impounding of domesticated and wild animals. Facility operations include impounding and caring for stray, abandoned, or unwanted animals until the animals are reclaimed by an owner, adopted, surrendered to a humane receiving facility. 
    Animal control officer means a competent individual appointed by the city manager, and who shall take the basic animal control officer certification training offered by the state department of health. The appointed animal control officer shall be qualified to perform such duties under the laws of this state and this chapter. 
    Animal nuisance means any animal or animals that unreasonably annoy humans, endanger the life or health of other animals or persons, or substantially interfere with the rights of citizens, other than their owners, to enjoyment of life or property. The term "animal nuisance" means, but is not limited to, a public nuisance created within the corporate limits of the city by the following acts or omissions of animal owners: 
(1)  The keeping of an animal in such a manner whereby the animal is free of restraint to repeatedly roam or run at large, at will; 
(2)  The keeping of an animal that barks or whines in such a manner, with such intensity, or with such continued duration, so as to annoy, distress, or disturb the quiet comfort or repose of persons of normal nervous sensibilities within the vicinity of hearing thereof; 
(3)  The keeping of an animal that bites or injures other animals or humans without provocation; 
(4)  The keeping of an animal that has a propensity to damage or destroy public property or the property of a person other than its owners' private property; 
(5)  The keeping of an animal that runs at large and defecates or urinates on public or property of a person other than its owners' private property; or 
(6)  The keeping of an animal that trespasses on school grounds, chases vehicles, molests or intimidates pedestrians or passersby, or attacks other domestic animals. 
    Animal registration means the annual process by which animals covered by this chapter are registered with the city; such registration includes paying the appropriate fee and providing proof of rabies vaccination in the year for which the animal registration has been issued. 
    Animal shelter means any of a number of facilities that keep or legally impound stray, homeless, abandoned, or unwanted animals. 
    At large means off the premises of the owner, and not under the control of the owner or a responsible person by leash, cord, chain, or other humane and effective method. 
    Bee means any insect species of the bee family. 
    Beekeeper means a person who owns, leases, or manages one or more colonies of bees for pollination or the production of honey, beeswax or other byproducts. 
    Cat means a felis catus, including cat hybrid, both the male and the female. 
    Dangerous dogs has the same meaning provided in V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 822.041. 
    Disposal means any of the methods by which animals are removed from the care of the city animal control facility. The term "disposal" may include, but is not limited to: 
(1)  Returning the animal to its rightful owner. 
(2)  Transferring the animal to another animal care facility (also known as a humane receiving facility) or breed rescue group or other such entities. 
(3)  Transferring the animal to a licensed veterinarian for euthanasia or adoption. 
(4)  Adopting the animal to a new owner. 
    Dog means a canis familiaris, including dog hybrid, both the male and the female. 
    Domestic animal means any animal such as cat or dog adapted to life in intimate association with and to the advantage of man. 
    Euthanasia means the humane destruction of an animal accomplished by a method that produces rapid unconsciousness and subsequent death without evidence of pain and distress, or a method that uses anesthesia produced by an agent that causes painless loss of consciousness and subsequent death. 
    Feral means having escaped from domestication and reverted to a wild state. 
    Guard dog means a dog that is housed on a premises for the purposes of protecting humans or property. 
    Guide dog means a domestic dog that is in service to a legally blind or deaf person. 
    High-risk animal means raccoons, foxes, bats, skunks, coyotes, and any other animals so identified by the state with a high chance of transmitting rabies. 
    Humane receiving facility means any shelter, humane society organization, or any other agency or group or individual that has an ongoing adoption program or rescues animals for placement, whether to the public or private. 
    Hybrid means any offspring of two animals of different species. 
    Implant means an electronic animal identification device or EAID. 
    Impoundment means the collecting and confining of an animal. 
    Impoundment area means the city's animal care facility. 
    Intact means any animal that has not been spayed or neutered. 
    Local rabies control authority means that individual appointed by the city manager to conduct all duties and responsibilities of a rabies control authority as defined in V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.017. 
    Observation period means the time following a bite incident during which the biting animal's health status is monitored for signs of rabies. 
    Owner means any person who harbors or keeps, or causes or permits to be harbored or kept, or has an animal in his care or custody, or permits an animal to remain on or about his premises for 72 hours or longer. 
    Police dog means any domestic dog that is owned or employed by a governmental law enforcement agency. 
    Quarantine means the detention or isolation of an animal suspected of carrying an infectious or contagious disease. 
    Quarantine facility means any shelter or veterinary clinic that is licensed by the state department of health to quarantine suspect animals for the rabies observation period. 
    Rabies means an acute virus disease of the nervous system of any warm blooded animals, usually transmitted through the bite of a rabid animal. 
    Rabies vaccination means protective inoculation against rabies with an antirabies vaccine recognized by a veterinarian and administered under his direct supervision. 
    Restraint means any animal secured by a leash or lead of sufficient strength and length and under the control of a responsible person and obedient to that person's commands. 
    Stray animal means any domestic animal not under restraint. 
    Tagged means any animal that displays on a collar around its neck an animal registration either from the city or from another recognized municipal entity. 
    Tattoo means that method of permanently marking a domestic animal to indicate ownership. 
    Vaccination certificate means a document showing on its face that the animal described thereon has received a current inoculation of anti-rabies vaccine inscribed with the date of the inoculation and the name of the animal's owner and signed by a licensed veterinarian. 
    Veterinarian means a person licensed to practice veterinary medicine in the state. 
    Veterinary hospital means any establishment maintained and operated by a veterinarian for surgery, diagnosis of and treatment of diseases and injuries of animals. 
    Vicious animal means an animal that habitually or repeatedly without provocation chases, snaps at, attacks, or bites any person or domestic animal. 
    Wild animal means any nonhuman primate, raccoon, skunk, fox, wolf, leopard, panther, tiger, lion, lynx, bobcat, dog or cat hybrid, or any poisonous or dangerous snake that can be found in an untamed state. The term "wild animal" excludes all domestic animals. The term "wild animal" includes, but not by way of exclusion, deer, opossums, and squirrels. 
(Code 1995, § 3.101) 
Sec. 6-2. - Fees. 
    All registration, impoundment, boarding and other fees referred to in this chapter shall be in the amount provided in the city fee schedule. 
(Code 1995, § 3.501) 
Secs. 6-3-6-22. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 6-23. - Animal control officer. 
(a)  Appointment. The city manager will appoint an animal control officer and will ensure that the appointed individual takes the basic animal control officer certification training offered by the state department of health. The individual should attend the training within six months of being appointed animal control officer, and shall also maintain continuing education in the area of animal control through the state department of health at the rate of a minimum of ten hours per year. The appointed animal control officer shall be responsible for successfully performing all requirements as directed by this chapter. 
(b)  Duties. The city animal control officer is responsible for developing and implementing effective procedures for responding to resident requests for animal assistance as specified in this chapter, including response to reports of dangerous dogs, and safely and humanely conducting animal impoundment, care, and disposal. If the animal control officer is appointed also as the local rabies control authority, he shall fulfill all the duties and responsibilities required by that office. 
(Code 1995, § 3.103(b), (e)) 
State Law reference- Animal control officer defined, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 829.001. 
Sec. 6-24. - Local rabies control authority. 
(a)  Appointment. The city manager shall designate an individual to act as the local rabies control authority to carry out all related duties as described in V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 826. The individual designated as the local rabies control authority may be the county health officer, municipal health officer, animal control officer, peace officer, or any entity that the city manager considers appropriate. 
(b)  Duties. Among other duties, the local rabies control authority shall enforce this chapter and state law and rules that comprise the minimum standards for rabies control. 
(Code 1995, § 3.103(a), (c)) 
Sec. 6-25. - Interference with officials and facilities prohibited. 
    No person shall interfere with, hinder, or molest any city employee in the performance of the employee's duties under this chapter. It is further unlawful for any person to remove without permission of the city animal control officer to remove or turn loose impounded animals or to damage or destroy any cage, fence, or other part of the city animal care facility. 
(Code 1995, § 3.104(g)) 
Sec. 6-26. - Authority for euthanization of wild animals. 
    The animal control officer may order the seizure and humane euthanasia of any wild animal found in the city. 
(Code 1995, § 3.104(f)) 
Sec. 6-27. - Citations. 
    The animal control officer or a city police officer may, at his discretion, issue a citation for any violation of this chapter. 
(Code 1995, § 3.502(c)) 
Sec. 6-28. - Penalties. 
(a)  Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this chapter or fail to comply with any of the provisions thereof, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, and upon conviction shall be fined in a sum not less than $10.00 and not more than $500.00, unless specifically listed on the minimum penalty schedule in subsection (c) of this section. Each day of violation shall constitute a separate and distinct offense. 
(b)  Subsequent convictions for any violation of this chapter within a 12-month period shall double the minimum applicable fine listed in subsection (c) of this section, up to and including the maximum allowed by law. 
(c)  Upon conviction of the specific violation listed, the minimum fine shall be as follows: 
Animal abandonment $ 50.00 No rabies vaccination   30.00 Not registered - 1st offense   10.00 Not registered - 2nd offense   30.00 Not registered - 3rd offense  100.00 Running at large (plus impound fee)   25.00 More than 4 dogs or cats   25.00 Failure to surrender for rabies observation  200.00  
(d)  Nothing in this section shall limit the remedies available to the city in seeking to enforce the provisions of this chapter. 
(Code 1995, § 3.502(a), (b), (f)) 
Sec. 6-29. - Revocation of registration for animal care violations. 
    If any person is found guilty by a court of violating the animal care requirements of this chapter, that person's registration to own, keep, harbor, or have custody of animals shall be deemed automatically revoked and no new registration may be issued. 
(Code 1995, § 3.502(a)) 
Sec. 6-30. - Appeals to city manager. 
(a)  A person aggrieved by an action of the city in amending, limiting, defining, suspending, or revoking any approval required by this chapter may request a hearing before the city manager or his appointed supervisory officer. 
(b)  A hearing must be requested in writing and filed with the city manager within ten days of the protested decision or action by the aggrieved party. If no such request is received, the decision or action of the animal control officer becomes final. Any decision should include the written opinion of a licensed veterinarian when indicated. 
(c)  Based on the recorded evidence presented at the hearing, the city manager shall make a final finding and shall sustain, modify or rescind any notice or order considered in the hearing. 
(d)  Within five working days, a written report of the hearing decision shall be furnished to the person requesting the hearing by the animal control officer or the city manager. 
(Code 1995, § 3.503; Ord. No. 897, 7-10-2001; Ord. No. 1011, 12-9-2008) 
Secs. 6-31-6-48. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - IMPOUNDMENT[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Authority of municipality to impound and provide for humane disposition of unclaimed stray dogs and cats, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.033; treatment of impounded animals, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 821.002; animal shelters, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 823.001 et seq.; minimum standards for quarantine and impoundment facilities, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.051. 

Sec. 6-49. - Records. 
    When an animal is impounded, whether wild or domestic, the animal control officer shall maintain records on the impoundment. The animal control officer will establish procedures for record keeping to ensure all vital data on impounded animals are captured and stored in such a manner that data can be compiled and retrieved as necessary to assist in process improvement, budgeting, identifying trends, providing information to residents seeking lost pets, etc. 
(Code 1995, § 3.201(a)) 
Sec. 6-50. - Surrender of animal to shelter prohibited. 
    An owner shall not surrender their owned animal for impoundment in the city animal control facility at any time. 
(Code 1995, § 3.201(c)(4)) 
Sec. 6-51. - Dogs and cats at large. 
    Any dog or cat running at large contrary to this chapter, or that meets the provisions of state law regarding dangerous dogs, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 822.041 et seq. or is noticeably sick or injured and not in the care of an owner may be impounded by the city animal control officer or city police officer. Residents who have lost an animal should go to the city animal control facility to determine whether or not their pet has been impounded. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(k)(1)) 
State Law reference- Local regulation of dangerous dogs, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 822.047. 
Sec. 6-52. - Notice of impoundment. 
(a)  When an animal is impounded, the animal control officer shall develop procedures for posting notice on the city bulletin board located in the maintenance area to include a photograph and specific impoundment information on the animal and copies of the information to city dispatch for use in responding to resident inquiries. 
(b)  Within 24 hours of impoundment, the animal control officer shall attempt to contact the owner using information from tags, tattoos, or electronic animal identification devices that may be on the animal. 
(Code 1995, § 3.201(b), (c)(2)) 
Sec. 6-53. - Holding periods. 
(a)  Wild animals. The city animal control officer may contact the wildlife rescue and rehabilitation organization to arrange for no-cost transfer of non-high-risk wild animals when possible. The city animal control officer may destroy all wild animals if no other means of disposal is possible. 
(b)  Domestic animals. The holding period for impounded animals shall be a maximum of seven consecutive days that the facility is open to the public, during which time the animal control officer shall attempt to locate the owner. Under circumstances approved by the animal control officer, the animal may remain for a longer period. Upon contacting the owner, the owner shall have three days that the facility is open to the public from the time the notification is confirmed to retrieve the animal from the city. 
(c)  Sick or injured animals. There is no specific holding period for sick or injured animals without identification. The animal control officer will seek the advice of a licensed veterinarian to determine the extent of medical care needed to relieve suffering and, upon advice of the veterinarian, may arrange to have the veterinarian euthanize the injured or sick animal. 
(Code 1995, § 3.201(c)(1), (c)(2), (c)(2)(a), (c)(3)) 
Sec. 6-54. - Medical care for animals injured while at large. 
(a)  If an animal with city identification is injured while at large and the owner cannot be immediately contacted, the animal control officer will refer to the city registration application to see whether or not the owner agreed to pay for veterinary care. 
(b)  If the owner agrees, the animal control officer will obtain medical care for the animal as recommended by a licensed veterinarian. If the owner indicated at the time of registration with the city that he did not agree to pay for veterinary expenses, the animal control officer will consult with the licensed veterinarian to make the animal as comfortable as possible and will continue attempts to contact the owner. 
(c)  Animals without identification will be given veterinary treatment on a case by case basis as determined appropriate by the animal control officer in consultation with a licensed veterinarian. 
(Code 1995, § 3.201(c)(3)) 
State Law reference- Treatment of impounded animals, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 821.002; animal shelters, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 823.001 et seq.; minimum standards for quarantine and impoundment facilities, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.051. 
Sec. 6-55. - Release of impounded animal to owner. 
(a)  Impounded animals will be released to the owner when the following conditions have been satisfied: 
(1)  Provide proof of ownership by way of a registration and rabies vaccination certificate, bill of sale, photograph, affidavits from neighbors, or other reliable documentary evidence. The city may also require a sworn statement of ownership. 
(2)  Provide proof of rabies vaccination and registration tag. No dog or cat shall be released from the city without a current rabies vaccination and registration information. Owners will be encouraged to spay or neuter intact pets. 
(3)  Pay all impoundment fees, daily boarding costs, medical expenses, and other costs related to such impoundment as set by the animal control officer. 
(b)  If the owner does not retrieve the animal within three days that the facility is open to the public after confirmation of notification, the animal becomes the property of the city. 
(c)  The city animal control officer is responsible for ensuring that all requirements of this section are met, including but not limited to citing the owner for violating any section of this chapter and ensuring that all fees are paid before release. 
(Code 1995, § 3.201(c)(2), (d)) 
Sec. 6-56. - Adoption of unclaimed animals. 
    If the owner of an animal without identification cannot be located within three days that the facility is open to the public, then the animal control officer may arrange to adopt out the animal. 
(Code 1995, § 3.201(d)(2)) 
Sec. 6-57. - Destruction of healthy animals prohibited. 
    Healthy animals under the care of the city animal control officer will not be destroyed by city personnel under any circumstances. 
(Code 1995, § 3.201(d)(3)) 
Sec. 6-58. - Transfer of unclaimed animal to alternate facilities. 
(a)  If at the end of three days that the facility is open to the public an animal has not been claimed or adopted, the animal control officer will arrange with a humane receiving facility or breed rescue group to receive the animal. 
(b)  If at the end of the holding period an animal has not been claimed, adopted or transferred to a humane receiving facility or breed rescue group, the animal may be transported to the San Antonio animal control facility or, in the case of sick or injured animals as specified in section 6-59, euthanized by a licensed veterinarian. 
(c)  The animal will be transported in a safe and humane manner to the receiving facility. The term "safe and humane" means that the animal will be transported in a secured cage. Such cage should be covered. 
(Code 1995, § 3.201(d)(3)) 
Sec. 6-59. - Euthanization of sick or injured animals and feral cats. 
    The city will arrange with a licensed veterinarian to euthanize domestic animals or feral cats. Those animals certified by a licensed veterinarian as too sick or too injured to survive shall be euthanized by the licensed veterinarian. If no licensed veterinarian or certified euthanization technician is available, a city police officer may be summoned to destroy the injured animal. 
(Code 1995, § 3.201(e)) 
Secs. 6-60-6-89. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - ANIMAL CARE AND CONTROL COMMITTEE 

Sec. 6-90. - Members. 
(a)  Appointment. The city manager shall appoint a committee of interested individuals to fairly study animal care issues and advise the city council, recommending necessary action. 
(b)  Term; multiple terms encouraged. The term of membership shall be two years, with the city manager making interim appointments if a member is unable to complete his term. Members are encouraged to serve more than one term if at all practical. 
(c)  Composition of membership. The members of the committee will include the city manager, a certified law enforcement officer, and three or four city residents. 
(d)  Medical adviser. A licensed veterinarian practicing within the city limits will act as medical adviser to the committee on an as-needed basis. 
(Code 1995, § 3.301(a)) 
Sec. 6-91. - Meetings; duties. 
(a)  The committee shall meet at least twice a year. The committee shall visit the city animal care facility and will recommend actions deemed necessary or beneficial to the city on animal care and control issues. 
(b)  The committee chair will oversee and coordinate the actions of the individuals who wish to donate time, funds, or goods in support of the animals of the city. 
(c)  The committee may also convene at the direction of the committee chair to hear appeals of permit revocations. 
(Code 1995, § 3.301(b)) 
Secs. 6-92-6-110. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - REGISTRATION[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Authority of local governments to require registration of dogs and cats and collect fees therefor, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.031. 

Sec. 6-111. - City manager to develop procedures. 
    The city manager shall develop procedures for administering the animal registration and tagging program. 
(Code 1995, § 3.103(d)) 
Sec. 6-112. - Registration generally; complimentary registrations for service dogs. 
    The owner or keeper of any cat or dog more than four months old must be licensed by the city. Registration fees shall not be required for governmental police dogs or dogs depended upon by an individual with physical disabilities to alleviate or compensate for the person's disability or for any dog properly trained to guide or otherwise assist a person with physical disabilities. Such dogs shall be issued a complimentary registration upon the presentation of proof of rabies vaccination. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(d)(6); Ord. No. 897, 7-10-2001) 
Sec. 6-113. - Registration of guard dogs; control of dog during emergencies. 
    Any resident or business that maintains a dog for the purposes of protection must register that animal as such with the city and must post a clearly visible "Guard Dog on Premises" sign. Upon registration, guard dog owners must provide specific instructions on where the guard dogs are usually found on the premises during business and nonbusiness hours. Owners will be liable for the actions of the guard dogs with regard to the emergency personnel responding to the scene. In the event that the owner is not on the scene at the time of response, emergency personnel will take such action as deemed necessary to neutralize any threat posed by the guard dog on the premises. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(d)(9); Ord. No. 897, 7-10-2001) 
Sec. 6-114. - Procedure. 
(a)  Upon acceptance of the registration application and fee, the city or a licensed veterinarian shall issue a durable registration tag that is numbered consecutively and printed or impressed with the name of the city. The city shall assign a registration number to each animal registered with the city and shall give the owner or person having control of the animal the identification tag and a registration certificate. The city shall record the registration, including the age, breed, color, sex, and registration date. 
(b)  Owners must present a current certificate of rabies vaccination by a licensed veterinarian for registration. 
(c)  Veterinarians who issue registration tags for the city are hereby authorized to retain 25 percent of the fee to cover the cost of issuing the tag. The tags shall be designed so that they can be fastened or riveted to the animal's collar or harness. 
(d)  Cats are exempt from wearing registration tags. Dogs or cats that are tattooed or micro-chipped are also exempt from wearing tags, but proof of vaccination against rabies and registration with the city is required. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(d)(2); Ord. No. 897, 7-10-2001) 
Sec. 6-115. - Duplicate tags. 
    A duplicate tag will be issued upon payment of a replacement fee and presentation of the registration receipt. No refunds will be given for animals who die or when owners and animals move out of the city. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(d)(4); Ord. No. 897, 7-10-2001; Ord. No. 972, 11-14-2006) 
Sec. 6-116. - Animals to wear registration tags; exception. 
    Animals must wear registration tags at all times provided nothing in this section will be construed to require animals that are kept for show or exhibition purposes to wear such tags as long as the animals are otherwise under restraint. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(d)(3); Ord. No. 897, 7-10-2001) 
Sec. 6-117. - Unauthorized taking and use of tags prohibited. 
    Residents may not use a tag for any animal other than the animal for which the tag was issued; tags are not transferable. Also, it is unlawful to willingly take from any animal its tag. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(d)(7); Ord. No. 897, 7-10-2001) 
Sec. 6-118. - Disposition of registration revenue. 
    The fee collected for the registration of animals shall be used only to defray the costs of administering the animal control function of the city, including the costs of the registration and tags, and costs for related equipment, training, supplies, care, and disposition as allowed by state law. The city shall accurately record all amounts received into and paid out of the fees collected and such data shall be included in the city's monthly treasurer's report. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(d)(5); Ord. No. 897, 7-10-2001) 
Secs. 6-119-6-147. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - CARE AND CONTROL 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 6-148. - Number of animals allowed per household limited. 
    In all residential areas of the city, no household shall keep, shelter, maintain, or harbor more than four adult dogs or cats. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(c)) 
Sec. 6-149. - Keeping wild animals prohibited; exceptions. 
    It is unlawful for any person to keep anywhere in the city any wild animal, such as lions, bears, monkeys, panthers, wildcats or any other animal, large or small, not considered to be a domestic animal in this country. 
(Code 1995, § 3.104(b)) 
State Law reference- Dangerous wild animals, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 822.101 et seq.; predatory animals and animal pests, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 825.001 et seq. 
Sec. 6-150. - Keeping horses and pot belly pigs prohibited; exceptions. 
    It shall hereafter be unlawful to keep a horse or a pot belly pig in, on, or near any premises in the city unless the premises has at least one acre total area or unless the horse or pot belly pig shall be securely penned up in an enclosure which, at any given point hereon, shall be no less than 150 feet from the nearest residence not under ownership or possession of the horse or potbelly pig owner. Horses or potbelly pigs do not require registration with the city. 
(Code 1995, § 3.104(c)) 
Sec. 6-151. - Adequate food, shelter and health care. 
    Animal owners are responsible for providing their animals with what is necessary to ensure their species-specific health, physical, social, and behavioral needs are met. At a minimum, care will include adequate supplies of clean water and food, proper housing, prompt health care, and sufficient exercise. 
Sec. 6-152. - Cruelty to animals. 
    No person shall beat, cruelly ill treat, torment, overload, overwork, or otherwise abuse an animal, or cause, instigate, or permit any dogfight, cockfight, bullfight, or other combat between animals or between animals and humans. Such offense is punishable as a Class "A" misdemeanor. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(a)) 
Sec. 6-153. - Abandonment. 
    No person is allowed to abandon an animal within the city limits. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(b)) 
Sec. 6-154. - Exposing animals to poisonous substances prohibited. 
    No person shall expose any known poisonous substance, whether mixed with food or not so that the same may be attractive to any warm-blooded animal or human. It shall be sufficient to constitute a violation under this section that the poisonous substance was attractively exposed by such person in such a manner that the same may have been eaten or was in fact eaten by any warm-blooded animal or human, not intent or further culpable mental state shall be required to prove a prima facie violation. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(n)) 
Sec. 6-155. - Traffic in animals for scientific experimentation prohibited. 
    It is unlawful for city staff to sell, give, or offer any living animal to any person or institution for vivisection or experimentation; give or sell any living animal for resale purposes; or give or sell any living animal to any person, firm, or corporation, public or private, for breeding purposes. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(h)) 
Sec. 6-156. - Animal feces to be removed by owner. 
(a)  Owners are responsible for not allowing their animals to defecate on public or private property unless such owner immediately cleans up (i.e., picks up and removes waste). Those walking their animals off their own premises must have appropriate removal material on their person while walking such animals. 
(b)  Prosecution of any such individual for violating the control or cleanup requirements as of this section may be instituted in municipal court by any person filing a sworn written complaint charging such individual with such offense. 
(c)  Owners will be held liable for their animals that are identified as defecating on other than the owner's property without clean up. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(l)) 
Sec. 6-157. - Animals in moving vehicles. 
    Animals in moving vehicles are required to be inside or safely and humanely tethered or crated in the back of such open vehicles as trucks. Such tethering must ensure that the tethering precludes the animal from exiting the vehicle either partially or completely and keeps the animal safely inside the back of the vehicle. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(i)) 
Sec. 6-158. - Animals in parked vehicles. 
(a)  No animals shall be left inside a parked vehicle or in an open vehicle when the temperatures inside the parked vehicle or outside conditions (e.g., intense direct sun with no shade) shall constitute a health hazard. 
(b)  If a health hazard is indicated, a city police officer or the animal control officer shall determine whether or not the animal is in danger and shall attempt to locate the owner. If the owner cannot be located in a timely manner, the city police shall facilitate entry into the vehicle if necessary and the city police officer or animal control officer shall remove the animal for impoundment. 
(c)  The animal control officer shall leave notice on the vehicle that the animal has been impounded due to violation of this section. Owners may be issued a warning or may be fined. 
(d)  For every occurrence, owners will be responsible for reimbursing the city for all costs associated with impoundment of the animal. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(j)) 
Sec. 6-159. - Drive to notify city if animal is struck by motor vehicles. 
    Any person who strikes a large wild animal such as a deer with a motor vehicle with such force that the animal is killed or seriously injured should notify the animal control officer as soon as possible so the city can arrange for disposition of the carcass. Any person who strikes a domestic animal with a motor vehicle should notify the animal control officer so that steps can be taken to identify and contact the owner. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(q)) 
Sec. 6-160. - Duty upon finding lost domestic animals. 
    Residents who find an animal shall immediately notify the city animal control officer, providing a full description of the animal, where the animal was found, and any other information to assist in locating the rightful owner. After the established holding period for domestic animals has expired, the resident finding the animal may own the animal, and shall comply with all vaccination and spay or neuter requirements according to state law. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(s)) 
Sec. 6-161. - Deer feeders prohibited. 
    It is unlawful for any person to maintain a deer feeder within the city or to provide a significant amount of food in such a manner that encourages deer to feed repeatedly in a specific place. 
(Code 1995, § 3.104(a)) 
Sec. 6-162. - Trapping animals prohibited; exceptions. 
(a)  No person shall set up or allow to be set up on his property steel jaw traps, spring (mouse) traps with teeth or perforated edges on the holding mechanism, or any type of trap with a holding mechanism designed in such a fashion as to reasonably ensure the cutting, slicing, tearing, or otherwise traumatizing of the entrapped prey, for the purpose of ensnaring domestic or wild animals with the city. 
(b)  This section is not to be construed to include those traps designed to kill common rodents (e.g., rats, mice, and gophers), provided the owner is responsible for taking care that any of the above-the "rodent" traps are not placed or used on or about his property in such a manner as to reasonably ensure the trapping of any other domesticated or wild animal or human. 
(c)  It shall be a prima facie violation of this section that the traps proscribed in this section were, in fact, set up by the person in question, or were allowed to be set up by the person in question; no intent or further culpable mental state shall be required to prove such a prima facie violation. 
(d)  Residents may request from the city animal control officer temporary loan of humane traps for the purposes of trapping a nuisance wild animal or domestic animal. Humane traps shall be checked at least once every 12 hours by the resident requesting the trap. 
(e)  Humane care shall be provided for any trapped animals including the provision of food, water, and protection from environmental extremes, including heat, cold, and precipitation. 
(f)  Trapped domestic animals shall be turned over to the city animal control officer or returned to the animal's owner as soon as possible. 
(Code 1995, § 3.104(d)) 
Sec. 6-163. - Dangerous dogs. 
    The city will comply with the provisions of V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 822.041 et seq. when responding to reports of dangerous dogs. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(m)) 
Sec. 6-164. - High-risk wild animals. 
    The city shall be responsible for those situations involving animals designated by the state as "high-risk animals" (e.g., raccoons, foxes, bats, skunks, and coyotes). 
(Code 1995, § 3.104(e)) 
State Law reference- Dangerous wild animals, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 822.101 et seq.; predatory animals and animal pests, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 825.001 et seq. 
Sec. 6-165. - Report of suspected animal mistreatment. 
    Any resident who suspects mistreatment of animals should contact the animal control officer and request further investigation. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(r)) 
Secs. 6-166-6-183. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - DOGS AND CATS AT LARGE[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
State Law reference- Authority of municipality to impound stray dogs and cats, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.033; authority of municipalities to require restraint of dogs and cats, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.033. 

Sec. 6-184. - Confinement and leashing required; exception. 
(a)  Every owner of a dog, whether registered or unregistered (includes those animals under four months old), or any person having charge, care, custody or control of the same shall prevent such dog from running at large. It is unlawful for any person owning or in possession of a dog to permit it to be outside of such person's premises (unless in a motor vehicle), either upon the private property of another or upon the streets, alleys or other public places of the city, unless such dog shall be at all times under restraint. 
(b)  At all other times, a dog shall be confined to the realty or premises of the owner of such dog by a substantial fence of sufficient strength and height to prevent such dog from escaping therefrom, or inside a house on such premises, or secured on such premises by a leash consisting of a material of sufficient strength to prevent the dog from escaping from such premises. 
(c)  It is unlawful for the leash to be arranged in a manner that allows the dog to get on or across any street or other public land when such leash is stretched to its full length. Any dog so arranged shall be considered a nuisance to the public in general and shall be impounded. 
(d)  Although cats shall be exempt from the leash requirement while on the premises of the owner, any cat straying on the property of anyone except its owner shall be deemed a nuisance animal and will be subject to impoundment. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(k)(intro.)) 
Sec. 6-185. - Destruction of dangerous and biting animals. 
    Only those animals at large required to be tested for rabies and in rare instances those animals at large that prove to be too dangerous to catch or subdue by any other means may be destroyed by the animal control officer or city police. Any dog or cat found running at large may be destroyed if the domestic animal has bitten a person or other domestic animal and the biting animal must be tested for rabies. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(k)(2)) 
Sec. 6-186. - Use of catchpoles and anesthetics for capture. 
    For animals running at large that do not require rabies testing, other means of impounding or subduing the animal, including using a catchpole or shooting with some kind of anesthetic dart, must be implemented. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(k)(2)) 
Secs. 6-187-6-210. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - NUISANCE ANIMALS 

Sec. 6-211. - Prohibited. 
    Nuisance animals are prohibited in the city. Examples of nuisance behavior include, but are not limited to: 
(1)  Animals defecating on other people's property; 
(2)  Rooting through trash cans; 
(3)  Chasing persons or vehicles; 
(4)  Digging up yards; 
(5)  Barking loudly and incessantly; or 
(6)  Other acts that negatively affect the well being of the residents of the city. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(o)) 
Sec. 6-212. - Informal resolution encouraged; report of continued violations. 
    Responsible pet ownership is vital to a safe, healthy, friendly city atmosphere. In the event that the owner of a nuisance animal can be identified, residents are strongly encouraged to speak to the owners first to attempt to resolve the nuisance behavior. In the event that the nuisance behavior continues and is a violation of this chapter, residents should contact the city animal control officer for enforcement. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(o)) 
Sec. 6-213. - Complaint procedure. 
(a)  Complaint content; investigation. The animal control officer shall investigate an alleged violation of this division upon the notice of a complaint. The complainant should specify the address or location of the alleged violation; the nature, time, and date of the act; the name and address of the owner if known; and a description of the animal, if known. 
(b)  Voluntary resolution encouraged; issuance of citation. The animal control officer should attempt first to discuss the complaint with the owner and seek prompt voluntary resolution of the nuisance issue. If voluntary resolution is not achieved or sustained, the animal control officer may issue a citation to the owner or custodian of any animal alleged to be in violation of this section. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(p)) 
Secs. 6-214-6-234. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - RABIES[5] 

Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
State Law reference- Minimum standards for rabies control, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.012; authority of municipalities to adopt local rabies control regulations, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 826.015. 

Sec. 6-235. - Vaccinations required for dogs and cats. 
    All cats and dogs must be vaccinated by a licensed veterinarian at the owner's expense against rabies by the time that they reach four months of age and as necessary thereafter to ensure that the animal's vaccination remains current. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(d)(1); Ord. No. 897, 7-10-2001) 
Sec. 6-236. - Report of animal bites and potential rabies exposure required. 
    A person who knows of an animal bite or scratch to an individual that the person could reasonably foresee as capable of transmitting rabies, or who knows of an animal that the person suspects is rabid, shall report the incident or animal to the local rabies control authority of the county or municipality in which the person lives, in which the animal is located, or in which the exposure occurs. 
(Code 1995, § 3.105(f)) 
Sec. 6-237. - Quarantine. 
    The city will comply with the state quarantine rules and state board of health rules. Guide dogs, police dogs, or therapy dogs with current vaccinations that inflict bites in service shall not be required to be quarantined. 
(Code 1995, §§ 3.105(d)(1), (g); Ord. No. 897, 7-10-2001) 
Secs. 6-238-6-267. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 5. - BEEKEEPING 

Sec. 6-268. - Purpose. 
    The purpose of this division is to establish beekeeping practices intended to avoid problems that may otherwise be associated with the keeping of bees in populated areas and to protect the health, safety, and general welfare of the citizens. 
(Code 1995, § 3.401) 
Sec. 6-269. - Compliance required. 
    It is unlawful for any person to keep or allow bees, their hives, or any abandoned hives within the city limits unless all of the conditions of this division are satisfied. 
(Code 1995, § 3.402; Ord. No. 1011, 12-9-2008) 
Sec. 6-270. - Commercial beekeeping prohibited. 
    The keeping of bees in the city shall be for the personal and hobby use of the beekeeper and shall not be for commercial purposes. 
(Code 1995, § 3.402(i); Ord. No. 1011, 12-9-2008) 
Sec. 6-271. - Beekeeper to reside on premises with hives. 
    All beekeepers shall reside on the premises where the beekeeper's hives are located to assure that the hives are closely and regularly monitored for compliance with the requirements of this division. 
(Code 1995, § 3.402(i); Ord. No. 1011, 12-9-2008) 
Sec. 6-272. - Violations. 
    Except as authorized in this division or otherwise allowed by law, the keeping of bees is hereby declared a nuisance for which the city may invoke any legal recourse available in addition to prosecuting violations of this chapter. 
(Code 1995, § 3.402(i); Ord. No. 1011, 12-9-2008) 
Sec. 6-273. - Notice to city of hive number and location; inspections. 
(a)  A beekeeper shall notify the city manager in writing of the location and number of hives on his property. 
(b)  Any person who owns, harbors, or possesses bees shall, upon request by the city manager or his designee, make his bees, premises, facilities, equipment and queen certification available for inspection for the purpose of ascertaining compliance with the provisions of this chapter. 
(Code 1995, § 3.402(e), (f); Ord. No. 1011, 12-9-2008) 
Sec. 6-274. - Species of bees permitted; annual replacement of queen. 
    The only species of bees which may be kept in the city shall be the common domestic honeybee, Apis mellifera species, which is the same as the European honeybee. The queen of each colony of permitted bees shall be replaced annually by a new queen certified to be of the Apis mellifera species or the European honeybee. 
(Code 1995, § 3.402(a); Ord. No. 1011, 12-9-2008) 
Sec. 6-275. - Colonies contaminated by Africanized bees prohibited. 
    Any colony contaminated by Africanized bees is absolutely prohibited. In any instance in which a colony exhibits aggressive characteristics typical of Africanized bees such as stinging without provocation or a disposition to swarm, the city manager or his designee after investigation may order the beekeeper to promptly destroy the hives or colonies or remove them from the beekeeper's property. 
(Code 1995, § 3.402(a), (g); Ord. No. 1011, 12-9-2008) 
Sec. 6-276. - Hive location restricted. 
    All hives shall be located at least ten feet from side yard property lines and at least five feet from rear yard property lines. 
(Code 1995, § 3.402(b); Ord. No. 1011, 12-9-2008) 
Sec. 6-277. - Maximum hive density. 
    There shall be no more than two colonies on a half-acre or less tract of land and no more than four colonies on a larger tract of land. The term "colony" means the hive and its equipment and appurtenances, including bees, comb, honey, pollen and brood. 
(Code 1995, § 3.402(c); Ord. No. 1011, 12-9-2008) 
Sec. 6-278. - Water source required. 
    There must be a convenient source of water available to the bees at all times so that the bees will not congregate at swimming pools, pet watering bowls, bird baths or other water sources where they may cause human, bird or domestic pet contact. 
(Code 1995, § 3.402(d); Ord. No. 1011, 12-9-2008) 
Sec. 6-279. - Flyway barriers required. 
    The owner of a colony shall establish and maintain a flyway barrier at least six feet in height consisting of a solid wall, fence, dense vegetation or combination thereof that is parallel to the property line and extends ten feet beyond the colony in each direction so that all bees are forced to fly at an elevation of at least six feet above ground level over the property lines in the vicinity of the colony. 
(Code 1995, § 3.402(h); Ord. No. 1011, 12-9-2008) 
Chapter 8 - BUILDINGS AND BUILDING REGULATIONS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2017-03-14, adopted March 14, 2017 , repealed former Ch. 8, Arts. I-XII, in its entirety and enacted new provisions as herein set out. Former Ch. 8 pertained to similar subject matter. See the Code Comparative Tables at the back of this volume for a listing of former Code sections and ordinances that this former chapter derived from. 
State Law reference- Municipal authority to regulate housing and other structures, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.001 et seq.; building and rehabilitation codes, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.211 et seq.; verification of builder registration required for issuance of local building permit, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.906; regulation of municipal public buildings and grounds generally, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code §§ 281.001 et seq., 301.001 et seq.; Plumbing inspector, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.011; plumbing regulations, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.012; dangerous buildings, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.002. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 8-1. - Violations. 
(a)  Notwithstanding provisions of any code adopted by reference in this chapter, persons who violate a provision of this chapter or fail to comply with any of the requirements thereof or who shall erect, install, alter, repair or do work in violation of the approved construction documents or directive of the code official, or of a permit or certificate used under provisions of this Code, shall be guilty of a Class C misdemeanor, punishable by a fine of not more than $500.00. 
(b)  Any person who continues any work on the system after having been served with a stop work order, except such work as that person is directed to perform to remove a violation or unsafe condition, shall be liable for a fine of not less than $100.00 or more than $500.00. 
(c)  Each day that a violation continues shall be deemed a separate offense. 
( Ord. No. 2017-03-14, 3-14-2017 ) 
Sec. 8-2. - Permit and certificate issuance requires payment of assessments. 
    No permit for any kind of construction (building, alteration, or repair; lawn sprinkler; swimming pool; sewer connection; electrical; plumbing or any other), except fence construction, and no certificate of occupancy, shall be issued for any such work on, or occupancy of, any lot, house, or residence in the city on any street as to which a paving or sewer charge, assessment, or voluntary payment plan has been carried out to pave or sewer such street, or any block or blocks thereof (upon which street or block such lot or house and lot is located) unless and until all such charges, assessments, or payments due and owing on such property have first been paid in full, together with a penalty of six percent per annum on such sum. 
( Ord. No. 2017-03-14, 3-14-2017 ) 
Secs. 8-3-8-22. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ARCHITECTURAL REVIEW COMMITTEE 

Sec. 8-23. - Created; members; officers. 
(a)  The architectural review committee (ARC) shall consist of five members who are citizens of the city and who are not members of the city council, the board of adjustment, or the zoning commission. Members are to be nominated by the mayor and approved by the city council for a term of two years beginning on June 1 of each odd-numbered year. 
(b)  If feasible in the view of the city council, two members shall be professional architects, landscape architects, engineers, or the equivalent in training for executing the purposes of the committee. The mayor shall appoint a chairperson of the ARC to serve concurrently with the term of the mayor. 
(c)  The mayor shall also nominate, and the council shall approve, two alternate members who shall serve in the absence of one or more regular members. In the event that any person appointed by the mayor is not approved by a majority of the city council, the mayor shall make another appointment subject to the approval of a majority of the city council within 30 days. 
(d)  A city staff member will be appointed by the city manager to serve as the secretary to the committee. The secretary's duties include the ability to attend to all correspondence, send out or cause to be published all required notices, attend all meetings of the committee, and compile all required records. The secretary shall maintain a log of cases with the name of applicant, the number of the case, other necessary information, and the final disposition of the case. He shall also take or cause to be taken minutes of all proceedings, noting the members present and the vote of each member on each case. The minutes and other records of the action of the committee shall be public record and kept in the city offices. 
( Ord. No. 2017-03-14, 3-14-2017 ) 
Sec. 8-24. - Causes for removal from the committee. 
    Any committee member or alternate can be removed from office by the city council for cause. Causes for removal include: 
(1)  Malfeasance; 
(2)  Failure to maintain reasonable familiarity with statutes, ordinances, and rules affecting the committee, or failure to be governed thereby; 
(3)  Failure to disclose conflict of interest; and 
(4)  Failure to attend three consecutive meetings without the recorded consent of the chair. 
( Ord. No. 2017-03-14, 3-14-2017 ) 
Sec. 8-25. - Conflict of interest. 
    Whenever any committee member or any alternate or any staff member serving the committee becomes aware of any conflict of interest in any case to come before the committee, he shall notify the chair of the particulars. If the chair finds that conflict clearly exists, he shall disqualify the committee member from acting in the case and shall cause the circumstances to be entered into the record and shall arrange for an alternate to serve. 
( Ord. No. 2017-03-14, 3-14-2017 ) 
Sec. 8-26. - Purposes of architectural review. 
    The purposes of architectural review are to ensure high standards for aesthetic quality of development or redevelopment in commercial and multifamily housing areas of the city, promote orderly and harmonious development within the city, enhance living and business conditions within the city, assure that natural features are appropriately preserved and integrated with the development, serve in an advisory capacity to the city council and to provide information that will assist the city council in making difficult design decisions, and provide relief to city staff from some minor responsibilities. The architectural review process must be completed before the building official is authorized to accept any applications for building permits. 
( Ord. No. 2017-03-14, 3-14-2017 ) 
Sec. 8-27. - Meetings. 
    The architectural review committee shall meet monthly as needed or when an application is submitted for architectural review committee consideration. All formal architectural review committee meetings shall be open to the public and posted in accordance with state law. 
( Ord. No. 2017-03-14, 3-14-2017 ) 
Sec. 8-28. - Typographical or publishing errors do not affect validity of committee action. 
    Typographical or publishing errors shall not invalidate any action of the architectural review committee. 
( Ord. No. 2017-03-14, 3-14-2017 ) 
Sec. 8-29. - Annual report to city council. 
    The architectural review committee shall send a report not less than once a year to the city council to communicate concerns of the committee with respect to the city's plans, policies, ordinances, and procedures as those affect the projects which the committee reviews. 
( Ord. No. 2017-03-14, 3-14-2017 ) 
Secs. 8-30-8-46. - Reserved. 
Sec. 8-47. - Preliminary zoning issues to be resolved prior to architectural review committee application and permit consideration. 
    The building permit and architectural review committee process provided in this article does not start unless and until all zoning issues are completed. An application for a special use permit and the procedure with reference thereto is a zoning matter. The architectural review committee has no zoning jurisdiction and no building permit may be issued unless any zoning issues are resolved. 
( Ord. No. 2017-03-14, 3-14-2017 ) 
Sec. 8-48. - Application; referral to architectural review committee; exceptions. 
(a)  An application and request for a hearing with the architectural review committee must be filed with the city manager on a form approved by the committee and accompanied by an application fee in the amount provided in the city fee schedule. The city manager, upon determination that the application is in proper form with supporting documentation and that the proposed structure and use is permitted in the zoning district in question, will refer the matter to the architectural review committee unless excepted pursuant to this section. The application submission deadlines and architectural review committee hearing dates shall be established annually for the calendar year. 
(b)  Interior remodeling of any structure and single-family residences and two-family residences are completely exempt from the requirement for referral to and approval by the architectural review committee. In addition, if both the city manager and the chairperson of the architectural review committee concur, building projects costing less than $50,000.00 may be exempted from architectural review committee review and approval if: 
(1)  The project will not negatively affect the visual character of the city; 
(2)  No significant changes in existing parking and traffic circulation will result; 
(3)  No removal of significant existing vegetation will occur; 
(4)  The project includes repair or replacement of existing materials which no longer meet city standards; 
(5)  The design of the project is compatible with the immediate environment of the site; 
(6)  The planning and siting of the various functions and buildings on the site create an internal sense of order and provide a desirable environment for occupants, visitors and neighbors; and 
(7)  Flues, chimneys, exhaust fans, air conditioning equipment, elevator equipment, fans, cooling towers, antennae, down spouts, stairs, ramps, loading docks and other special purpose appendages, awnings and lighting will not affect the appearance and tranquility of the neighborhood. 
(c)  If the project requires removal of trees, this request must be clearly documented in the architectural review committee application, and payment for the tree removal as provided in the city fee schedule shall accompany the application, and supporting documentation per Chapter 48 Article II shall be provided. The applicant shall post city-provided signage on the property in question advising the public of the tree removal application and of the hearing date. A sign must be visible from each street that borders the property and shall be posted within five days of filling of the application and fee payment and shall be maintained until the day after the city council hearing. Sign location shall be subject to city manager approval. 
(d)  The application for review by the architectural review committee shall include, at a minimum, all of the following: 
(1)  Plat to scale showing project square footage and location of building or buildings. 
(2)  Information necessary to show compliance with building code and zoning code. 
(3)  Building plans (preliminary) giving footprint square footage as well as total square footage, site and grading/drainage plan, a survey which includes a tree survey, demolition plans if relevant, all to be included whether a new building, an addition, or exterior remodeling is intended. 
(4)  A sample board showing all exterior elevations, in color, reflecting specified exterior building materials. 
(5)  Preliminary landscape plans reflecting landscape areas including landscape buffer, plant specifications and locations, exterior lighting layout, parking, and any site screening. 
(6)  Design of any permanent sign showing size, color, and other structural and design specifications, whether freestanding or building-mounted. 
(7)  Photographs showing existing property, existing structures including any to be demolished, and adjacent neighbors' property. 
(8)  Provisions for location of trash and garbage containers for collection and removal and for any exterior storage, with plans for screening same. 
(9)  Size and location of any rooftop equipment with method and design of screening. 
(10)  Site and exterior building illumination. 
(11)  A traffic impact analysis (TIA) is required when a new or remodeled facility (development) is anticipated to generate more than 100 peak hour trips (PHTs) based on the latest version of the "Trip Generation Manual" by the Institute of Transportation Engineers (ITE). A TIA is also required when a change in use or a new or relocated business, operation, entity, or facility (also considered a development under his chapter) at a property or set of connected properties is anticipated to increase traffic by more than 100 peak hour trips based on the Trip Generation Manual. The purpose of a TIA is to identify any adverse impacts caused by the development to the adjacent roadway network. 
(e)  All plans, including preliminary plans for construction must be prepared, sealed, and signed by a state-registered architect. In the case of any new building or an addition to an existing building, the plans will also require a licensed state professional engineer to provide structural engineering services. 
(f)  A preliminary architectural review committee meeting may be requested by an applicant and held informally as no formal vote will be taken. The purpose of a preliminary architectural review committee meeting would be to assist an applicant in providing the necessary plans and specifications. A preliminary architectural review committee meeting may be conducted with at least two committee members just prior to the regular meeting or at a time more convenient to those involved. 
( Ord. No. 2017-03-14, 3-14-2017 ; Ord. No. 2017-05-01, 5-1-2017 ; Ord. No. 2017-05-09, 5-9-2017 ) 
Sec. 8-49. - Notice of hearing before architectural review committee. 
    Notice of the hearing where the architectural review committee may act upon an application shall be mailed at least ten calendar days prior to the date of the hearing to the applicant and to owners of real property within 200 feet of the exterior boundary of the property involved as such owners of record are shown on the tax roll. Compliance with the procedures set forth in this section shall constitute a good faith effort to provide notice, and the failure of any owner to receive notice shall not prevent the city from proceeding with the hearing or from taking any action or affect the validity of any action. 
( Ord. No. 2017-03-14, 3-14-2017 ) 
Sec. 8-50. - Posting notice on property required. 
    The applicant requesting a hearing by the architectural review committee shall post a notice on the property in question advising the public of the hearing date. This notice shall be a uniform sign furnished by the city which includes the date of the hearing. The sign shall remain on the property until after the completion of the hearing. A sign must be visible from each street that borders the property and shall be posted within five days of filling of the application and be maintained until the day after the hearing. Sign location shall be subject to city manager approval. 
( Ord. No. 2017-03-14, 3-14-2017 ) 
Sec. 8-51. - Factors to be considered by committee. 
    In reviewing applications and accompanying plans and specifications, the architectural review committee shall consider, at a minimum, the following factors: 
(1)  Appropriate signage; structural aspects, size limitations, color, and other aesthetic considerations. All permanent signs must be approved by the architectural review committee. 
(2)  Conservation of trees and other natural habitat considerations. 
(3)  Harmony of design, colors, materials, and finishes. 
(4)  Quality, character, and scale of design. 
(5)  Visibility and effect upon view at all sight lines. 
(6)  Suitability of building materials. 
(7)  Energy efficiency of design. 
(8)  Irrigation and maintenance. 
(9)  Accessibility design considerations for persons with disabilities. 
(10)  The traffic impact analysis submitted by the applicant as required by subsection 8-48 (d)(11). The architectural review committee shall carefully consider any adverse impacts caused by the development to the adjacent roadway network and furthermore shall consider any adverse impacts to neighbors. The final analysis by the architectural review committee shall not only include the technical analysis submitted, but shall also include common sense and reasoned judgment. For example, the city has received requests to locate large institutional facilities patronized by large numbers of persons on tiny rural roadways only two lanes in width. Streets such as S. Winston Lane, W. Castle Lane and Fox Hall Lane do not have the traffic capacity to accommodate large institutional facilities patronized by large numbers of persons without compromising the safety of users of the streets and the neighbors. 
( Ord. No. 2017-03-14, 3-14-2017 ; Ord. No. 2017-05-01, 5-1-2017 ) 
Sec. 8-52. - Preliminary consultation between applicant and city representative. 
    The applicant shall meet with the City of Castle Hills (City) staff and/or designated representative to determine the scope of the TIA prior to submittal of the TIA. The following sections 8-53 through section 8-58 are guidelines and general requirements to complete a TIA. 
( Ord. No. 2017-05-01, 5-1-2017 ) 
Sec. 8-53. - Definition of impact areas. 
    The area of impact includes the intersections or access points that may be affected by vehicular trips generated by the development. Table 1 shows the anticipated boundary of a TIA as determined by the number of trips generated by the development. Using engineering judgment, the city reserves the right to adjust the boundary area based on characteristics of the development and the surrounding roadway network and therefore may include intersections outside the boundary areas identified in Table 1. All TIAs should, at a minimum, extend to the first signalized intersection. 
TABLE 1.
