(a)  Annual license fees. The annual license fees to cover the cost of inspection of food service establishments shall be in the amount provided in the city fee schedule and shall be paid in advance upon issuance of the license. 
(b)  Copy of rules to be provided to proprietors. Upon annual payment of the required license fee, the proprietor of each food establishment shall be given a copy of the Rules of Food Service Establishments, including the compliance procedures, and shall be required to receipt in writing therefor. 
(c)  Issuance of license. Licenses shall be signed by the chief health inspector and attested by the city secretary. 
(d)  Term of license; renewal; proration of fees. Licenses shall expire on the May 31 following the date of its issuance, and reapplications must be made by the proprietor of each such food establishment for its renewal past June 1 each year. Applications received after the December 1 of any year shall require the proprietor to pay one-half of the stated annual charge. 
(e)  Temporary food licenses for special events. The city may issue a temporary food license for special events, daily fee for which shall be as provided in the city fee schedule. Temporary licenses shall not be issued for periods of more than 14 days and shall not be renewable. 
(f)  Reinspections; fee. Any establishment or vendor that requires an inspection beyond the normal schedule will be charged a fee in the amount provided in the city fee schedule for each reinspection. Fees are due upon the reinspection, and failure to pay the fee will result in the immediate suspension of the license. Such suspension will only be lifted at such time as the reinspection fee is paid and violations are corrected. 
(Code 1982, § 14.204; Code 1995, § 14.204; Ord. No. 540, 10-13-1987; Ord. No. 544, 11-10-1987; Ord. No. 943, 10-12-2004) 
Secs. 20-29-20-59. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - FOOD HANDLERS 

Sec. 20-60. - Registration. 
(a)  Any establishment or vendor regulated under this chapter must maintain a current register of employees who handle food in any form in their daily work activities. The register must include the name of the employee, the employee's current home address, the employee's current home telephone number, if any, and the employee's social security number. 
(b)  Failure to keep such a register or to allow access to this register by the city health inspector or an authorized agent shall result in the suspension of the appropriate license or permit issued by the health inspector under which the establishment or vendor operates. The suspension shall not be lifted until the establishment or vendor complies with this section. 
(Code 1982, § 14.205; Code 1995, § 14.205; Ord. No. 557, 6-14-1988) 
Sec. 20-61. - Employment of infected persons. 
(a)  No person operating or managing any public eating place or any place where food or drink is manufactured, processed, prepared, dispensed, or otherwise handled shall employ or schedule for work any person to handle such products, or utensils, dishes, or serving implements used in connection therewith, who is infected with any transmissible condition or any disease known to be normally communicable through the handling of food or drink. The provisions of this section apply to owner-workers as well as to employees. 
(b)  No person infected with a disease, the condition of that is transmissible to another through the handling of food or drink or who resides in a household with a transmissible case of a communicable disease which may be food borne, or who is known to be a carrier of the organism causing such disease, and no person having a local infection transmissible through food or drink shall be employed at any place or vehicle in which food or drink is manufactured, processed, prepared, or dispensed nor shall any such person at any time handle any food or drink or utensils, dishes, or serving implements used in connection therewith, which may be directly or indirectly for public sale or offered for the use or consumption of another. 
(Code 1982, §§ 14.301, 14.302; Code 1995, §§ 14.301, 14.302) 
Sec. 20-62. - Physical examination; certificate of physician. 
(a)  All persons and employees employed or seeking employment in any of the capacities provided in this article, before employment, shall secure an adequate examination of themselves by a licensed physician and secure in evidence thereof a certificate signed by such physician stating that such examination had been made and that to the best of his knowledge, the person examined was found, on that date, to be free of any transmissible condition of any disease or local infection commonly transmitted through the handling of food or drink. 
(b)  Such examinations shall be actual and thorough and conducted within the framework of practical scientific procedures for the determination of the existence of communicable disease which may be transmissible through the handling of foods. 
(c)  Such examination shall be made annually thereafter as to each such person and employee, and a new certificate secured. The provisions of this section apply to owner-workers as well as to employees. 
(Code 1982, § 14.303; Code 1995, § 14.303) 
Sec. 20-63. - Personal cleanliness and hygiene. 
    Every person engaged in the handling of food, drink, or unsealed containers therefor shall maintain personal cleanliness, shall wear clean outer garments, shall keep his hands clean at all times, and shall thoroughly wash the hands with soap and water after each visit to the toilet. The use (in, on, or about any place where food or drink for public consumption is handled or sold), by two or more persons, of any towel before it is thoroughly laundered is declared to be an unsanitary practice and shall constitute a violation of this Code. 
(Code 1982, § 14.304; Code 1995, § 14.304) 
Secs. 20-64-20-84. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - MEAT AND MEAT PRODUCTS 

Sec. 20-85. - Purpose. 
    It is essential in the public interest that the health and welfare of consumers be protected by assuring that meat products, meat food products, or prepared meals and dishes consisting of, or containing, meat of any kind distributed to them are wholesome, not adulterated, and are properly marked, labeled, and packaged and/or inspected as hereinafter provided. 
(Code 1982, § 14.401; Code 1995, § 14.401) 
Sec. 20-86. - Inspection required. 
    No person may sell, offer for sale, or have in his possession with intent to sell, store, or transport for sale any meat, meat products, meat food products, or prepared meals and dishes consisting of, or containing, meat of any kind which are capable of being used as food for human consumption unless such meat, meat product, or meat food products or meat of any kind used in the preparation of restaurant or catered meals, dishes, and prepared food items and the method of its slaughter, fabrication, processing, preparation, transportation, and storage has been inspected and passed by any state department of health appointed for the purpose, and is so marked by the official "inspected and passed" legend of the agency responsible for the inspection, or under the approved supervision of the federal department of agriculture meat inspection division. 
(Code 1982, § 14.402; Code 1995, § 14.402) 
Sec. 20-87. - Waiver of inspection. 
    The city council may waive the inspection required in this article under the following conditions: 
(1)  In favor of a nonprofit charitable, religious, or civic institution. 
(2)  For a period of not more than 48 hours. 
(3)  In connection with a money-raising social event or entertainment open to the public for compensation. 
(4)  Upon written application for such waiver addressed to the city council and delivered to the city office at least 20 days before the regular council meeting at which action is requested and signed by the chief executive officer of such institution. 
(5)  Together with the written assurance of an insurance company or agent therefor that it will write a liability policy in favor of the city in the amount of $500,000.00 in order to hold the city harmless from any liability up to such limit arising out of claims based on uninspected meat served at such event, followed by delivery to city of such policy at least ten days before the holding of such event. 
(Code 1982, § 14.403; Code 1995, § 14.403) 
Secs. 20-88-20-117. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - RODENTS 

Sec. 20-118. - San Antonio code provisions adopted. 
    The provisions of the City Code of San Antonio, Texas, regarding rodent control, as they may be amended from time to time, are adopted verbatim by this city as if written out fully herein, except insofar as the same should be inconsistent with other sections of this Code. Where the term "director of public health" is used in the adopted code provisions, it shall be meant to refer to the equivalent "chief health inspector" of this city. 
(Code 1982, § 14.501; Code 1995, § 14.501) 
Chapter 22 - HUMAN RELATIONS 
(RESERVED) 
Chapter 24 - LAW ENFORCEMENT[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal police forces generally, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 341.001 et seq.; municipal authority relating to jails, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 361.001 et seq.; municipal contracts with county or private entity for jail facilities, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 361.061 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 24-1-24-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - POLICE DEPARTMENT 

Sec. 24-19. - Creation. 
    There is created the city police department, which shall be operated as a department function of the city. The city council shall procure patrol cars and other apparatus for the enforcement of laws and ordinances (with advice from the police chief), and shall authorize employment of patrolmen. The police chief shall be the administrative head of such department. 
(Code 1995, § 19.101) 
Sec. 24-20. - Police officer positions. 
    The police department shall consist of at least 20 regular (or fully paid) positions. The city council may create additional positions by ordinance at any time. One of such positions shall be that of police chief. The city council may create such additional positions in the police department as it deems advisable from time to time. Appointments to all positions of patrolman or other peace officer position shall be made by the city manager subject to the advice of the police chief. 
(Code 1995, § 19.102) 
Sec. 24-21. - Police chief. 
(a)  There is created the position of police chief. The police chief shall be appointed by the city manager, subject to approval by the city council. 
(b)  The police chief is the executive head of the police department and is directly responsible to the city manager for the proper and efficient operation of the department. The duties of the police chief are to supervise, regulate, and manage the department and have control of all its activities; to reorganize any section of the department when in his judgment such reorganization should best serve the department; to prepare and submit to the city manager the department's budget; and to control and supervise the expenditure of the department's budget and payroll. 
(Code 1995, § 19.103) 
Sec. 24-22. - Powers. 
    The police officers appointed pursuant hereto shall have all of the powers, rights, and authorities vested in city marshals by state law 
(Code 1995, § 19.104; Ord. No. 776, 12-12-1996) 
Chapter 26 - NUISANCES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal authority for regulation of nuisances and disorderly conduct, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 217.001 et seq.; persons not to permit abandoned property to become public health nuisance, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 341.013; municipality authority to require the owner of a lot in the municipality to keep the lot free from weeds, rubbish, brush, and other environmental nuisances, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 342.001 et seq.; abatement of junked vehicle declared to be a public nuisance, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.071 et seq.; regulation of fireworks, V.T.C.A., Occupations Code § 2154.001 et seq.; enhanced penalty for violation ordinances governing fire safety, zoning, or public health and sanitation, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 54.001(b); abatement of common and public nuisances, V.T.C.A., Civil Practice and Remedies Code § 125.001 et seq.; municipal authority regarding substandard buildings, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.001. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 26-1. - Penalties. 
    Violations of the provisions under this chapter are hereby deemed violations of ordinances, rules, or police regulations that govern fire safety, zoning, and public health and sanitation, punishable as provided in section 1-17. 
State Law reference- Enhanced penalty for violation ordinances governing fire safety, zoning, or public health and sanitation, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 54.001(b). 
Secs. 26-2-26-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ABANDONED AND JUNK VEHICLES[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Abandoned motor vehicles, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.001 et seq.; abatement of junked vehicle declared to be a public nuisance, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.071 et seq.; abandonment of personal property, V.T.C.A., Property Code § 72.001 et seq. 

Sec. 26-21. - Definition of junked vehicle. 
    For the purposes of this article, the term "junked vehicle" shall have the meaning provided in V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.071. The term "junked vehicle" does not include antique and special interest vehicles described in V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 683.077. The term "junked vehicle" includes a portion or part of a junked vehicle. 
(Code 1995, § 26.801) 
Sec. 26-22. - Junked vehicles declared a public nuisance. 
    A junked vehicle, including part of a junked vehicle, that is visible from a public place or public right-of-way is a public nuisance. 
(Code 1995, § 26.802) 
Sec. 26-23. - Enforcement officials. 
    Abatement procedural requirements and removal of a junked vehicle or junked vehicle part as authorized in this article shall be conducted by regularly salaried full-time employees of the city, except that a junked vehicle or junked vehicle part may be removed by any designee of the chief of police. 
(Code 1995, § 26.803(f)) 
Sec. 26-24. - Right of entry. 
    The chief of police or his designee may enter private property to examine a junked vehicle or junked vehicle parts to obtain information to identify the junked vehicle or junked vehicle part and to remove or direct the removal of the junked vehicle or junked vehicle part. 
(Code 1995, § 26.806; Ord. No. 1073, 6-14-2011) 
Sec. 26-25. - Content and service of notice of violation. 
(a)  Notice requiring abatement and removal of a junked vehicle or part of a junked vehicle shall be furnished by the chief of police or his designee not less than ten days before the date the junked vehicle or part of a junked vehicle must be abated and removed. 
(b)  The notice must be personally delivered, sent by certified mail with a five-day return requested or delivered by the United States Postal Service with signature confirmation to: 
(1)  The last known registered owner of the junked vehicle or motor vehicle part; 
(2)  Each lienholder of record of the junked vehicle or junked vehicle part; and 
(3)  The owner or occupant of the property on which the junked vehicle or junked vehicle part is located, or, if a junked vehicle or junked vehicle part is located on a public right-of-way, the owner or occupant of the property adjacent to the right-of-way. 
(c)  The notice shall include an admonition that the junked vehicle must be abated and removed not later than the tenth day after the date on which the notice was personally delivered or mailed, and that any request for a public hearing regarding the abatement and removal must be made before that ten day period expires. 
(d)  The notice shall state that persons notified have a right to request a public hearing before the city council in the manner provided in this article. 
(e)  If the post office address of the last known registered owner of the junked vehicle or motor vehicle part is unknown, notice may be placed on the junked vehicle or junked vehicle part, or, if the owner is located, personally delivered. 
(f)  If the notice is returned undelivered, action to abate the nuisance shall be continued to a date not earlier than the 11th day after the date of the return. 
(Code 1995, § 26.803(a)-(e)) 
Sec. 26-26. - Public hearing. 
(a)  Time of holding. If a public hearing is requested by a person to whom notice has been sent, the public hearing shall be held not earlier than the 11th day after the date of the service of notice. 
(b)  Presumption that vehicle is inoperable. At the public hearing, the junked vehicle or vehicle part is presumed, unless demonstrated otherwise by the owner, to be inoperable. 
(c)  Content of order requiring removal. If the information is available at the location of the junked vehicle or junked vehicle part, an order or resolution requiring removal of the junked vehicle or junked vehicle part shall include the vehicle's description, vehicle identification number, and license plate number. 
(Code 1995, § 26.804) 
Sec. 26-27. - Relocation of vehicle has no effect on pending action. 
    The relocation of a junked vehicle or junked vehicle part to another location in the city after a proceeding for the abatement and removal of the junked vehicle or junked vehicle part has commenced has no effect on the proceeding if the junked vehicle or junked vehicle part constitutes a public nuisance at the new location. 
(Code 1995, § 26.805) 
Sec. 26-28. - Disposal of vehicle; reconstruction prohibited. 
    A junked vehicle, including a part of a junked vehicle, may be removed to a scrap yard, a motor vehicle demolisher, or a suitable site operated by a municipality or county. The junked vehicle or junked vehicle part shall not be reconstructed or made operable after removal. 
(Code 1995, § 26.805) 
Sec. 26-29. - Notice of removal. 
    The chief of police or his designee shall furnish notice of the removal of a junked vehicle or junked vehicle part to the state department of transportation within five days after the date of removal. 
(Code 1995, § 26.805) 
Sec. 26-30. - Penalties and other remedies. 
(a)  Any person violating the provisions of this article shall be, upon conviction thereof, punished by a fine not exceeding $200.00. 
(b)  In addition, the city shall be entitled to injunctive relief against any violation of this article and for any damages that may result to the city of the general public by reason of such violations. 
(c)  As an alternative to abatement in the manner described in this article, the municipal court may issue orders necessary to enforce this article and shall order abatement and removal of the nuisance on conviction. 
(Code 1995, § 26.806; Ord. No. 1073, 6-14-2011) 
Secs. 26-31-26-48. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - NOISE 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 26-49. - Purpose and intent. 
    The provisions and the prohibitions contained in this article are declared a public interest necessity and are a matter of legislative determination and public policy. The prohibitions of this section are for the purpose of securing and promoting the public health, comfort, convenience, safety, welfare and prosperity and the peace, quiet, and repose of the city and its inhabitants. 
(Code 1995, § 17.101) 
Sec. 26-50. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, unless the context of their usage clearly indicates another meaning: 
    A-weighted sound level means the total sound level in decibels of all sounds as measured with a sound level meter using the A-weighting network. The level read is designated dB(A) or dBA. 
    Daytime hours means the hours between 7:00 a.m. and 10:00 p.m. on the same day. 
    dB(A) means the intensity of a sound expressed in decibels read from a calibrated sound level meter utilizing the A-level weighting scale and the slow meter response, as specified by the American National Standards Institute. 
    Emergency means any occurrence or set of circumstances involving actual or imminent physical trauma or property damage or loss which demands immediate action. 
    Emergency work means any work performed for the purpose of preventing or alleviating the physical trauma or property damage threatened or caused by an emergency, or that is otherwise necessary to restore property to a safe condition following a fire, accident or natural disaster, or which is required to protect persons or property from exposure to danger, or which is required to restore public utilities. 
    Exterior noise level means sounds which originate from any source that is not within a building or structure. 
    Interior noise means any sound that originates from inside any building or structure. 
    Nighttime hours means the hours between 10:00 p.m. on one day and 7:00 a.m. the following day. 
    Nonresidential property means any real property within the limits of the city which is not included in the definition of residential property as defined in this section. 
    Property line means the line along the ground surface, and its vertical extension, which separates the real property owned, leased or occupied by one person from that owned, leased or occupied by another person and the imaginary line which represents the legal limits of property of any person who owns, leases or otherwise occupies an apartment, condominium, hotel or motel room, office or any other type of occupancy. 
    Public right-of-way means any street, avenue, boulevard, highway, road, thoroughfare, sidewalk, alley or any other property which is owned or controlled by a governmental entity. 
    Residential property means any real property developed and used for human habitation and which contains living facilities, including provisions for sleeping, eating, cooking and sanitation, unless, such premises are actually occupied and used primarily for purposes other than human habitation. 
    Sound level meter means an instrument meeting American National Standard Institute standards S1.4-1984 (ANSI S1.4-1984) or most recent revision thereof for Type 1 or Type 2 sound level meters or an instrument and the associated recording and analyzing equipment which will provide equivalent data. 
    Sound nuisance means any sound which either exceeds the maximum permitted sound levels specified in section 26-54 or, for purposes of sections 26-55 and 26-57, otherwise unreasonably disturbs, injures or endangers the comfort, repose, health, peace or safety of others within the limits of the city. 
(Code 1995, § 17.102) 
Sec. 26-51. - Penalty. 
    Any person who violates any provision of this article is guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be subject to a fine of not less than $50.00 or more than $500.00. Each day that any violation continues shall constitute a separate offense. To the extent that any conduct prohibited under this article also constitutes an offense under state law, then it shall be punishable as provided by state law. 
(Code 1995, § 17.111) 
Sec. 26-52. - Method of sound measurement. 
(a)  Whenever this article prohibits sound over a certain decibel limit, measurement of sound shall be made with a Type 1 or Type 2 calibrated sound level meter utilizing the A-weighting scale and the slow meter response as specified by the American National Standards Institute (ANSI S1.4-1984/85A). Noise levels shall be measured in decibels and A-weighted. The unit of measurement shall be designated as dB(A). 
(b)  Meters shall be maintained in calibration and good working order. Calibrations shall be employed which meet ANSI S1.4-1984 prior to and immediately after every sampling of sound. 
(c)  Measurements recorded shall be taken so as to provide a proper representation of the sound being measured. The microphone of the meter shall be positioned so as not to create any unnatural enhancement or diminution of the measured sound. A windscreen for the microphone shall be used. 
(d)  Except as otherwise provided in this article, measurements shall be taken at or near the nearest property line of the property where the sound is being received. 
(Code 1995, § 17.109) 
Sec. 26-53. - Noise disturbances prohibited and declared nuisance. 
    No person shall make or cause to be made any loud and raucous noise in the city which is offensive to the ordinary sensibilities of the inhabitants of the city, which noise renders the enjoyment of life or property uncomfortable or interferes with public peace and comfort. The acts prohibited by this section are declared a sound nuisance. 
(Code 1995, § 17.101) 
Sec. 26-54. - Maximum permissible sound levels. 
(a)  Generally. No person shall conduct, permit or allow any activity or sound source to produce a sound that is discernible from the nearest property line of a property under separate ownership on which the sound is being received that when measured as provided in this article exceeds the applicable dB(A) level listed below for the property on which the sound is received: 
(1)  Residential property. During daytime hours, exterior or interior noise level may not exceed 60 dB(A). During nighttime hours, exterior or interior noise level shall not exceed 50 dB(A). 
(2)  Nonresidential property. During either daytime or nighttime hours, exterior or interior noise level of 65 dB(A). 
(b)  Prima facie evidence of sound nuisance. Evidence that an activity or sound source produces a sound that exceeds the dB(A) levels specified in this section, when measured at the site where the sound is being produced, if available, shall be prima facie evidence of a sound nuisance which unreasonably disturbs, injures or endangers the comfort, repose, health, peace or safety of others within the limits of the city in violation of this article. 
(Code 1995, § 17.103) 
Sec. 26-55. - Noisy vehicles. 
    The use of any automobile, motorcycle, or other vehicle so out of repair, so loaded, or in such a manner so as to create loud and unreasonable grating, grinding, rattling or any other loud and unreasonable sound is hereby prohibited and declared to be unlawful and a violation of this article, regardless of whether the sound so created by any automobile, motorcycle, or other vehicle is within the maximum permissible sound levels specified in this article. 
(Code 1995, § 17.105) 
Sec. 26-56. - Amplified sound from motor vehicle. 
    The production or reproduction of sound from amplification equipment contained in or mounted on a motor vehicle that produces sound in excess of the maximum permissible sound limits set forth in this article, when measured at or near 15 feet from the nearest external point on the vehicle, is hereby prohibited and declared to be unlawful as a sound nuisance in violation of this article, unless a permit is obtained pursuant to division 2 of this article. 
(Code 1995, § 17.106) 
Sec. 26-57. - Noisy animals and birds. 
    The keeping of any animal or bird that causes or makes frequent or long and continued sound which unreasonably disturbs, injures or endangers the comfort, repose, health, peace or safety of persons who reside in the vicinity thereof is hereby prohibited and declared to be unlawful as a sound nuisance in violation of this article, regardless of whether the sound so created by the animal or bird is within the maximum permissible sound levels specified in this article. 
(Code 1995, § 17.107) 
Sec. 26-58. - Defenses. 
    The following defenses shall apply to any violation of this article: 
(1)  The emission of any sound was for the purpose of alerting persons to the existence of an emergency, danger or attempted crime. 
(2)  The sound was produced by an authorized emergency vehicle. 
(3)  The sound was produced by emergency work necessary to restore public utilities, or to restore property to a safe condition, or to protect persons or property from imminent danger, following a fire, accident or natural disaster. 
(4)  The sound was generated by: 
a.  A parade and spectators and participants on the parade route during a permitted parade; 
b.  Patrons and participants using cannons and gunfire during historical battle reenactments for which a pyrotechnic permit was obtained and the explosives were inspected by the fire marshal; 
c.  A pyrotechnic display that was inspected and approved by the fire marshal; 
d.  Spectators and participants of any outdoor event, fun run, race, festival, fiesta, or concert which was sponsored, cosponsored, or permitted by the city; or 
e.  Any other lawful activity which constitutes protected expression pursuant to the First Amendment of the United States Constitution. 
(5)  The sound was produced by the erection, excavation, construction, demolition, alteration, or repair work, or the permitting or causing thereof, of any building or other structure, or the operation or the permitting or causing the operation of any tools or equipment used in any such activity conducted between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 8:00 p.m., Monday through Saturday, and which activity did not produce a sound exceeding 75 dB(A) when measured from the nearest residential property where the sound is being received. 
(6)  The sound was produced by aircraft in flight or in operation at an airport, or railroad equipment in operation on railroad rights-of-way. 
(7)  The sound was produced by operating or permitting the operation of any mechanically powered saw, drill, sander, router, grinder, lawn or garden tool, lawnmower, or any other similar device used between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 8:00 p.m. and which device did not produce a sound exceeding 85 dB(A) when measured from the nearest residential property where the sound is being received and was used for the maintenance or upkeep of the property on which it was used. 
(8)  The sound was generated as authorized under the terms of a permit issued under this article. 
(9)  The sound was produced by the operation of any air conditioning unit that did not produce a sound exceeding 60 dB(A) on residential property or 65 dB(A) on non-residential property, when measured at or near 15 feet from the air conditioning unit producing the sound being measured. 
(10)  The sound was produced by church bells or church chimes when used as part of a religious observance or service during daytime hours and that did not exceed five continuous minutes in duration in any one-hour period. 
(Code 1995, § 17.108) 
Secs. 26-59-26-89. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PERMITS FOR OUTDOOR SOUND AMPLIFICATION 

Sec. 26-90. - Required. 
    No person shall use or cause to be used any loudspeaker, loudspeaker system, sound amplifier or any other machine or device that produces, reproduces, or amplifies sound outside of buildings or other enclosed structures in a manner which exceeds the maximum permissible sound levels specified in this article, when measured from the property where the sound is being received, without first obtaining a permit as provided in this division. 
(Code 1995, § 17.110(a)) 
Sec. 26-91. - Applications; fees. 
    Permits may be obtained by making application to the director of the city department designated by the city manager. The fee for issuance of the permit shall be as provided in the city fee schedule. The application for the permit shall contain the following information: 
(1)  The date of the application and the date and hours for which the permit is requested. 
(2)  The name and address of the applicant. 
(3)  The name and address of the person who will have charge of the sound amplifying equipment. 
(4)  The address and a description of the location where the sound equipment will be used. 
(5)  A description of the type of sound amplifying equipment to be used. 
(Code 1995, § 17.110(a)(1), (c)) 
Sec. 26-92. - Permit valid for one day; hours. 
    A permit issued under this division is valid for one day between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and 10:00 p.m. 
(Code 1995, § 17.110(a)(2)) 
Sec. 26-93. - Sound level restricted. 
    Permits issued under this division shall not authorize, allow, or otherwise permit the production, reproduction, or amplification of sound which exceeds 65 dB(A) when measured from the nearest receiving property. 
(Code 1995, § 17.110(a)(3)) 
Sec. 26-94. - Sound source restricted to music and human speech. 
    The only sound allowed pursuant to a permit issued under this division are either music or human speech or both. 
(Code 1995, § 17.110(b)) 
Secs. 26-95-26-116. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - WEEDS AND TRASH[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Municipality authority to require the owner of a lot in the municipality to keep the lot free from weeds, rubbish, brush, and other environmental nuisances, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 342.001 et seq.; protection of endangered plants, V.T.C.A., Parks and Wildlife Code § 88.001 et seq.; municipal landscaping services, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code § 756.101 et seq.; noxious weeds control districts, V.T.C.A., Agriculture Code § 78.001 et seq.; local regulation of noxious and invasive plants prohibited, V.T.C.A., Agriculture Code § 71.153; nuisance or noxious aquatic vegetation control, V.T.C.A., Parks and Wildlife Code § 12.010. 

Sec. 26-117. - Prohibition of weeds, high grass, and debris. 
    It is unlawful for any person, or his agent, owning, renting, or having under his control any lot or premises, whether vacant or improved, within the city to permit the same to be covered, in whole or in part, with any weeds, high grass, downed timber or brush, old logs, decaying vegetable matter, trash or trash piles, junk, scrap, open garbage, filth, or debris whatsoever, and same are declared to be public nuisances, a hazard and menace to public health, and fire hazards. 
(Code 1982, § 28.101; Code 1995, § 28.101; Ord. No. 252, 8-18-1965) 
Sec. 26-118. - Maintaining city easements and rights-of-way. 
(a)  It is unlawful for any person, or his agent, owning, renting, or having under his control any lot or premises, whether improved or vacant, within the city, which lot or premises consists in part of city-owned easements or rights-of-way (whether sidewalk, construction, utility, or drainage) to permit same to be covered with high grass or weeds or any of the unsightly conditions enumerated in this article. Such city easements and rights-of-way shall be kept mowed, trimmed, and clean at all times. 
(b)  All provisions in this chapter respecting a privileged lien on such lots or premises as provided by V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code §§ 342.001 through 342.007 shall apply as full to such city easements and rights-of-way as to the balance of such lots or premises. 
(Code 1982, § 28.101.1; Code 1995, § 28.101.1) 
Sec. 26-119. - Nuisance; abatement. 
    The mayor, city manager, fire marshal, fire chief, chief of police, and city health officer shall each have the power and duty, when any such situation shall constitute a health or fire hazard, or both, to summarily abate same, or have same abated, using city firefighters, or police officers, or city employees. 
(Code 1982, § 28.102; Code 1995, § 28.102; Ord. No. 252, 8-18-1965) 
Sec. 26-120. - Weeds in alleys. 
    It shall be unlawful for both the owner and the tenant of any property in the city abutting upon a public alley or way to permit any weeds, grasses, or other vegetation whatsoever to grow therein to the center line to a height of greater than five inches. 
(Code 1982, § 28.103; Code 1995, § 28.103; Ord. No. 230, 7-14-1964) 
Sec. 26-121. - Notice to remove weeds. 
    It shall be the duty of the city manager of the city to notify the owner or agent of any premises within the city which are grown up in weeds to a greater height than 12 inches, to remove such weeds within ten days. This notice shall be in writing and may be served on the owner or agent by handing it to him in person by certified mail, addressed to such owner or agent at his post office address, or by publication as many as two times within ten consecutive days if personal service may not be had or his address is unknown. 
(Code 1982, § 28.104; Code 1995, § 28.104) 
State Law reference- Similar provision, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code §§ 342.001 through 342.007. 
Sec. 26-122. - City authorized to remove weeds. 
    Upon the failure of any such owner or agent to comply with the notice, or upon the written request and authorization of such owner or agent so notified, it shall become the responsibility of the city manager to have such weeds cut, raked, and removed on all property within the city that abuts or adjoins improved property by the employment of city forces, or by an authorized independent contractor. The high weeds will be cut, raked, and removed to a depth of at least 50 feet inward from all property lines of the property which adjoins or abuts improved property. 
(Code 1982, § 28.105; Code 1995, § 28.105) 
Sec. 26-123. - Charge to be levied and collected for weed or debris removal. 
(a)  A charge of actual costs plus 25 percent administrative costs for each cutting, raking, and removal of the weeds and removal of the debris shall be levied, assessed, and collected against such property each time such cutting, raking, and removal of the weeds or removal of the debris shall be performed. 
(b)  The charges provided for herein shall be levied, assessed, and collected by the authorized official, and if any person shall fail to pay such charges so assessed within ten days after proper notice, the authorized official will file, with the county clerk of the county, a statement by the mayor setting out the expenses that the city has incurred pursuant to the provisions of this section, and the city shall thereby perfect a privileged lien on the property involved, second only to tax liens and liens for street improvement, to secure the expense to the city, together with ten percent per annum interest from the date such payment is due. 
(Code 1982, § 28.106; Code 1995, § 28.106) 
Secs. 26-124-26-144. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - GRAFFITI 

Sec. 26-145. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Felt tip marker means any indelible marker or similar implement with any size tip containing an ink that is not water soluble. 
    Graffiti means any unauthorized inscription, word, figure, or design that is marked, etched, scratched, drawn, or painted on any surface of public or private buildings, structures or other facility or upon any other property, regardless of its content or nature and regardless of the nature of the material of the structural component or property. 
    Graffiti implement means any aerosol paint container, a felt tip marker, or a paint stick or etching tool capable of scarring or otherwise defacing glass, metal, concrete or wood. 
    Paint stick or graffiti stick means any device containing a solid form of paint, chalk, was epoxy, or other similar substances capable of being applied to a surface by pressure, and upon application, leaving a visible mark, and that is not water soluble. 
(Code 1995, § 26.601) 
Sec. 26-146. - Unauthorized defacing of property prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person who shall be in any place, public or private, to deface, write or mark, cut print, stamp, indent or display any word, sentence, symbol or figure on public or privately owned buildings, permanent structures, or places located on within the city, without authorization of the property owner. 
(Code 1995, § 26.602(a)) 
Sec. 26-147. - Possession of graffiti implements prohibited. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to have in his possession, any graffiti implement in any public park, public schoolground, public playground, public swimming pool, public recreational facility, any public right-of-way, or other public grounds in the city when the public facility is closed to the public. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to have in his possession, for the purpose of defacing property, any graffiti implement while on private property not open to the public. The graffiti implement shall be presumed to be for the purpose of defacing property if it is in the holder's possession while the holder is on private property closed to the public, without the permission from the owner or his lawful agent. 
(Code 1995, § 26.602(b), (c)) 
Sec. 26-148. - Responsibility for violations by minors. 
    It shall be an offense for the parent or legal guardian of a child under 17 years of age to intentionally, knowingly, recklessly, or with criminal negligence allow the child to violate the provisions of this article. 
(Code 1995, § 26.602(d)) 
Sec. 26-149. - Penalties. 
(a)  Violation of any of the provisions of this article shall be an offense and shall be punished by a fine not to exceed $500.00. The court shall have the discretion to provide other means of punishment, which may include community service. 
(b)  In setting the penalties due consideration will be given to the costs incurred by the property owner to remove the graffiti, the amount and visual prominence of the graffiti, and the past history of the offender. In all cases, requiring removal of graffiti will be at the offender's expense. 
(Code 1995, § 26.603) 
Chapter 28 - OFFENSES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Concurrent jurisdiction of municipal court concerning certain violations of state statutes, V.T.C.A., Government Code § 29.003(b); municipal authority for regulation of firearms and explosives, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 229.001; municipal regulation of discharge of firearms, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 229.002; juvenile curfews in general law municipalities, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 341.905; municipal policy regarding enforcement of drug laws, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 370.003. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 28-1. - Aiding or abetting. 
    The prohibition of any act in this Code, and in any rule of regulation adopted hereunder, shall include the causing, securing, aiding, or abetting of another person to do such act. 
(Code 1982, § 1.701; Code 1995, § 1.701) 
Secs. 28-2-28-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - CITATIONS 

Sec. 28-21. - Applicability. 
    This article does not apply to licensed peace officers who are employed by the city as peace officers. 
(Code 1995, § 2.701) 
Sec. 28-22. - Authority to issue citations to appear in municipal court. 
    The city manager or his designee may issue a citation or citations to a person requiring such person to appear in the municipal court if the city manager or his designee believes that the person has engaged in conduct that violates a law or ordinance of the city. 
(Code 1995, § 2.702) 
Sec. 28-23. - Designated employees. 
(a)  City manager to designate; qualifications; training. The city manager may designate employees to issue citations. A person designated under this section must be an employee of the city and successfully complete a training program approved by the city manager. Peace officers may not be designated under this article. 
(b)  No arrest authority. A person designated under this section is not authorized to arrest an individual for violation of a city ordinance. 
(c)  Identification cards. The city manager shall provide a designated employee with an identification card, including the department name, the name of the employee, and photograph of the employee. A designated employee shall show the employee's identification card on request. 
(Code 1995, § 2.703) 
Sec. 28-24. - Interference with designated employee prohibited. 
    A person commits an offense if the person interferes with or hinders a city employee in the performance of the employee's duties under this article. 
(Code 1995, § 2.706(B)) 
Sec. 28-25. - Citation form and content. 
    A citation issued under this section must be on a form approved by the municipal court clerk that includes the following information: 
(1)  If available, the name, address, date of birth, or driver's license number and physical description, and telephone number of the person cited; 
(2)  The offense for which the person is charged; 
(3)  The date and location of the offense; 
(4)  An appearance date; 
(5)  A statement requiring the person receiving the citation to appear at municipal court on or before the appearance date indicated on the citation; 
(6)  A statement of the person's promise to respond to the citation by the appearance date indicated on the citation, including a place for the person cited to provide the person's signature; 
(7)  The signature of the person issuing the citation; and 
(8)  Other information as may be determined necessary or desirable by the city manager. 
(Code 1995, § 2.704(A)) 
Sec. 28-26. - Processing of issued citations. 
    Upon receipt of a completed citation, the municipal court clerk shall process the citation and cause a complaint to be filed, in the same manner as a citation issued by a peace officer. 
(Code 1995, § 2.704(B)) 
Sec. 28-27. - Duty to respond to citation. 
    On or before the appearance date indicated on the citation, a person cited shall submit a plea to each charge indicated on the citation. The person may enter a plea of guilty, not guilty, or no contest. The plea may be submitted by mail, in person, or by other method acceptable to the municipal court. A person may enter a plea of guilty or no contest to a charge on a citation by paying the fine for the charge. 
(Code 1995, § 2.705(A)) 
Sec. 28-28. - Failure to enter plea constitutes offense. 
    A person commits an offense if the person has been issued a citation and the person fails to enter a plea to a charge indicated on the citation on or before the appearance date indicated on the citation. 
(Code 1995, § 2.706(A)) 
Sec. 28-29. - Cumulative remedies. 
    The remedies authorized in this article are cumulative of other remedies. This article does not require the city manager or his designated employee to issue a citation in lieu of other remedies. 
(Code 1995, § 2.707; Ord. No. 1058, 10-12-2010) 
Secs. 28-30-28-46. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - OFFENSES AGAINST PERSONS 

Secs. 28-47-28-65. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - OFFENSES AGAINST PROPERTY 

Sec. 28-66. - Unlawful to enter without consent; refusal to leave. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to enter or intrude in, or upon, any real property of another in the city without the consent of the owner, proprietor, occupant, lessee, or agent in charge of such property unless the person so going upon such property immediately makes known to the owner, proprietor, occupant, lessee, or agent in charge of such property his purpose in being upon such property. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person who enters or intrudes upon any real property of another in the city without the consent of the owner, proprietor, occupant, lessee, or agent in charge of such property to fail or refuse to leave such property when requested or ordered to do so by such owner, proprietor, occupant, lessee, or agent in charge of such property. 
(Code 1982, §§ 26.101, 26.102; Code 1995, §§ 26.101, 26.102; Ord. No. 16, 12-19-1952) 
Sec. 28-67. - Defacing public property. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to paint, mark, place, scratch, chisel, or post bills, posters, signs, words, letters, pictures, numbers, symbols, or graffiti of whatever kind on any curb, street, sidewalk, utility pole, public building, public structure, public vehicle, or public property whatsoever, or otherwise in any way deface any public property within the city, whether owned by the city, county, state, or any public utility franchisee of the city. 
(Code 1982, § 22.601; Code 1995, § 22.601) 
Sec. 28-68. - Trespass on stormwater drainage channels. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person, other than a city employee or authorized person, to purposely, at any time of the day, remain, walk, run, stand, drive, skate, ride about, in, or upon any stormwater drainage channel owned or controlled by the city as a drainage easement. 
(b)  Violation of this section shall be punished as provided in section 1-17. The court shall have the discretion to provide other means of punishment, which may include community service. In setting the penalties due consideration will be given the past history of the offender. 
(Code 1995, §§ 26.701-26.703; Ord. No. 796, 7-9-1996) 
Secs. 28-69-28-94. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC HEALTH AND SAFETY[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal authority to regulate discharge of firearms, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 229.002; discharge of firearm as disorderly conduct, V.T.C.A., Penal Code § 42.01. 

Sec. 28-95. - Discharge of weapons. 
(a)  Firearms. It shall be unlawful to discharge any gun, rifle, pistol, or firearm of any kind within the limits of the city. 
(b)  Airguns. It shall be unlawful to discharge any airgun, air rifle, or air pistol of any description (by whatever name known) that by means of compressed air, compressed gas, springs, or any other means is capable of discharging shots, pellets, or any solid object at any velocity, anywhere within the limits of the city. 
(c)  Exception for indoor ranges; permit required. The city council may grant a permit, after a public hearing based upon specific plans submitted to it, for indoor rifle and pistol ranges for instruction and target practice, provided use of same is limited to .22 caliber ammunition, is fully enclosed, is insulated against sound, incorporates approved safety features, and is operated only with a qualified instructor or range officer in attendance. Indoor ranges must meet all other requirements of this Code, including, without limitation, business licensing and zoning requirements. 
(Code 1982, §§ 10.101, 10.201, 10.301; Code 1995, §§ 10.101, 10.201, 10.301; Ord. No. 108, 11-15-1960) 
Sec. 28-96. - Sale and inhaling of certain volatile solvents prohibited. 
(a)  Except as otherwise provided herein, no person shall, within the city, sell, offer for sale, deliver, or give to any individual under the age of 17 years any glue or cement commonly known as model airplane glue, plastic cement, household cement, cement, or any other similar substance, if such glue or cement contains one or more of the following volatile solvents: 
(1)  Toluol. 
(2)  Hexane. 
(3)  Trichloroethylene. 
(4)  Acetone. 
(5)  Toluene. 
(6)  Ethyl acetate. 
(7)  Methyl ethyl ketone. 
(8)  Trichloroethane. 
(9)  Isopropanol. 
(10)  Methyl isobutyl ketone. 
(11)  Methyl cellosolve acetate. 
(12)  Cyclohexanone. 
(b)  The provisions of subsection (a) of this section shall not apply where the glue or cement is sold, delivered, or given simultaneously with, and as part of, a kit used for the construction of model airplanes, model boats, model automobiles, model trains, or other similar models. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for any person within the city to inhale any glue or cement containing one or more of the solvents named in subsection (a) of this section with the intent of obtaining intoxicating or narcotic effect thereby. 
(Code 1982, §§ 26.201-26.203; Code 1995, §§ 26.201-26.203; Ord. No. 240, 2-9-1965) 
Secs. 28-97-28-120. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC PEACE AND ORDER 

Sec. 28-121. - False burglar alarms. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for the owner or occupant of any residence or business in the city equipped with a burglar alarm system to sound a false alarm thereon either knowingly or by negligence or to permit a false alarm to be sounded thereon by a spouse, companion, child, servant, customer, invitee, or guest of such owner or occupant, either deliberately or through any negligent act or omission. 
(b)  For purposes of this section, the term "negligence" means the failure to exercise that degree of care than would be exercised by a person of ordinary prudence under the same or similar circumstances, which includes failure to keep such system in proper repair and properly protected and supervised. 
(c)  Each violation hereof shall be punished by a fine of not less than $10.00 or more than $500.00. 
(Code 1982, §§ 26.301-26.303; Code 1995, §§ 26.301-26.303; Ord. No. 368, 10-11-1977) 
Sec. 28-122. - False fire alarms. 
(a)  For purposes of this section, the term "negligence" means the failure to exercise that degree of care that would be exercised by a person of ordinary prudence under the same or similar circumstances and includes failure to keep such fire alarm system in proper repair and properly protected and supervised. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for the owner or occupant of any residence or business in the city equipped with a fire alarm system to sound a false alarm thereon either knowingly or by negligence, or to permit a false fire alarm to be sounded thereon by a spouse, companion, child, servant, customer, invitee, or guest of such owner or occupant, either deliberately or through any negligent act or omission. 
(c)  Each violation hereof shall be punished by a fine of not less than $50.00 or more than $1,000.00. 
(Code 1982, §§ 26.401-26.403; Code 1995, §§ 26.401-26.403; Ord. No. 722, 7-13-1993) 
Secs. 28-123-28-142. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - MINORS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Secs. 28-143-28-167. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - CURFEW[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal authority to establish a juvenile curfew, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 341.905; requirement that juvenile curfew ordinances be reviewed and readopted every three years, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 370.002. 

Sec. 28-168. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Emergency includes, but is not limited to, fires, natural disasters, automobile accidents, and efforts to obtain immediate medical care. 
    Guardian means any person to whom custody of a minor has been given by a court order. 
    Minor means any person under 17 years of age. 
    Parent means a person who is the natural or adoptive parent of a person and includes, without limitation, a court appointed guardian or other person 18 years of age or older, authorized by the parent, by a court order, or by the court appointed guardian to have the care and custody of a person. 
    Public place means any place to which the public or a substantial group of the public has access and includes, but is not limited to, streets, highways, and the common areas of schools, hospitals, apartment houses, office buildings, transport facilities, and shops. 
(Code 1995, § 26.501; Ord. No. 734, 3-9-1994) 
Sec. 28-169. - Penalties. 
    Any minor violating the provisions of this division shall be guilty of a Class C misdemeanor and shall be subject to punishment in the manner provided by state law. A parent who violates this division shall be guilty of a misdemeanor punishable by a fine of not less than $50.00 or more than $500.00. In assessing punishment for either a parent or a child, the municipal court judges are encouraged to consider the community service program. 
(Code 1995, § 26.505; Ord. No. 734, 3-9-1994) 
Sec. 28-170. - Curfew hours. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any minor to purposefully remain, walk, run, stand, drive, or ride about, in, or upon any public place in the city between the hours of 12:00 a.m. and 5:00 a.m. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for the parent having legal custody of a minor to knowingly allow or permit the minor to be in violation of the curfew imposed in this section. 
(Code 1995, § 26.502; Ord. No. 735, 3-9-1994; Ord. No. 2012-5-12A, 5-12-2015 ) 
Sec. 28-171. - Defenses. 
    It is a defense to prosecution under this division if: 
(1)  The minor was accompanied by his parent; 
(2)  The minor was accompanied by another adult, approved by the parents; 
(3)  The minor was on an emergency errand; 
(4)  The minor was attending a school or religious activity or is going to, or coming from, a school, religious, or government sponsored activity; 
(5)  The minor was engaged in a lawful employment activity or is going directly to, or coming directly from, lawful employment; 
(6)  The minor was on the sidewalk of the place where such minor resides, or on the sidewalk of a place where the minor has permission from his parent or guardian to be, or on the sidewalk of a next-door neighbor not communicating an objection to the police officer; 
(7)  The minor was upon an errand directed by his parent; 
(8)  The minor was in a motor vehicle involved in intrastate or interstate transportation, or transportation for which passage through the curfew area is the most direct route; 
(9)  The minor was exercising his First Amendment rights protected by the United States Constitution, including, but not limited to, the free exercise of religion, freedom of speech, and the right of assembly; or 
(10)  The minor was married or had been married or had disabilities of minority removed in accordance with state law. 
(Code 1995, § 26.503; Ord. No. 734, 3-9-1994) 
Sec. 28-172. - Enforcement procedure. 
(a)  Any police officer, upon finding a minor in violation of this division, shall determine the name and address of the minor and the name and address of the minor's parents or guardians. The police officer may issue a warning notice to the minor, who shall be ordered to go home by the most direct means and route. A copy of the notice shall be forwarded to the parents or guardians of the minor advising of the fact that the minor was found in violation of this division and soliciting cooperation in the future. In the alternative, the police officer may proceed as provided in subsection (b) of this section. 
(b)  Any police officer, upon finding a minor in violation of this division, may, and in the event the minor has previously received a warning under subsection (a) of this section or has previously been found guilty of violating this division shall, transfer the case to proper authorities for handling under the provisions of state law. In addition, a complaint shall be filed against the parents or guardian of the minor in municipal court for violation of this division. 
(c)  The police department shall file all necessary legal papers, supply all necessary documentation, and provide necessary testimony as required for pursuing violation of this division by either the minor or by any parent or guardian. 
(Code 1995, § 26.504; Ord. No. 734, 3-9-1994; Ord. No. 1013, 1-20-2009) 
Chapter 29 - PARADES AND OTHER GATHERINGS 
ARTICLE I. - GENERAL 

Secs. 29-1--29-19. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PARADES 

Sec. 29-20. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Demonstration means a public display of the attitude of assembled persons toward a person, cause, issue, or other matter. 
    Parade means any parade, demonstration, march, ceremony, show, exhibition, pageant, or procession of any kind, or any similar display, in or upon any street, park, or other public place in the city. 
    Parade permit means a permit as required by this article. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-21. - Permit required. 
    No person shall engage in, participate in, aid, form or start any parade, unless a parade permit shall have been obtained from the chief of police. This section shall not apply to: 
(1)  Funeral processions; 
(2)  Students going to and from school, classes, or participating in educational activities, providing such conduct is under the immediate direction and supervision of the proper school authorities; 
(3)  A governmental agency acting within the scope of its functions. 
(4)  A private party held on private property and to which the public is not invited, provided such party does not impact public rights-of-way or involve activities or facilities not permitted by applicable zoning regulations. 
(5)  An event wholly contained on property specifically designed or suited for the event and that holds a certificate of occupancy for such use including adequate parking (e.g., a hotel ballroom). 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-22. - Applications. 
(a)  A person seeking issuance of a parade permit shall file an application with the chief of police on forms provided by such officer. The application for a parade permit shall be filed with the chief of police not less than five days, or more than thirty days, before the date on which it is proposed to conduct the parade and shall set forth the following information: 
(1)  The name, address, and telephone number of the person seeking to conduct such parade; 
(2)  If the parade is proposed to be conducted for, or on behalf of, or by an organization, the name, address, and telephone number of the headquarters of the organization and of the authorized and responsible heads of such organization; 
(3)  The name, address, and telephone number of the person who will be the parade chairperson and who will be responsible for its conduct; 
(4)  The date when the parade is to be conducted; 
(5)  The route to be traveled, the starting point, and the termination point; 
(6)  The approximate number of persons, and the animals and vehicles, which will constitute such parade; the type of animals and description of the vehicles; 
(7)  The hours when such parade will start and terminate; 
(8)  A statement as to whether the parade will occupy all or only a portion of the width of the streets proposed to be traversed; 
(9)  The location by streets of any assembly areas for such parade; 
(10)  The time at which units of the parade will begin to assemble at any such assembly area or areas; 
(11)  The interval of space to be maintained between units of such parade; 
(12)  If the parade is designed to be held by, and on behalf of, or for any person other than the applicant, the applicant for such permit shall file with the chief of police a communication in writing from the person proposing to hold the parade, authorizing the applicant to apply for the permit on his behalf; 
(13)  Any additional information which the chief of police shall find reasonably necessary to a fair determination as to whether a permit should issue. 
(b)  The chief of police, where good cause is shown therefore, shall have the authority to consider any application hereunder which is filed less than five days before the date such parade is proposed to be conducted. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-23. - Fee. 
    There shall be paid at the time of filing the application for a parade permit a fee in the amount provided in the city fee schedule. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-24. - Standards for issuance. 
    The chief of police shall issue a permit as provided for hereunder when, from a consideration of the application and from such other information as may otherwise be obtained, the chief of police makes a finding in accord with the following: 
(1)  Traffic. The conduct of the parade will not substantially interrupt the safe and orderly movement of other traffic contiguous to its route. 
(2)  Police protection. The conduct of the parade will not require the diversion of so great a number of police officers of the city to properly police the line of movement and the areas contiguous thereto as to prevent normal police protection to the city. 
(3)  Ambulances. The conduct of such parade will not require the diversion of so great a number of ambulances as to prevent normal ambulance service to portions of the city other than that to be occupied by the proposed line of march and areas contiguous thereto. 
(4)  Concentration of persons. The concentration of persons, animals, and vehicles at assembly points of the parade will not unduly interfere with proper fire and police protection of, or ambulance service to, areas contiguous to such assembly areas. 
(5)  Firefighting equipment. The conduct of such parade will not interfere with the movement of firefighting equipment en route to a fire. 
(6)  Disorderly conduct. The conduct of the parade is not reasonably likely to cause injury to persons or property, or to provoke disorderly conduct or create a disturbance. 
(7)  Schedule. The parade is scheduled to move from its point of origin to its point of termination expeditiously and without unreasonable delays en route. 
(8)  Non-commercial purpose. The parade is not to be held for the sole purpose of advertising any product, goods, or event, and is not designed to be held purely for private profit. 
(9)  Picketing or demonstrations. Picketing or demonstrations shall not be conducted without a parade permit and then shall be required to remain at a minimum distance of 400 feet from the center of any residential lot within the city. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-25. - Alternative permit. 
(a)  The chief of police, in denying an application for a parade permit, shall be empowered to authorize the conduct of the parade on a date, at a time, or over a route different from that named by the applicant. 
(b)  An applicant desiring to accept an alternate permit shall, within ten days after notice of the action of the chief of police, file a written notice of acceptance with the chief of police. An alternate parade permit shall conform to the requirements of, and shall have the effect of, a parade permit under this article. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-26. - Notice to city and other officials. 
    Immediately upon the issuance of a parade permit, the chief of police shall send a copy thereof to the mayor, city manager, city attorney and fire chief. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-27. - Contents of permit. 
    Each parade permit shall state the following information: 
(1)  Starting time; 
(2)  Minimum speed; 
(3)  Maximum speed; 
(4)  Maximum interval of space to be maintained between the units of the parade; 
(5)  The portions of the streets to be traversed that may be occupied by the parade; 
(6)  The maximum length of the parade in miles or fractions thereof; 
(7)  Such other information as the chief of police shall find necessary to the enforcement of this chapter. 
(8)  An applicant for a parade permit must execute a written agreement to indemnify the city and its officers and employees against all claims of injury or damage to persons or property, whether public or private, arising out of the parade. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-28. - Notice of rejection. 
    The chief of police shall act upon the application for a parade permit within ten days after the filing thereof. If the chief of police disapproves the application, he shall mail to the applicant, within ten days after the date upon which application was filed, a notice of his action, stating the reasons for his denial of the permit. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-29. - Revocation of permit. 
(a)  The chief of police shall have the authority to revoke a parade permit issued hereunder upon application of the standards for issuance as herein set forth. 
(b)  The city may, in its sole discretion, postpone, cancel, suspend or close any parade or special event or revoke a permit for any force majeure event (a "force majeure event" means and includes fire, casualty, failure of power, governmental authority, inclement weather, acts of God, war or terrorism or the potential or actual threat thereof, public safety or public welfare considerations, riots, or local, national or international emergencies, or other reason of like nature). 
(c)  The city shall have no liability for such postponement, cancellation, suspension or closing. Further, the city shall have no liability for failure to postpone, cancel, suspend, or close a parade or special event for the above-listed or any other reason. 
(d)  The city may revoke a permit at any time due to the failure of the permittee to comply with any of the terms or conditions of the permit, or any other rules and regulations of the city. 
(e)  The failure of the city to revoke a permit or to exercise any right, power or authority shall not constitute a waiver of the terms or conditions of the permit and shall not affect the rights of the city to enforce against any other or subsequent breach by the permittee. 
(f)  The revocation of a permit does not prohibit the city from exercising any and all additional rights and remedies available at law or equity against the permittee for failure to comply with the terms and conditions of the permit, or other ordinance, rule or regulation of the city. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-30. - Appeal procedure. 
    Any person aggrieved shall have the right to appeal the denial of a parade permit to the city council. The appeal shall be taken within ten days after notice. The city council shall act upon the appeal within 30 days after its receipt. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-31. - Duties of permittee. 
    A permittee hereunder shall comply with all permit directions and conditions and with all applicable laws and ordinances. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-32. - Possession of permit. 
    The parade chairperson or other person heading or leading such activity shall carry the parade permit upon his person during the conduct of the parade. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-33. - Interference and obstruction of parade prohibited. 
    Public conduct during parades shall comply with the following: 
(1)  Interference. No person shall unreasonably hamper, obstruct, or impede, or interfere with any parade or parade assembly or with any person, vehicle, or animal participating or used in a parade. 
(2)  Driving through parades. No driver of a vehicle, street car, or trackless trolley shall drive between the vehicles or persons comprising a parade when such vehicles or persons are in motion and are conspicuously designated as a parade. 
(3)  Parking on parade route. The chief of police shall have the authority, when reasonably necessary, to prohibit or restrict the parking of vehicles along a highway or part thereof constituting a part of the route of a parade. The chief of police shall post signs to such effect. It is unlawful for any person to park or leave unattended any vehicle in violation thereof. No person shall be liable for parking on a street unposted in violation of this chapter. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
ARTICLE III. - OTHER GATHERINGS 

Sec. 29-34. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning. 
    Bona fide educational purpose means providing cooking demonstrations solely for the purpose of informing, training, or educating persons how to prepare foods or providing samples in order to inform persons of the quality and characteristics of the sample and is not done in conjunction with the sale of food or food products. 
    Cottage food production operation means an individual, operating out of the individual's home, who: 
(1)  Produces a baked good, candy, coated and uncoated nuts, unroasted nut butters, fruit butters, a canned jam or jelly, a fruit pie, dehydrated fruit or vegetables, including dried beans, popcorn and popcorn snacks, cereal, including granola, dry mix, vinegar, pickles, mustard, roasted coffee or dry tea, or a dried herb or dried herb mix. 
(2)  Has an annual gross income of $50,000.00 or less from the sale of the described foods; and 
(3)  Sells the foods produced directly to consumers at the individual's home, a farmers' market, a farm stand, or a municipal, county, or nonprofit fair, festival or event. 
(4)  Delivers products to the consumer at the point of sale or another location designated by the consumer. 
A cottage food production operation is not a food establishment. 
    Farmer's market means a designated location used primarily for distribution and retail sales directly to consumers of food by farmers, cooperatives and other producers. 
    Labeling means food packaged in a food establishment shall include the common name of the food, a list of ingredients in predominance by weight if made from two or more products, declaration of quantity of contents, and the name and place of business of the manufacturer, packer or distributor. 
    Potentially hazardous food means a food that requires time and temperature control to limit pathogen growth or toxin production. 
    Producer means a person or entity that produces agricultural products by practice of the agricultural arts upon land that the person or entity controls. 
    Sample means a bite-sized portion of food or foods offered free of charge to demonstrate its characteristics and does not include a whole meal, an individual portion, or a whole sandwich. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-35. - Farmer's market. 
    Farmer's markets are authorized to be held in the city limits of Castle Hills in zoning districts allowing retail sales or on church, school or other nonprofit properties upon meeting the following requirements: 
(a)  The operator must provide to the city a lease or user agreement signed by both the operator of the farmer's market and the property owner; 
(b)  The operator must provide a site plan detailing the exact location of the set-up for the booths, trucks, or trailers, demonstrate that adequate parking is available for both producers and customers, show that adequate ingress and egress is available for the event, and ensure that fire lanes will remain unobstructed during the Farmer's Market; 
(c)  Producers must obtain from the city individual food licenses and farmer's market non-food vendor permits which will be subject to the city manager's approval; 
(d)  Noise permits must be obtained from the city if amplified sound is used at the farmer's market; 
(e)  "Hawking" to attract customers to the farmer's market or to a particular vendor is prohibited; 
(f)  Producers and vendors must comply with all state and local laws and regulations regarding farmer's markets, cottage food production, potentially hazardous food handling procedures, labeling requirements and sales and use taxes; and 
(g)  Cooking demonstrations and sampling are allowed but must be in compliance with state and local regulations. 
(h)  All permits and licenses shall be available for inspection upon request by any city official. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-36. - Mobile food vendors. 
(a)  Food trucks, food carts, and food trailers must have current inspection and licenses from a Texas city or county health district proof thereof and shall be available for inspection upon request by any city official. 
(b)  Mobile food vendors are allowed at special events hosted on church, school, government or other non-profit properties, and at farmer's markets and must obtain a temporary food license for the special event as detailed in section 20-28 of this Code. Any mobile food vendor wanting to operate at any other location requires the approval of the city manager. 
(c)  Mobile food vendors are not allowed to conduct sales on city streets or right-of-ways. 
(d)  Mobile food vendors may not utilize amplified sound without a noise permit. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-37. - Special events. 
    Special events sponsored by school, church, non-profit organizations or governmental entities such as fairs, festivals, haunted houses, pumpkin patches, horseshoe and washer tournaments, chili cook-offs, carnivals, and concerts held on the hosting organizations property are allowed without an event permit. Temporary food licenses, noise permits, other permits or licenses may be required. 
    Other special events including but not limited to fairs, festivals, haunted houses, chili cook-offs, run/walks, carnivals, concerts, block parties and other events or functions that could interfere with traffic and flow of emergency responder personnel and units will be with the approval of the city manager and the chief of police and may require an event permit. There shall be paid at the time of filing the application for a special event permit a fee in the amount provided in the city fee schedule. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Sec. 29-38. - Christmas tree sales. 
    Christmas tree sales shall be allowed with the following conditions: 
(a)  Christmas tree sales are permissible from November 15th thru December 25th. 
(b)  The tree vendor must provide to the city a lease or user agreement signed by both the operator of the tree sales and the property owner; 
(c)  All tree sales must be conducted in a zoning district allowing retail sales or on the property of the church, school or other nonprofit organization which is conducting the sale as a fund raiser for their organization. 
(d)  At the time of filing an application for a Christmas tree sales license, a Christmas tree sales permit fee shall be paid in the amount provided in the city fee schedule. 
( Ord. No. 2015-04-14A, 4-14-2015 ) 
Chapter 30 - PARKS AND RECREATION 
(RESERVED) 
Chapter 32 - PEDDLERS, SOLICITORS AND DISTRIBUTORS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Authority to permit, tax, suppress or otherwise regulate hawkers and peddlers, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 215.031; cancellation of certain home solicited consumer transactions, V.T.C.A., Business and Commerce Code § 601.001 et seq.; certain peddlers regarded as retailers for purposes of sales and use taxes, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 151.024. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 32-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Canvasser means a person who attempts to make personal contact with a resident at his residence without prior specific invitation or appointment from the resident, for the primary purpose of: 
(1)  Attempting to enlist support for or against a particular religion, philosophy, ideology, political party, issue or candidate, even if incidental to such purpose the canvasser accepts the donation of money for or against such cause; or 
(2)  Distributing a handbill or flyer advertising a noncommercial event or service. 
    Itinerant vendor or hawker means a person who sets up and operates a temporary business on privately owned property, whether improved or unimproved, in the city, soliciting, selling, or taking orders for, or offering to sell or take orders for any goods or services. A temporary business is one that continues for 45 days or less; and, exists whether solicitation is from a stand, vehicle, or freestanding.
