Such approval may be given only if lots in the area are more than one-half acre in size. The suggested scale of the key map is one inch equals one mile. 
(c)  The plat shall show or be accompanied by the following information: 
(1)  The name and legal description of the subdivision. 
(2)  Total acreage and total number of lots and blocks. 
(3)  Name of owner and, if the owner is a company or corporation, the name of responsible individual, such as president or vice-president. 
(4)  Name of the professional engineer and/or registered public surveyor. 
(5)  North arrow with north being at the top of the sheet, if possible. 
(6)  Date or most recent revision date. 
(7)  Key map showing the relation of the proposed subdivision to well-known streets, railroads, and watercourses in all directions to a distance of at least one mile. 
(8)  Boundaries. 
(9)  Subdivider's ownership boundaries (drawn in heavy lines) with overall dimensions and bearings. 
(10)  Departing lot and property lines as light or dashed. 
(11)  Approximate ties to well-established points. 
(12)  Name and boundary location of adjacent subdivisions, streets, easements, pipelines, watercourses, acreage tracts, and similar landmarks. 
(13)  Contours at two-foot intervals for subdivisions having an average slope of up to five percent and five-foot interval for subdivisions having an average slope over five percent. Contours may not be required on replats. 
(14)  The certificate of the professional engineer who performed engineering calculations or design for the plat (not needed for some replats). 
(15)  The certificate of the licensed surveyor who surveyed, mapped, and monumented the land. 
(16)  A certificate of ownership and dedication of all streets, easements, alleys, parks, and playgrounds to public use forever, signed and acknowledged before a notary public by the owner and lienholder of the land. 
(17)  A certificate of approval to be signed by the mayor after the city council approves the final plat. 
(18)  Two paper copies and one digital ("pdf" format) copy of the preliminary design plans and specifications prepared by professional engineers for water, sewer, paving, drainage, gas mains, and electric lines, Plans for sanitary sewers, streets, and drainage shall be drawn on sheets 11 by 17 or 22 by 34 inches. 
(d)  Where a site for a school, park, or other public facility is proposed, such site shall be reserved on the proposed plat for the proposed facility. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-48. - Action on preliminary plat. 
    The city manager and city engineer shall review the preliminary plat, and the provisions of law and of this Code applicable thereto, and consider the same in relation to the master plan of the city and other pertinent planning considerations, and then consult with the heads of city departments as needed. Thereafter, the city manager or city engineer shall issue comments, if necessary, to the subdivider. Once all of the city manager's and city engineer's comments have been addressed to the city manager's and city engineer's satisfaction, the plat will be eligible for submittal as a final plat. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Secs. 40-49-40-69. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - FINAL PLAT 

Sec. 40-70. - Required. 
    Application for a subdivision shall be made only by final plat. Preliminary plats will not be accepted for filing or considered to be filed, and shall not be considered as plats submitted for approval or disapproval. The city council will not act on preliminary plats, but only on final plats submitted with applications for subdivision. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-71. - Form and content; recording. 
(a)  The subdivider shall submit the final plat in the form of one original Mylar plat (final version), two white print copies, and one digital file in "pdf" format to the city manager for city council action. The city manager shall immediately forward one paper copy and one digital copy to the city engineer for verification. The original Mylar plat will be recorded in the county clerk's office, if approved, and a reproducible digital copy shall remain filed with the city as its permanent record thereof. No final plat will be considered by council unless a preliminary plat has first been submitted to and accepted by the city manager. Final plats to be considered by council shall be filed with the city manager at least five days prior to the meeting at which approval is requested. 
(b)  Plats shall be drawn in ink on Mylar and paper sheets 18 by 24 inches to with a 21/2 margin on the left and one-half-inch border on the other three sides. 
(c)  The final plat shall show or be accompanied by all items required for a preliminary plat plus the following: 
(1)  An accurate on-the-ground boundary survey of the property with perimeter and internal lot lines, bearings and distances, pinned corners, monuments, and curve data. 
(2)  Departing lot and property lines with descriptions of adjacent land. 
(3)  Streets, alleys, rights-of-way, and easements, in and adjacent to the proposed subdivision with names and widths. 
(4)  Ties to well-established points, such as property corners at street intersections, and geo-referenced coordinates based on NAD83. For subdivisions of five acres or less, provide a minimum of one tie and two geo-referenced points on property corners. For each five acres in excess of five acres, add one tie and one geo-referenced point. Space the ties and geo-referenced points as evenly as feasible around the perimeter of the proposed subdivision. 
(5)  Two paper copies and one digital ("pdf" format) copy of the detailed design plans and specifications prepared by professional engineers for water, sewer, paving, drainage, gas mains, and electric lines, which must be approved by the city engineer prior to the beginning of any construction of the subdivision. Plans for sanitary sewers, streets, and drainage shall be drawn on sheets 11 by 17 or 22 by 34 inches. 
(6)  Monuments to be located as approved by the city engineer shall be shown on the plat, one-half-inch iron rod, four feet long, set in concrete six inches in diameter and 18 inches deep set flush with the top of the rod and flush with the natural ground. 
(7)  A letter from the city engineer to the city council, stating that he does not object to the plans for the subdivision drainage. 
(8)  A letter from the servicing utility companies stating that the plat includes the easements required by them in the furnishing of utilities to this and future subdivisions and that they are willing and able to furnish utility service to the proposed lots. 
(9)  Two copies of deed restrictions. 
(10)  Maintenance bond required by this chapter. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-72. - Action on final plat. 
(a)  The final or record plat shall be presented to the city council by the city manager at a regularly called or special meeting thereof within 30 days after the filing of same with the city manager, together with the city manager's final recommendations and those of the city engineer, and the council shall fully consider and finally act on such plat, either to approve or disapprove the same (one or the other, with no partial or conditional approval to be made) at the same meeting. 
(b)  If the final plat is considered at a meeting held less than 30 days after the filing of same with the city manager, the council may, in its discretion, recess the final consideration thereof to its next meeting, provided such meeting is to be held within the 30-day period as regularly scheduled under the provisions of this code, or is legally called within such period by the mayor or by three members of the council at or before the time action thereon is postponed. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Secs. 40-73-40-102. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - STREETS, ALLEYS, WALKS AND RELATED STRUCTURES 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 40-103. - Definitions. 
    When the term "engineer" is used in the Standard Specifications for Construction and Maintenance of Highways, Streets and Bridges, published by the Texas Department of Transportation and referred to in this article, it shall be interpreted to mean the city engineer. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-104. - Maintenance bond required; acceptance of improvements by city. 
(a)  The subdivider shall file an agreement in writing to provide a maintenance bond prior to final subdivision plat approval. After final approval, but before the plat shall be recorded, the subdivider shall furnish the city a bond, executed by a surety company holding a license to do business in the state and acceptable to the city council, in an amount equal to ten percent of the total cost of the streets, curbs, sidewalks, and storm drains required to be constructed in the subdivision, as estimated by the developer's engineer, conditioned that upon completion thereof, and upon approval of same by the city engineer, the subdivider will maintain such streets, storm drains, and the like in good condition at his expense for a period of at least one year after the date of the final approval of the completed construction by the city engineer and until acceptance thereof by the city. 
(b)  The city council shall not accept such streets and storm drains on behalf of the city for a period of at least one year after such proper completion, as certified by the city engineer, and not then unless and until the city engineer again certifies that they have been maintained in good condition for a period of one year and are in good condition at such time. 
(c)  The city shall accept such streets and sewers only by written ordinance or resolution duly passed at a regular or legally called special meeting of the city council, and the subdivider shall remain responsible for the maintenance of such improvements until thus legally accepted by the city. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-105. - Laboratory tests to be submitted; cost to be born by developer. 
    All laboratory test results referred to in this article will be performed at the expense of the developer and submitted to the city engineer as proof of the adequacy of material or operation. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Secs. 40-106-40-123. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PLANNING AND DESIGN 

Sec. 40-124. - Planning. 
(a)  The plan and profile drawings for street, alley, cross walkways, and drainage easement improvements shall include the following information: 
(1)  For each different type of street or alley in the subdivision, typical sections showing the proposed pavement width, type, thickness, and crown; the proposed curb or curb and gutter type, location in relation to centerline and exposure; the proposed sidewalk dimensions and location in relation to curbs and property lines; and the proposed parkway grading slopes. 
(2)  Construction details of all drainage structures, including dimensions, reinforcing and components such as grates and manhole covers. 
(3)  Alignment of each street, alley, cross walkway, and drainage easement showing: 
a.  A beginning and ending station; 
b.  Each deflection angle of the centerline and the station of the point of intersection; 
c.  The station of the point of curvature and the point of tangency of each curve; 
d.  The station and angle of intersection of each street, alley, or drainage easement intersection; 
e.  The station and radius of each curb return; 
f.  The location of adjacent right-of-way lines; 
g.  The location and limits of sidewalks and curbs of each street; 
h.  The location of each drainage structure; 
i.  The location and size of all storm sewers. 
(4)  The length, width, and thickness of the flexible, cement-stabilized, or asphaltic base. 
(5)  The location of monuments. 
(6)  Location, description, and elevation of: 
a.  Bench marks; 
b.  The top of curb grade at each curb end, each 50-foot station, and each end of each curb return; 
c.  The centerline grade at each end and at each 50-foot station of alleys and drainage ditches; 
d.  The slope of each tangent and the location and length of each vertical curve; 
e.  The direction of storm drainage flow at each intersection; 
f.  The flow line elevations of each drainage structure; 
g.  The flow line elevation of each storm sewer at each point of slope change; and 
h.  The natural ground at adjacent property lines, the proposed centerline, and near the proposed edge of pavement. 
(b)  The plan and the profile shall be drawn to scale of one inch equals 20 feet horizontally and one inch equals two feet vertically. 
(c)  All street and alley plans and profiles shall bear the seal of a registered professional engineer. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-125. - Design standards. 
(a)  At each street intersection the curb shall be rounded with radius to the face of the curb varying with the interior angle as specified in the following table, unless sufficient data is presented to show the strict adherence to this requirement is impractical due to topographic or engineering considerations.

Secs. 40-126-40-148. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - CONSTRUCTION STANDARDS AND SPECIFICATIONS 

Sec. 40-149. - Preparation of subgrade. 
(a)  The subgrade shall be shaped in conformity to the lines and grades established by the plans by removal of existing material or addition of approved material. Material removed in one area may be utilized in the addition of material to the subgrade in another area if approved by the city engineer. All material required for completion of the subgrade shall be subject to approval by the City Engineer. 
(b)  Remove all unstable or otherwise objectionable material of the subgrade and replace with approved materials. Fill all holes, ruts, and depressions with approved material, and, if required, thoroughly wet the subgrade with water, reshape, and roll to the extent directed in order to place the subgrade in an acceptable condition to receive the base material. 
(c)  Rock Cuts. Excavate to finished subgrade elevation. Manipulate and compact subgrade in accordance with (e) below, unless excavation is to clean homogenous rock at finished subgrade elevation. If excavation extends below finished subgrade, use approved material compacted in accordance with (e) below to replace undercut material. 
(d)  Earth cuts. Scarify all earth cuts to a uniform depth of at least 6-inches below the required finished subgrade elevation. Compact the scarified subgrade in accordance with (e) below. 
(e)  Compaction. Subgrade materials shall be compacted to the required density and moisture content as shown below, unless otherwise shown on the plans: 
PI Range Density Moisture Content PI = 20 = 95% of Max. Dry Density -2% of Opt. or greater PI > 20 = 95% of Max. Dry Density = Opt. Moisture  
  
(1)  Determine maximum dry density and optimum moisture content in accordance with TxDOT Test Method Tex-114-E. Test for in-place density in accordance with TxDOT Test Method Tex-115-E and within 24 hours after compacting operations are completed. If the material fails to meet the density specified, re-work it as necessary to obtain the density required. 
(2)  For materials with a PI > 20, test the top three inches of compacted subgrade for density and moisture content just prior to placing any base materials or stabilization. If tests show the density to be more than two percent below the specified minimum or the moisture content to be more than three percent above or below the optimum, rework the course as necessary to obtain the specified compaction and moisture content. 
(3)  If the material used to replace undercuts or unsuitable material contains more than 30 percent oversize fraction (i.e. 30% or more retained on the 3/4-inch sieve) or is gap-graded (many large particles with limited small particles), the maximum density determined by Tex-114-E may not be appropriate for field compaction. If this situation is encountered, the city engineer may elect to accept the material without density testing. With the approval of the city engineer, place layers in loose lifts not to exceed 12 inches. Before and during rolling operations, bring each layer to the moisture content directed. Compact each layer until there is no evidence of further consolidation. Maintain a level layer to aid in uniform compaction. If the required stability or finish is lost for any reason, re-compact. 
(4)  Compact trenches installed in conformance to this specification. 
(f)  Tolerances. Finish the surface of the subgrade to the lines and grades as shown on the plans. Correct any deviation in excess of one-half-inch in cross section and in a length of 16-feet measured longitudinally by loosening, adding, or removing material, reshaping and compacting by sprinkling and rolling in accordance with (e) above. 
(g)  Quality control. After each layer of embankment or select material is complete, test as necessary to the satisfaction of the City Engineer. If the material fails to meet the density specified, the course shall be reworked, as necessary, to obtain the specified compaction. Should the subgrade, due to any reason or cause, lose the required stability, density, or moisture content as described in (e) above or finish before the pavement is placed, it shall be re-compacted in accordance with (e) above. Prevent excessive loss of moisture in the subgrade by sprinkling, sealing, or covering with a subsequent layer of asphaltic or other approved material. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-150. - Flexible base course. 
(a)  Construct a base course for surfacing, pavement, or other base courses composed of crushed stone, and constructed as herein specified in one or more courses in conformance with the typical sections shown on the plans. 
(b)  Furnish uncontaminated materials of uniform quality. Flexible base shall be TxDOT Type A, Grade 1 or Grade 2. Modifications, such as the addition of recycled asphalt pavement (RAP) will be considered on a case by case basis. 
(c)  Notify the city engineer of the proposed material sources and of changes to material sources. The city engineer may sample and test project materials at any time to assure specification compliance. Use the TxDOT standard laboratory test procedure Tex-100-E for material definitions. 
(d)  Construct each layer uniformly, free of loose or segregated areas, and with the required density and moisture content. Provide a smooth surface that conforms to the typical sections, lines, and grades shown on the plans or as directed. 
(e)  Spread and shape flexible base into a uniform layer with an approved spreader the same day as delivered unless otherwise approved. Construct layers to the thickness shown on the plans. Maximum lift thickness shall be 10 inches of loose material. Maintain the shape of the course. Control dust by sprinkling, as directed. Correct or replace segregated areas as directed. Place successive base courses and finish courses using the same construction methods required for the first course. 
(f)  Compact in courses not to exceed eight inches compacted depth using density control unless otherwise shown on the plans. Multiple lifts are permitted when shown on the plans or approved. Bring each layer to the moisture content directed. When necessary, sprinkle the material in accordance with TxDOT Item 204, "Sprinkling." 
(g)  Compact to at least 95 percent of the maximum density determined by TxDOT's standard laboratory test procedure Tex-113-E unless otherwise shown on the plans. Determine the moisture content of the material at the beginning and during compaction in accordance with TxDOT's standard laboratory test procedure Tex-103-E. 
(h)  After completing compaction, clip, skin, or tight-blade the surface with a maintainer or subgrade trimmer to a depth of approximately one-quarter inch. Remove loosened material and dispose of it at an approved location. Seal the clipped surface immediately by rolling with a pneumatic tire roller until a smooth surface is attained. Add small increments of water as needed during rolling. Shape and maintain the course and surface in conformity with the typical sections, lines, and grades as shown on the plans or as directed. 
(i)  In areas where surfacing is to be placed, correct grade deviations greater than one-quarter inch in 16 feet measured longitudinally or greater than one-quarter inch over the entire width of the cross-section. Correct by loosening, adding, or removing material. Reshape and re-compact. 
(j)  Cure the finished section until the moisture content is at least three percentage points below and above optimum or as directed before applying the next successive course or prime coat. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Secs. 40-151, 40-152. - Reserved. 
Sec. 40-153. - Surface treatment. 
(a)  All materials shall be of the type and grade as shown on the plans and shall conform to the pertinent material requirements of the following: 
(1)  Asphaltic Cement. TxDOT Item 300, "Asphalts, Oils, and Emulsions." 
(2)  Aggregates. TxDOT Item 302, "Aggregates for Surface Treatments." 
(b)  Provide applicable equipment in accordance with this specification. 
(1)  Distributor. Furnish a distributor that will apply the asphalt material uniformly at the specified rate or as directed. 
(2)  Aggregate spreader. Use a continuous-feed, self-propelled spreader to apply aggregate uniformly at the specified rate or as directed. 
(3)  Broom. Furnish rotary, self-propelled brooms. 
(4)  Aggregate haul trucks. Unless otherwise authorized, use trucks of uniform capacity to deliver the aggregate. Provide documentation showing measurements and calculation in cubic yards. Clearly mark the calibrated level. 
(5)  Rollers. Unless otherwise shown on the plans, rollers shall be the Pneumatic Tire type. 
(c)  Weather. Do not place surface treatments when, in the city engineer's opinion, general weather conditions are unsuitable. 
(d)  Standard temperature limitations. Apply surface treatment when air temperature is above 50°F and rising. Do not apply surface treatment when air temperature is 60°F and falling. In all cases, do not apply surface treatment when surface temperature is below 60°F. 
(e)  Polymer-modified asphalt cement temperature limitations. When using materials described in TxDOT Item 300, Section 2.B, "Polymer Modified Asphalt Cement," apply surface treatment when air temperature is above 70°F rising. Do not apply surface treatment when air temperature is 80°F and falling. In all cases, do not apply surface treatment when surface temperature is below 70°F. 
(f)  Surface preparation. Remove existing raised pavement markers. Repair any damage incurred by removal as directed. Remove dirt, dust, or other harmful material before sealing. 
(g)  Place building paper over all manholes, valve boxes, grates, etc., so as to protect the surfaces from asphaltic materials. Asphaltic materials shall not be placed, lapped, or splashed onto adjacent structures. 
(h)  Asphalt placement. 
(1)  General. Adjust the shot width so operations do not encroach on traffic or interfere with the traffic control plan, as directed. Use paper or other approved material at the beginning and end of each shot to construct a straight transverse joint and to prevent overlapping of the asphalt. Unless otherwise approved, match longitudinal joints with the lane lines. The city engineer may require a string line if necessary to keep joints straight with no overlapping. Use sufficient pressure to flare the nozzles fully. In those areas where the asphalt distributor is not accessible, hand spraying may be permitted by the city engineer. Select an application temperature, as approved. Uniformly apply the asphalt material at the rate shown on the plans or as directed by the city engineer, within 15°F of the approved temperature, and not above the maximum allowable temperature. 
(2)  Limitations. Do not apply asphalt to the roadway until: 
i.  Traffic control methods and devices are in place as shown on the plans or as directed; 
ii.  The loaded aggregate spreader is in position and ready to begin; 
iii.  Haul trucks are loaded with enough aggregate to cover the shot area; and 
iv.  Haul trucks are in place behind the spreader box. 
(3)  Non-uniform applications. Stop application if it is not uniform due to streaking, ridging, puddling, or flowing off the roadway surface. Verify equipment condition, operating procedures, application temperature, and material properties. Determine and correct the cause of non-uniform application. If the cause is high or low emulsion viscosity, replace emulsion with material that corrects the problem. 
(4)  Test strips. The city engineer may stop asphalt application and require construction of test strips at the contractor's expense if any of the following occurs: 
i.  Non-uniformity of application continues after corrective action; 
ii.  On three consecutive shots, application rate differs by more than 0.03 gallons per square yard from the rate directed; or 
iii.  Any shot differs by more than 0.05 gallons per square yard from the rate directed. 
The city engineer will approve the test strip location. The city engineer may require additional test strips until surface treatment application meets specification requirements. 
(i)  Aggregate placement. As soon as possible, apply aggregate uniformly at the rate directed without causing the rock to roll over. 
(j)  Rolling. Start rolling operation on each shot as soon as aggregate is applied. Use sufficient rollers to cover the entire mat width in one pass, i.e., one direction. Roll in a staggered pattern. Unless otherwise shown on the plans, make a minimum of: 
(1)  Five passes; or 
(2)  Three passes when the asphalt material is an emulsion. 
If rollers are unable to keep up with the spreader box, stop application until rollers have caught up, or furnish additional rollers. Keep roller tires asphalt-free. 
(k)  Patching. Before rolling, repair spots where coverage is incomplete. Repair can be made by hand spotting or other approved method. When necessary, apply additional asphalt material to embed aggregate. 
(l)  Brooming. After rolling, sweep as soon as aggregate has sufficiently bonded to remove excess. After rolling of the finished surface is completed, all parkways, private property, and driveways adjacent to the work shall be cleared of any surplus aggregate by the Contractor by sweeping. Prevent loose aggregate from creating a hazard to traffic. 
(m)  Two-course surface treatments. It is the intent of this specification that the application of asphalt and aggregate for multiple courses be applied within the same day, or immediately thereafter, and prior to opening the roadway to traffic. Apply asphaltic material for each course of the surface treatment and cover with aggregate in the same manner specified for the first application. Each surface shall then be broomed or raked and thoroughly rolled as specified for the first course. Asphaltic material and aggregate for each course shall be applied at the rates directed by the city engineer or as shown on the plans. 
(n)  Repair all holes or failures in the surface by use of additional asphalt and aggregate. Cover all fat or bleeding surfaces with approved cover material in such a manner that the asphaltic material will not adhere to or be picked up by the wheels of vehicles. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-154. - Tack coat. 
(a)  The asphaltic material used for tack coat shall meet the requirements for "Asphalt Cement", "Cut-Back Asphalt" or "Emulsified Asphalt" in Item No. 300, "Asphalts, Oils and Emulsions" of the Texas Department of Transportation Standard Specifications. The asphaltic material used for Tack Coat shall be the type or grade shown in the referring specification, or on the plans, or as directed/approved by the city engineer. 
(b)  Before the tack coat is applied, the surface shall be cleaned thoroughly with a vacuum sweeper. The asphaltic material shall be applied on the clean surface by an approved type of self-propelled pressure distributor evenly and smoothly under a pressure necessary for proper distribution. The tack coat shall be applied at the rate specified by the referring specification or on the plans. Unless otherwise stated or allowed by the city engineer the application rate shall not exceed 0.10 gallon per square yard of surface. 
(c)  Where the pavement mixture will adhere to the surface on which it is to be placed without the use of a tack coat, the tack coat may be eliminated. All contact surfaces of curbs and structures and all joints shall be painted with a thin uniform coat of the asphaltic material used for tack coat. During the application of tack coat, care shall be taken to prevent splattering of adjacent pavement, curb and gutters or structures. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-155. - Hot mix asphaltic concrete pavement. 
(a)  Materials used in hot mix asphaltic concrete pavement shall meet the requirements as set forth herein. If shown on the plans, materials may also meet the requirements as described in Item 340, "Dense-Graded Hot-Mix Asphalt (Method)" or Item 341, "Dense-Graded Hot-Mix Asphalt (QC/QA)" of the Texas Department of Transportation Standard Specifications for Construction and Maintenance of Highways, Streets, and Bridges. 
(b)  Unless otherwise shown on the plans, provide aggregates that meet the aggregate quality requirements of TxDOT's Bituminous Rated Source Quality Catalog (BRSQC). Aggregates shall conform to the requirements shown in Table 1 herein, and as specified in this section. When reclaimed asphalt pavement (RAP) is used, provide RAP stockpiles in accordance with this section. Aggregate from RAP is not required to meet Table 1 requirements unless otherwise shown on the plans. 
(c)  Document all test results on a mixture design report and submit to the city engineer for approval. The city engineer may perform tests on independent or split samples to verify contractor mix design results. Stockpile aggregates for each source and type separately. Determine aggregate gradations for mixture design and production testing based on the washed sieve analysis given in TxDOT standard laboratory test procedure Tex-200-F, Part II. 
(d)  Unless otherwise shown on the plans, reclaimed asphalt pavement (RAP) may be used in asphalt pavement maintenance or rehabilitation applications and shall be limited to a maximum of 20 percent RAP for surface or wearing courses and 30 percent RAP for courses below the surface or wearing course. 
(e)  Coarse aggregate. Provide aggregates with a surface aggregate classification (SAC) as shown below: 
Street Classification Min. SAC Primary and Secondary Arterials A Collector and Local Type B Streets B Local Type A Street With Bus Traffic B Local Type A Street Without Bus Traffic C  
  
(f)  Reclaimed asphalt pavement (RAP). RAP is defined as a salvaged, pulverized, broken or crushed asphalt pavement. The RAP to be used in the mix shall be crushed or broken to the extent that 100 percent will pass the two-inch sieve. The stockpiled RAP shall not be contaminated by dirt or other objectionable materials. Unless otherwise shown on the plans, stockpiled, crushed RAP shall have a decantation of five percent or less and a plasticity index of eight or less, when tested in accordance with TxDOT standard laboratory test procedures Tex-406-A, Part I, and Tex-106-E, respectively. This requirement applies to stockpiles from which the asphalt has not been removed by extraction. 
(g)  Fine aggregate. Fine aggregates may consist of manufactured sands, screenings and field sands. Supply fine aggregates that are free from organic impurities. Field sands and other uncrushed aggregates shall be limited to 15 percent of the total aggregate. If ten percent or more of the fine aggregate stockpile is retained on the No. 4 sieve, test the stockpile and verify that it meets the requirements in Table 1 for coarse aggregate angularity (TxDOT standard laboratory test procedure Tex-460-A) and flat and elongated particles (TxDOT standard laboratory test procedure Tex-280-F). 
(h)  Asphalt binder. Unless shown on the plans, provide the type and grade of performance graded asphalt binder in accordance with TxDOT Item 300.2.J. "Performance-Graded Binders" and as specified below:

(i)  Mineral filler. Mineral filler consists of finely divided mineral matter such as agricultural lime, crusher fines, hydrated lime, cement, or fly ash. Mineral filler is allowed unless otherwise shown on the plans. Do not use more than two percent hydrated lime or cement, unless otherwise shown on the plans. The plans may require or disallow specific mineral fillers. When used, provide mineral filler that: 
(1)  Is sufficiently dry, free-flowing, and free from clumps and foreign matter; 
(2)  Does not exceed three percent linear shrinkage when tested in accordance with Tex-107-E; and 
(3)  Meets the gradation requirements of Table 3 herein. 
(j)  Baghouse fines. Fines collected by the baghouse or other dust collecting equipment may be reintroduced into the mixing drum. 
(k)  Tack coat. Unless otherwise shown on the plans or approved, furnish CSS-1H, SS-1H, or a PG binder with a minimum high-temperature grade of PG 58 for tack coat binder and in accordance with Item 203, "Tack Coat." Do not dilute emulsified asphalts at the terminal, in the field, or at any other location before use. 
(l)  Additives. When shown on the plans, use the type and rate of additive specified. Other additives that facilitate mixing or improve the quality of the mixture may be allowed when approved. If lime or a liquid antistripping agent is used, add in accordance with TxDOT Item 301, "Asphalt Antistripping Agents." Do not add lime directly into the mixing drum of any plant where lime is removed through the exhaust stream, unless the plant has a baghouse or dust collection system that reintroduces the lime back into the drum.

(m)  Equipment. All equipment for the handling of all materials, mixing, placing and compacting of the mixture shall be maintained in good repair and operating condition and subject to the approval of the city engineer. Any equipment found to be defective and potentially having a negative effect on the quality of the paving mixture or ride quality will not be allowed. 
(n)  Design. Provide the City Engineer with a mixture design report that includes the following items: 
(1)  The combined aggregate gradation, source, specific gravity, and percent of each material used; 
(2)  Results of all applicable tests; 
(3)  The mixing and molding temperatures; 
(4)  All applicable correlation and correction factors; 
(5)  The signature of the Level II person or persons who performed the design; 
(6)  The date the mixture design was performed; and 
(7)  A unique identification number for the mixture design.

(o)  Tack coat. The surface upon which the tack coat is to be placed shall be cleaned thoroughly. The surface shall be given a uniform application of tack coat using asphaltic materials of this specification. Unless otherwise shown on the plans, tack coat shall be applied with an approved sprayer at an approved rate between 0.04 and 0.10 gallon residual asphalt per square yard of surface. 
(p)  Transporting asphaltic concrete. The asphaltic mixture shall be hauled to the work site in vehicles previously cleaned of all foreign material and with beds that do not discharge or lose materials during the haul. Trucks that do not meet the satisfaction of the city engineer or inspector will not be allowed to deliver materials to city projects. The dispatching of the vehicles shall be arranged so that all material is delivered, placed, and rolled during daylight hours unless otherwise shown on the plans. In cool weather, or for long hauls, covering and insulating of the truck bodies may be required. If necessary, to prevent the mixture from adhering to the inside of the truck body, the inside of the truck may be given a light coating of release agent satisfactory to the city engineer. 
(q)  Placement. 
(1)  Weather conditions. Place mixture, when placed with a spreading and finishing machine, or the tack coat when the roadway surface temperature is 60°F or higher unless otherwise approved. Measure the roadway surface temperature with a handheld infrared thermometer. Place mixtures only when weather conditions and moisture conditions of the roadway surface are suitable in the opinion of the city engineer. 
(2)  Temperature conditions. The asphaltic mixture, when placed with a motor grader, shall not be placed when the surface temperature is below 65°F and is falling, but may be placed when the surface temperature is above 55°F and is rising. The maximum depth of asphalt mixture placed with a motor grader will not exceed five inches of compacted material. Mat thicknesses of 11/2 inches and less shall not be placed when the temperature of the surface on which the mat is to be placed is below 60°F. 
(3)  Tack coat or asphaltic mixture shall be placed only when the humidity, general weather conditions, temperature and moisture condition of the base are suitable. 
(4)  Placement temperature. If, after being discharged from the mixer and prior to placing, the temperature of the asphaltic mixture falls below 200°F, all or any part of the load may be rejected and payment will not be made for the rejected material. 
(5)  Placement operations. Prepare the surface by removing raised pavement markers and objectionable material such as moisture, dirt, sand, leaves, and other loose impediments from the surface before placing mixture. Remove vegetation from pavement edges. The asphaltic mixture shall be dumped and spread on the approved prepared surface with the spreading and finishing machine. Place the mixture to meet the typical section requirements and produce a smooth, finished surface with a uniform appearance and texture. In addition, the placing of the asphaltic mixture shall be completed without tearing, shoving, gouging or segregating the mixture and without producing streaks in the mat. Unloading into the finishing machine shall be controlled so that bouncing or jarring the spreading and finishing machine shall not occur and the required lines and grades shall be obtained without resorting to hand finishing. When approved by the city engineer, level-up courses may be spread with a motor grader. Construction joints of successive courses of asphaltic material shall be offset at least six inches. Construction joints on surface courses shall coincide with lane lines, or as directed by the city engineer. The spreading and finishing machine shall be operated at a uniform forward speed consistent with the plant production rate, hauling capability, and roller train capacity to result in a continuous operation. The speed shall be slow enough that stopping between trucks is not ordinarily required. If, in the opinion of the Inspector, sporadic delivery of material is adversely affecting the mat, the Inspector may require paving operations to cease until acceptable methods are provided to minimize starting and stopping of the paver. The hopper flow gates of the spreading and finishing machine shall be adjusted to provide an adequate and consistent flow of material. These shall result in enough material being delivered to the augers so that they are operating approximately 85 percent of the time or more. The augers shall provide means to supply adequate flow of material to the center of the paver. Augers shall supply an adequate flow of material for the full width of the mat, as approved by the city engineer. Augers should be kept approximately one-half to three-quarters full of mixture at all times during the paving operation. If a pattern of surface irregularities or segregation is detected, the contractor shall make an investigation into the causes and immediately take the necessary action. With the approval of the inspector, placement may continue for no more than one full production day from the time the Contractor is first notified and while corrective actions are being taken. Place mixture within the compacted lift thickness shown in Table 8, unless otherwise shown on the plans or allowed. Use the guidelines in Table 9 to establish the temperature of mixture delivered to the paver.

(r)  Compaction. The pavement shall be compacted thoroughly and uniformly with the necessary rollers to obtain the compaction and cross section of the finished paving mixture meeting the requirements of the plans and specifications. The edges of the pavement along curbs, headers and similar structures, and all places not accessible to the roller, or in such positions as will not allow thorough compaction with the rollers, shall be thoroughly compacted with lightly oiled tamps. Rolling with a trench roller will be required on widened areas, in trenches and other limited areas where satisfactory compaction cannot be obtained with the approved rollers. All rolling for compaction shall be completed before the mixture temperature drops below 175°F. 
(s)  Quality control and acceptance. Control and acceptance of hot mixed asphaltic concrete pavement shall be followed as specified herein or as directed on the plans. The contractor shall conduct production and placement operations in accordance with the method specified. All testing will be conducted in accordance with the testing methods shown in Table 10. 
Table 10 
Acceptable Production and Placement Testing Methods 
Description Test Method Gradation including % passing the #200 sieve Tex-200-F or Tex-236-F Laboratory-molded density Tex-207-F VMA Laboratory-molded bulk specific gravity In-Place air voids Segregation (density profile) Tex-207-F, Part V Longitudinal joint density Tex-207-F, Part VII Moisture content Tex-212-F, Part II Theoretical maximum specific (Rice).gravity Tex-227-F Asphalt content Tex-236-F Hamburg Wheel test Tex-242-F Thermal profile Tex-244-F Asphalt binder sampling and testing 1 Tex-500-C Boil test 1 Tex-530-C  
1.  The engineer may waive the sampling and testing requirements at then discretion. 
(1)  In-place density. For every 500 tons of compacted asphaltic material or as directed by the city engineer, test the in place density. The in place density shall be in the range of 92.0% to 97.0% of the maximum density. Do not increase the asphalt content of the mixture to increase pavement density. Unless otherwise shown on the plans, obtain 2 roadway specimens at each location selected by the city engineer for in-place density determination. Unless otherwise determined, the city engineer will witness the coring operation and measurement of the core thickness. Unless otherwise approved, obtain the cores within one working day after placement is completed. Obtain two six-inch diameter cores side-by-side from within one foot of the location provided by the city engineer. For Type C, D and F mixtures, four inch diameter cores are allowed. Mark the cores for identification. Visually inspect each core and verify that the current paving layer is bonded to the underlying layer. If an adequate bond does not exist between the current and underlying layer, take corrective action to insure that an adequate bond will be achieved during subsequent placement operations. Immediately after obtaining the cores, dry the core holes and tack the sides and bottom. Fill the hole with the same type of mixture and properly compact the mixture. Repair core holes with other methods when approved. If the core heights exceed the minimum untrimmed values listed in Table 8, trim the cores within one working day following placement operations unless otherwise approved. If the core height before trimming is less than the minimum untrimmed value shown in Table 8, decide whether or not to include the pair of cores in the density determination for that sublot. If the cores are to be included in density determination, trim the cores. If the cores will not be included in density determination, store untrimmed cores for the city engineer. The developer's engineer will measure density in accordance with Tex-207-F and Tex-227-F. If the in-place density in the compacted mixture is below 92 percent or greater than 97 percent, change the production and placement operations to bring the in-place density within requirements. The city engineer may suspend production until the in-place density is brought to the required level, and may require a test section as described below, before proceeding. 
(2)  At the onset of production, or after production and placement operations have been altered to bring the in-place density into conformance, construct a test section of one lane-width and at most 0.2 miles in length to demonstrate that compaction to between 92.0 percent and 97.0 percent in-place density can be obtained. Continue this procedure until a test section with the correct density can be produced. The city engineer will allow only two test sections per day. When a test section producing satisfactory in-place air void content is placed, resume full production. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-156. - Concrete sidewalk, cross walkways, and drive approaches. 
(a)  Concrete sidewalk, cross walkways, and drive approaches shall be constructed in conformity to the typical sections and to the established lines and grades. 
(b)  Forms may be either metal or wood. Where wood forms are used, they shall be of material well seasoned and clean. All forms must everywhere extend the full depth of the concrete, and must be well braced so that the placing and tamping of the concrete will not bulge them. 
(c)  Before concrete is placed, forms must be thoroughly wet with water, or treated with light clear oil. 
(d)  Subgrade for sidewalks, cross walkways, and drive approaches shall be excavated so as to have a layer or cushion at least two inches thick of crusher screening, gravel and sand, crushed rock, or coarse sand which must be spread, wetted, and thoroughly tamped and leveled not less than four inches below the established grade for sidewalks and cross walkways and not less than five inches below the established grade for driveway approaches. Where the subgrade is rock or gravel, the two inches of cushion need not be used. 
(e)  In the event the subgrade is undercut, the necessary backfill shall be made with the same material used for the two-inch cushion. 
(f)  Reinforcement for sidewalks and cross walkways shall consist of one layer of six by six-inch, No. 10 wire mesh or No. 3 (three-eighths-inch) round bars placed not more than 18 inches on centers, both directions. Where steel is lapped, the lap shall not be less than 15 inches. Reinforcement for drive approaches shall consist of one layer of six-inch by six-inch, No. 6 wire mesh or No. 3 bars as specified for sidewalks. 
(g)  Transverse expansion joints three-eighths-inch in thickness, and extending the full width of the walk, shall be provided at intervals of not more than 50 feet. Joints must be the full depth of the concrete, and shall be filled with satisfactory non-extruding elastic filler. Where a new section of sidewalk is to connect with a walk previously constructed, or abuts on the curbing, an expansion joint must be made and filled as above provided. Reinforcing bars shall extend ten inches beyond the expansion joint, and the ends shall be wrapped with building paper so that the ten inches shall not be bonded to the concrete. Approved types of slip joints may be used in place of wrapping ends of bars. When wire mesh reinforcing is used, three-eighths-inch round smooth dowel bars not less than 18 inches in length, installed as specified above for bar reinforcing, shall be provided at each expansion joint. 
(h)  Concrete for walks shall have a minimum compressive strength of 2,500 pounds per square inch at 28 days. The quantity of mixing water shall not exceed seven U.S. gallons per sack (94 pounds) of Portland cement. The slump of the concrete shall not exceed four inches. Concrete which has partially set shall not be re-tempered or remixed by adding additional ingredients, but shall be disposed of. All tests for ingredients and concrete shall be made in accordance with the applicable methods of tests of the American Society for Testing Materials. 
(i)  Sidewalks and cross walkways shall have a monolithic finish and shall be floated and troweled to a uniform smooth surface, then finished with a camel hair brush or wood float so as not to be left with a slick or glossy finish. 
(j)  The marking of joints of the top surface must be done with a specially devised marking tool made for such purposes. Edges of the sidewalk and expansion joints shall be rounded with an edger to a radius of one-half inch. 
(k)  The completed walks and drive approaches shall be cured in accordance with good engineering practice. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-157. - Curbs and gutters. 
(a)  Concrete curb or curb and gutter shall be constructed in conformity with the typical sections and to the established lines and grades. 
(b)  Forms may be either metal or well-seasoned wood not less than two inches in thickness. All forms must extend the full depth of the concrete and must be well braced so that the placing and tamping of the concrete will not bulge them. Before concrete is placed, all forms must be thoroughly cleaned and oiled with a heavy form oil or grease. 
(c)  Templates for joints shall be made of steel not less than one-sixteenth inch in thickness and patterned to the shape of the curb or curb and gutter. Templates shall be cleaned and oiled the same as the forms and spaced so as to cut the curb or curb and gutter in sections of not less than eight feet or more than ten feet in length. Steel templates shall extend throughout the entire cross sectional area of curb and gutter. Steel templates for curb shall be six inches wide and extend for a distance of eight inches from the top down. 
(d)  The subgrade shall be excavated so as to have a layer or cushion at least two inches thick of approved material as shown on the typical sections under curbs or curb and gutter. Where the subgrade is rock, adobe, or gravel, 70 percent of which is rock, the cushion need not be used if it is not necessary. In the event the subgrade is undercut, backfilling with earth will not be permitted. Such backfill shall be accomplished with the material used for base on the adjacent street or with other stable material. All such backfill and cushion shall be leveled, wetted, and thoroughly compacted. 
(e)  Where curb and gutter is to be built, base material shall first be applied, spread, and compacted, in accordance with the requirements of the section entitled "Flexible base course," to the full width of the cross section and in the quantities necessary to achieve the elevation of the bottom of the curb and gutter. 
(f)  Curb or curb and gutter shall be reinforced as shown on the typical sections. All steel laps shall be not less than 15 inches. 
(g)  Transverse expansion joints, one-half inch in thickness and extending the full width of the curb or curb and gutter, shall be provided at intervals of not more than 50 feet. 
(h)  Two round smooth steel dowel bars one-half inch in diameter and 18 inches in length shall be installed at each expansion joint in curb and curb and gutter. One nine-inch end of each dowel shall be thoroughly coated with hot oil asphalt or red lead, then wrapped in building paper so that the nine inches shall not be bonded to the concrete. Approved types of slip joints may be used in place of wrapping ends of bars. In curb, the dowels shall be placed on the vertical centerline three inches from the top and bottom. In curb and gutter, the dowels shall be placed as shown on the typical sections. 
(i)  Concrete for curbs or curb and gutter shall have a minimum compressive strength of 3,000 pounds per square inch at 28 days. The quantity of mixing water shall not exceed seven US gallons per sack (94 pounds) of Portland cement. The slump of the concrete shall not exceed four inches. Concrete which has partially set shall not be re-tempered or remixed by adding additional ingredients, but shall be disposed of. All tests for ingredients and concrete shall be made in accordance with the applicable methods of tests of the American Society for Testing Materials. 
(j)  The finish for curb or curb and gutter shall be as specified for sidewalk with all exposed surfaces finished. It shall not be permissible to plaster curb where forms have stayed on overnight. The forms must be removed and the curb finished monolithic the same day as concrete is poured. 
(k)  The completed curb or curb and gutter shall be cured in accordance with good engineering practice. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-158. - Utility trenches. 
    Construct utility trenches in conformance with methods and details specified in the "Work In the Right-of-Way" Ordinance [section 38-155 et seq. of this Code]. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-159. - Drainage structures. 
(a)  All concrete in drainage structures shall develop a compressive strength of not less than 3,000 pounds per square inch at 28 days and shall conform to the requirements of Item 420, Concrete for Structures, of TxDOT's Standard Specifications. 
(b)  All castings shall conform to the requirements of the Standard Specifications for Gray Iron Castings, ASTM Designation A-48 for Class 2 Gray Cast Iron. Castings shall be boldly filleted at angles and the rises shall be sharp and perfect. Castings shall be true to pattern in form and dimensions, free from pouring faults, sponginess, cracks, blow holes, and other defects in positions affecting their strength for the service intended. Bearing surfaces shall be cast with such precision or shall be so machined that perfect bearing will be attained. Manhole covers which rock in the ring will not be accepted. 
(c)  Outlet pipes shall be fitted into the forms with the ends flush with the inside face of the inlet walls, and the concrete shall be placed and rodded around the pipe so as to form a watertight joint. 
(d)  All bridges and culverts shall be designed for an H-20 loading. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Secs. 40-160-40-192. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - SANITARY SEWERS 

Sec. 40-193. - Design criteria. 
    Proposed sanitary sewer mains and collection systems will become a part of the San Antonio Water System (SAWS) infrastructure. All sanitary sewers shall meet SAWS specifications and technical requirements and must be approved and accepted by SAWS. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Secs. 40-194-40-211. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - STORM DRAINAGE DESIGN CRITERIA 

Sec. 40-212. - Run-off calculations. 
(a)  Either SCS methods or the Rational Method may be used for determining peak runoff rates. Peak runoff rates developed by the Rational Method shall be based on the following runoff coefficients:

(b)  Rainfall depths and intensities shall be derived from The Bexar County Infrastructures Services Technical Memorandum IDF Curves for Bexar County dated January 18, 2011. 
(c)  Detention pond design shall be based on methods that generate hydrographs for a 24-hour storm. Acceptable methods include SCS methods, but not the Modified Rational (Austin) Method. Post-development runoff peak discharges shall not exceed pre-development peak discharges under the five-, 25-, and 100-year storm conditions unless it can be demonstrated that the receiving storm water system has adequate capacity for a distance of 2,000 feet downstream of the project site boundary. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-213. - Drainage facilities. 
(a)  Drainage easements and rights-of-way. All drainage facilities, detention ponds, creeks, and watercourses shall be located within drainage easements or public rights-of-way that shall contain the 100-year peak discharge under proposed development conditions. 
(b)  Fencing. Secure detention ponds and vertical drops of 2 feet or greater with fencing or other barrier approved by the City Engineer. Such fencing must be at least 4 feet high. If the fencing has openings, they shall not be large enough to pass a 4-inch-diameter sphere. The fencing shall be fitted with gates that have the capacity to admit maintenance vehicles and shall be securable with locks. 
(c)  Maintenance access. Design all drainage facilities to allow access for maintenance vehicles and personnel. 
(d)  Streets. Streets may be used for storm drainage only if the 25-year peak discharge does not result in a Dangerous condition according to the following chart: 
Travel Conditions on Flooded Roadways 

(e)  Where the 25-year peak discharge causes a street flow depth to exceed a curb height of seven inches, drainage channels or storm sewers shall be provided. 
(f)  Concrete-lined channels. The design of concrete-lined channels shall be based on a 25-year runoff peak and shall comply with the following requirements: 
(1)  The concrete lining shall extend above the depth of the design peak flow water surface by the amount (freeboard) indicated below: 
i.  For flow depths of zero to five feet, the freeboard shall be at least 0.5 feet. 
ii.  For flow depths of five to ten feet, the freeboard shall be at least ten percent of the flow depth. 
iii.  For flow depths in excess of ten feet, the freeboard shall be at least one foot. 
iv.  Earth slopes above the concrete lining shall not exceed three horizontal to one vertical. 
(2)  The average flow velocity during the two-year peak discharge shall be two feet per second or greater. 
(3)  Vertical walls shall not to exceed two feet unless fenced or enclosed. 
(4)  Easements for concrete-lined channels shall extend a minimum of two feet on both sides of the extreme limits of the concrete lining. 
(g)  Earth channels. The design of earth channels shall be based on a 25-year runoff peak and shall comply with the following requirements: 
(1)  Place sod over the entire surface area of the earth channel. 
(2)  The average flow velocity during the 2-year peak discharge shall be two feet per second or greater. 
(3)  The average flow velocity during the 100-year peak discharge shall be six feet per second or less. 
(4)  The side slope shall not be steeper than three horizontal to one vertical. 
(5)  Easements for earth channels shall extend a minimum of two feet on one side and 15 feet on the opposite side beyond the extreme limits of the channel, when such channel does not abut an alley or roadway or provide direct maintenance vehicle access. Otherwise, the easement shall extend a minimum of two feet on both sides of the extreme limits of the channel. 
(h)  Storm sewers. Storm sewers shall be designed on a 25-year peak discharge, flowing under pressure with the energy grade line below the finished ground elevation. The minimum storm sewer diameter is 24 inches. 
(i)  Alleys. Alleys shall be designed to convey the 25-year peak discharge. 
(j)  All-weather crossings. All-weather crossings at streets shall pass the 25-year peak discharge without overtopping the street. All-weather crossings may be overtopped during the 100-year peak discharge as long as the travel condition is not Dangerous (see chart, Travel Conditions on Flooded Roadways, above). 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Secs. 40-214-40-234. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - UTILITY EASEMENTS 

Sec. 40-235. - Required. 
    Each residential block that does not have an alley shall have a utility easement reserved for the use of all public utilities lines, conduits, and equipment. These utility easements shall be 15 feet in width and shall be continuous for the entire length of the block. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-236. - Fencing restrictions. 
(a)  If the owner of the property upon which the utility easement is located desires to use it for lawn purposes, fencing across the easement shall be permitted but gates along the side lot lines must be provided. 
(b)  The gates shall be 15 feet wide (two 7&half-foot gates) and shall be capable of being opened and closed at all times. These gates shall be secured in the center by a drop rod or some similar device which does not obstruct free passage over the easement. The drop rod may be lowered into a drop rod keeper, installed so as to be flush with the ground level. No permanent-type center pole for the gates may be erected on the easement. 
(c)  The gates provided for herein shall remain unlocked at all times. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-237. - Post and chain gates required for ends. 
    Post and chain gates as specified herein shall be installed at the ends of the utility easements and shall be capable of being opened, closed, and locked at all times. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-238. - Duty of property owner to maintain easement; obstruction prohibited. 
    Maintenance of the easement shall be the responsibility of the owner of the property upon which it is located. It shall be the duty of the property owner to keep the area across, over, or under this easement clear of any structure, debris, vegetation, trees, shrubs, or landscaping whatsoever, except that lawn grass, which shall be regularly mowed and controlled, may be grown thereon. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-239. - Curb exposure. 
    Normal curb exposure shall be required where utility easements intersect streets. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-240. - Overhang easements. 
    Overhang easements in all utility easements for electric and telephone lines of at least four feet on each side of the 15-foot easement strip at a height at or above 18 feet shall be provided. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Sec. 40-241. - Curving or deviating rights-of-way. 
    Where utility easements are not themselves straight within each block, or if the same do not connect on a straight course with the utility easements of adjoining blocks, then an additional easement shall be provided for the placing of guy wires on lot division lines in order to support poles set on curving or deviating rights-of-way or alleys. 
( Ord. No. 1121, (att.), 4-8-2014 ) 
Secs. 40-242-40-244. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - ACCESS 

Sec. 40-245. - Street access required. 
    Safe and reliable access to at least one paved street for normal and emergency purposes shall be provided for all platted lots. In zoning districts E, F, FF, G and H, the requirement in this section may be satisfied by means of a shared access easement if such easement is approved by the city council. 
( Ord. No. 2017-09-12-K, 9-12-2017 ) 
Chapter 42 - TAXATION[1] 
Footnotes:

ARTICLE II. - PROPERTY TAXES 

Sec. 42-19. - County to act as tax collector for the city. 
    The tax assessor and appraisal review board of the county appraisal district of the county, of the state, are authorized and directed to act as the tax assessor and appraisal review board of the city as directed by V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 6.41 et seq. The county tax collector is authorized to act as the tax collector for the city. 
(Code 1982, § 24.101; Code 1995, § 24.101)

    All provisions of V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 1.01 et seq. are adopted to the full extent applicable.
