ARTICLE III. - TELECOMMUNICATIONS TAX 

Sec. 42-44. - Adoption of statutes. 
    All provisions of V.T.C.A., Tax Code §§ 6.23(b), 6.24, 31.03(b), and 33.01 are adopted to the full extent applicable. 
(Code 1982, § 24.102.1; Code 1995, § 24.102.1; Ord. No. 75, 9-9-1959) 
Sec. 42-45. - Tax authorized. 
    A tax is authorized on all telecommunications services sold within the city. For purposes of this chapter, the sale of communications services is consummated at the location of the telephone or other telecommunications device from which the call or other communication originates. If the point of origin cannot be determined, the sale is consummated at the address to which the call or other communication is billed. 
(Code 1982, § 24.201; Code 1995, § 24.201; Ord. No. 530, 6-9-1987) 
Sec. 42-46. - Tax rate. 
    The rate of tax imposed by this chapter shall be the same as the rate imposed by the city for all other local sales and use taxes as authorized by the legislature of the state. This tax shall be effective on October 1, 1987. 
(Code 1982, § 24.202; Code 1995, § 24.202; Ord. No. 530, 6-9-1987) 
Chapter 44 - TRAFFIC AND VEHICLES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Rules of the Road, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 541.001 et seq.; powers of local authorities regarding regulation of traffic, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 542.202; limitations on local authorities, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 42.203; municipal authority to regulate parking, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 601.001; municipal streets generally, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 312.001 et seq.; railroad and roadway crossings, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 471.001 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 44-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Alley means the minor ways which are used primarily for vehicular service access to the back or the side of properties otherwise abutting on a street. 
    Ambulance means any privately owned vehicle equipped or used for transporting the wounded, injured, or sick. 
    Authorized emergency vehicle means vehicles of the fire department, police department, and such vehicles of municipal departments, public service corporations, or other organizations which are designated or authorized as emergency vehicles by the chief of police. 
    Barricade means every barrier, obstruction, or block placed upon, or across, any road, street, or highway of this city by an authorized person for the purpose of preventing the passing of motor vehicles over such street, road, or highway during a period of construction or repair to the street, road, or highway. 
    Commercial vehicle means every truck and every private vehicle with the name of the firm represented inscribed or painted on the front door on both sides in letters at least two inches high in contrasting colors to that of the vehicle, which is maintained or used primarily for the transportation of property. 
    Controlled-access highway means every highway, street, or roadway in respect to which owners or occupants of abutting property or lands and other persons have no legal right of access to or from the same, except at such points only and in such manner as may be determined by the public authority having jurisdiction over such highway, street, or roadway. 
    Crosswalk means that part of a roadway at an intersection included within the connections of the lateral lines of the sidewalks on opposite sides of the highway measured from the curbs, or in the absence of curbs from the edges of the traversable roadway. The term "crosswalk" also includes, within the meaning of this chapter, any portion of a roadway at an intersection or elsewhere distinctly indicated for pedestrian crossing by lines or other markings on the surface. 
    Driver means every person who drives, or is in actual physical control of, a vehicle. 
    Driver's license means an authorization issued by a state for the operation of a motor vehicle. The term includes: 
(1)  A temporary license or instruction permit; and 
(2)  An occupational license. 
    Driveway means an entrance to, and exit from, private premises where it is possible to park completely off the street, and which is not open for vehicular traffic except by permission of the owner of such private premises. 
    Golf cart means a motor vehicle designed by the manufacturer primarily for use on a golf course. 
    Handheld mobile communication device means a text-messaging device or other electronic, two-way communication device that is designed to receive and transmit voice communication, text or pictorial communication, or both, whether by internet or other electronic means. The term "handheld mobile communication device" includes a mobile telephone and a personal digital assistant (PDA). 
    Intersection means the area embraced within the prolongation or connection of the lateral curb lines, or, if none, then the lateral boundary lines of the roadways of two highways which join one another at, or approximately at, right angles or the area within which vehicles traveling upon different highways joining at any other angle may come in conflict. 
    Laned roadway means a roadway which is divided into two or more clearly marked lanes for vehicular traffic. 
    Motor vehicle means every vehicle which is self-propelled and every vehicle which is propelled by electric power obtained from overhead trolley wires but not operated upon rails. 
    Motorcycle means every motor vehicle having a saddle for the use of the rider and designed to travel with not more than three wheels in contact with the ground, but excluding a tractor. 
    Motorized cart means those electric and gasoline powered carts, commonly referred to as golf carts, but which must have a minimum of four wheels and which have an attainable top speed not greater than 25 miles per hour on a paved level surface and which is manufactured in compliance with those federal motor vehicle safety standards for low-speed vehicles. Specifically excluded from this definition are those motorized conveyances commonly referred to as UTVs, ATVs, four-wheelers, mules, and gators. 
    Nighttime hours means the period commencing 30 minutes after sunset and ending 30 minutes prior to sunrise. 
    Owner means a person who holds the legal title of a vehicle. In the event a vehicle is the subject of an agreement for the conditional sale or lease with an option to purchase, and with an immediate right of possession vested in the conditional vendee or lessee, such conditional vendee or lessee shall be deemed the owner for the purpose of this chapter. 
    Parking area means those areas accessible to the public by motor vehicular traffic and which are designated for temporary parking of motor vehicles, usually in places referred to as parking lots. 
    Pedestrian means any person afoot. 
    Pole trailer means every vehicle with or without motive power designed to be drawn by another vehicle and attached to the towing vehicle by means of a reach or pole, or by being boomed or otherwise secured to the towing vehicle, and ordinarily used for transporting long or irregularly shaped loads such as poles, pipes, or structural members capable, generally, of sustaining themselves as beams between the supporting connections. 
    Police officer means every officer authorized to direct or regulate traffic or to make arrests for violations of traffic regulations. 
    Private road means every way or place in private ownership and used for vehicular travel by the owner and those having express or implied permission from the owner, but not by other persons. 
    Red flashing emergency light means any lamp mounted on an authorized emergency vehicle or ambulance which displays a red flashing light, visible under normal atmospheric conditions from a distance of 500 feet from such vehicle. 
    Right-of-way means the privilege of the immediate use of the roadway. 
    Roadway means that portion of a street or highway improved, designed, or ordinarily used for vehicular travel. In the event a highway includes two or more separate roadways, the term "roadway" refers to any such roadway separately but not to all such roadways collectively. 
    School bus means every motor vehicle owned by any private, public, or governmental agency and operated for the transportation of children to, or from, school; provided, however, the term "school bus" does not include motor vehicles which do not conform to the rules, regulations, and standards established by the state department of education in regard to color and marking, nor shall it include any vehicle constituting a part of the fleet of any street transportation company serving the public generally. 
    School crossing zone means that portion of any street or public property or way within or without any school zone which the traffic engineer may designate for the crossing of those attending a school or other institution of learning. 
    School or other institution of learning means any public or private organization giving regular instruction and having an average daily attendance of 50 students or more. 
    School zone means each and every street and all public property or ways within 1,000 feet of the boundaries of any school or other institution of learning. 
    Semitrailer means every vehicle with or without motive power, other than a pole trailer, designed for carrying persons or property and for being drawn by a motor vehicle and so constructed that some part of its weight and that of its load rests upon, or is carried by, another vehicle. 
    Sidewalk means that portion of a street between the curb lines, or the lateral lines, of a roadway and the adjacent property lines intended for the use of pedestrians. 
    Slow-moving-vehicle emblem means a triangular emblem that conforms to standards and specifications under Section 547.104 and displayed in accordance with Section 547.703 of the Texas Transportation Code. 
    Street or highway means the entire width between the boundary lines of every way publicly maintained when any part thereof is open to the use of the public for purposes of vehicular traffic. 
    Text message means a two-way communication (whether real time or asynchronous) in which data (composed in whole or in part of text, numbers, images, or symbols) is sent, entered, or received by a method other than by voice and transmitted through either a short message service (SMS) or a computer network. 
    Through highway means every street or highway or portion thereof at entrances to which vehicular traffic from the intersecting streets or highways is required by law to either stop or yield the right-of-way before entering or crossing. 
    Through truck traffic, with reference to truck traffic that is regulated in this chapter, means the driving or entry of a truck onto the a city street at any point, the proceeding of such truck upon and along the same, and the leaving of such truck at any point, unless the person driving or operating the truck has occasion to, and does, bring the truck to a stop at some point, place, or location upon the way for the purpose of loading or unloading or rendering a service at in connection with the business for which the truck is used. 
    Traffic means pedestrians, ridden or herded animals, vehicles, buses and other conveyances, either singly or together, in and during the act of using any street for purposes of travel or movement. 
    Traffic control device means any electric traffic control signals, stop signs, yield right-of-way signs, and any other such device designed and used to control the movement of traffic. 
    Trafficway is any land way open to the public as a matter of right or custom for moving persons or property from one place to another. The trafficway includes all property, both improved and unimproved, between the property lines of a roadway system. 
    Trailer means every vehicle with or without motive power, other than a pole trailer, designed for carrying persons or property and for being drawn by a motor vehicle and so constructed that no part of its weight rests upon the towing vehicle. 
    Truck means every motor vehicle designed, used, or maintained primarily for the transportation of property. 
    Truck tractor means every motor vehicle designed and used primarily for drawing other vehicles, and not so constructed as to carry a load other than a part of the weight of the vehicle and load so drawn. 
    Utility task vehicle is a motor vehicle that is not a golf cart or lawn mower. It is equipped with side-by-side seating for the use of the operator and passenger(s), designed to propel itself with at least four tires in contact with the ground, designed by the manufacturer for off-highway use only; and designed by the manufacturer primarily for utility work and not for recreational purposes. 
    Vehicle means every device in, upon, or by which any person or property is, or may be, transported or drawn upon a highway, except devices used exclusively upon stationary rails or tracks. 
    Warning sign means every sign, signal, marking, and device erected or placed upon any street, road, highway, or barricade, or erected or placed upon any street, road, or highway within the city which is under construction or being repaired, for the purpose of regulating, warning, or guiding traffic or otherwise stating the conditions under which traffic by motor vehicle may be had upon such street, road, or highway. The term "warning sign" includes, but shall not be limited to, a flagman placed upon any street, road, or highway for the purpose of directing traffic around or upon such street, road, or highway as is under construction or in the process of being repaired. 
    Wireless telephone service means two-way, real time voice telecommunications service that is interconnected to a public switched telephone network and is commonly referred to as cellular service or personal communication service. 
( Ord. No. 2016-05-10A, 5-10-2016 ) 
Sec. 44-2. - Table of traffic schedules. 
    The city maintains a table of traffic schedules, as amended from time to time, which is available in the office of the city secretary. The table has schedules related to the following topics: 
(1)  Through streets. 
(2)  Turns prohibited at certain street intersections. 
(3)  One-way traffic. 
(4)  Single, three-way and four-way stop streets. 
(5)  Stop sign exits. 
(6)  Yield intersections. 
(7)  School buses and zones. 
(8)  Speed zones. 
(9)  Weight and load restrictions. 
(10)  Specific streets and highways. 
(11)  Exceptions. 
(12)  Parking restrictions on certain streets. 
(Code 1982, §§ 25.101-25.107; Code 1995, §§ 25.101-25.107; Ord. No. 2016-01-12, 1-12-2016 ) 
Secs. 44-3-44-22. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT 

Sec. 44-23. - Authority of police and fire departments. 
(a)  It shall be the duty of the officers of the police department, or such officers as are assigned by the chief of police, to enforce all of the traffic provisions of this Code and all of the state vehicle laws applicable to street traffic in this city. 
(b)  Officers of the police department, or such officers as are assigned by the chief of police, are authorized to direct all traffic by voice, hand, or signal in conformance with traffic laws; provided that in the event of a fire or other emergency, or to expedite traffic, or to safeguard pedestrians, officers of the police department may direct traffic as conditions may require, notwithstanding the provisions of the traffic laws. 
(c)  Officers of the fire department, when at the scene of a fire, may direct or assist the police in directing traffic threat or in the immediate vicinity. 
(Code 1982, § 25.201; Code 1995, § 25.201) 
Sec. 44-24. - Obedience to police and fire department officials. 
    No person shall willfully fail or refuse to comply with any lawful order or direction of a police officer, or fire department official. 
(Code 1982, § 25.202; Code 1995, § 25.202) 
Sec. 44-25. - Towing of vehicles violating state financial responsibility law. 
    To ensure compliance with state financial responsibility laws, police officers of the city are authorized to require the towing off of public streets and roadways of motor vehicles found to be operating within the city without the financial responsibility required by state law. 
(Code 1995, § 25.1201; Ord. No. 1057, 10-12-2010) 
Secs. 44-26-44-53. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Traffic signs, signals and markings generally, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 544.001 et seq.; sign manual, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 544.001; traffic signals and signs in municipalities, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 553.002. 

Sec. 44-54. - State traffic manual adopted. 
    All traffic control devices, including signs, signals and markings, relating to pavement or curb, installed or used for the purpose of directing and controlling traffic within the city shall conform with the state Manual on Uniform Traffic Control Devices for Streets and Highways, Volumes I and II. All signs, signals and markings erected or used by the city shall be uniform and be located so far as practicable according to the directions shown in the manual throughout the city. All existing traffic control devices and those erected in the future by the city being consistent with the manual, state law and this article shall constitute official traffic control devices. 
State Law reference- State sign manual authorized, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 544.001; municipal authority to install traffic control devices, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 544.002. 
Sec. 44-55. - Avoidance of traffic control devices and controlled intersections. 
(a)  At the intersection of any streets at which vehicular traffic is controlled by an authorized traffic control device, it is unlawful for any person to drive any vehicle across the sidewalk area or across private property at such intersection to avoid complying with such traffic control device. 
(b)  It is unlawful for the operator of any motor vehicle, automobile, motor scooter, motorcycle, truck, carriage, bicycle, or vehicle whatever to cut across or drive across or traverse any private or public property, driveway, median, parkway, or easement whatever in order to short-cut an intersection or side-street or in order to proceed across such private or public property from one public street, road, or way, to the same public street, road, or way, or to another. 
(Code 1982, §§ 25.301, 25.1301; Code 1995, §§ 25.301, 25.1301) 
State Law reference- Compliance with traffic control devices required, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 544.004; interference with traffic control devices and railroad signs and signals prohibited, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 544.005. 
Sec. 44-56. - U-turns in business district prohibited; exception. 
    The driver of any vehicle shall not turn such vehicle so as to proceed in the opposite direction upon any street in a business district or at any intersection controlled by a traffic control signal, with the exception Northwest Military Highway (FM 1535) northbound at Lemonwood; nor shall any driver so turn a vehicle upon any other street unless such movement can be made in safety without interfering with other traffic. 
(Code 1982, § 25.302; Code 1995, § 25.302; Ord. No. 1066, 2-8-2011) 
Sec. 44-57. - Electric traffic control signal locations. 
(a)  Electric traffic control signals are situated at the following intersections: 
(1)  Interstate Highway 410 frontage road with West Avenue. 
(2)  Interstate Highway 410 frontage road with Honeysuckle Lane. 
(3)  Northwest Military Highway (Farm to Market Highway No. 1535) with West Avenue. 
(4)  Northwest Military Highway (Farm to Market Highway No. 1535) with Lemonwood Drive. 
(5)  Northwest Military Highway (Farm to Market Highway No. 1535) with Carolwood Drive. 
(6)  Northwest Military Highway (Farm to Market Highway No. 1535) with Winston Lane. 
(b)  The intersections listed in subsection (a) of this section are established as official full signal operations at such street intersections. Such traffic controls are expressly found to conform to the state highway commission's manual and specifications. The driver of a vehicle approaching the intersection shall obey the signal in accordance with state law. 
(Code 1982, § 25.303; Code 1995, § 25.303; Ord. No. 898, 8-14-2001) 
Secs. 44-58-44-87. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - STREETS AND ALLEY USE DESIGNATIONS 

Sec. 44-88. - Interstate Highway 410; frontage and access roads. 
(a)  Any person operating a motor vehicle along Interstate Highway 410, or any of its connection roads or ramps, shall operate such vehicle in the direction as designated by the state highway department, and as marked by appropriate signs installed by the state highway department. 
(b)  Any person operating a motor vehicle along a frontage, access, or connection road of Interstate Highway 410, and in a lane thereof designated by the state highway department and marked by appropriate signs as a "left lane must turn left" or "right lane must turn right" lane, shall continue in such lane when thus marked, and not leave the same except to complete such left turn or right turn, respectively, as commanded by the signs, and shall make such turn as commanded, and not continue in such lane beyond the intersection of turning thus indicated. 
(Code 1982, § 25.401; Code 1995, § 25.401; Ord. No. 51, 12-12-1957; Ord. No. 114, 2-14-1961) 
Secs. 44-89-44-119. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - RULES OF THE ROAD[3] 
Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- General rule of uniformity of traffic laws, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 542.201; power of local authorities to regulate and enforce, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 542.202; limitations on local authority, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 542.203; limitations on municipalities, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 542.2035; powers related to intersections, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 542.204. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 44-120. - Rules of the road; state law adopted. 
    Unless otherwise provided, the law of the road of the state is hereby adopted, and the rights-of-way and provisions therein set forth are here adopted for all and general purposes. 
State Law reference- Rules of the road, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 541.001 et seq. 
Sec. 44-121. - Use of hand-held mobile communication devices. 
(a)  A person commits an offense if the person uses a hand-held mobile communication device to send, read, or write a text message, view pictures or written text, whether transmitted by internet or other electronic means, engage in gaming or any other use of the device, besides dialing telephone numbers or talking to another person, while operating a moving motor vehicle. This section shall not apply to public safety personnel in the normal course and scope of performing their duties. 
(b)  It is an affirmative defense to prosecution of an offense under this section if a hand-held mobile communication device is used: 
(1)  While the vehicle is stopped, out of the moving lanes of the roadway; 
(2)  Strictly to engage in a telephone conversation, including dialing or deactivating the call; 
(3)  As a global positioning or navigation system that is affixed to the vehicle; 
(4)  To communicate with an emergency response operator, a fire department, a law enforcement agency, a hospital, a physician's office, or a health clinic regarding a medical or other emergency situation to prevent injury to a person or property; 
(5)  In the reasonable belief that a person's life or safety is in immediate danger; or 
(6)  Solely in a voice-activated or other hands-free mode. 
(c)  An offense under this section is not a moving violation and may not be made a part of a person's driving record or insurance record. 
(d)  In addition to enforcement by a peace officer of the city, this section may be enforced by a peace officer of another entity, including those employed by school districts, duly authorized to issue traffic citations within the city. 
(Code 1995, § 25.1601; Ord. No. 1067, 2-8-2011) 
Secs. 44-122-44-140. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - SPEED REGULATIONS[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
State Law reference- Speed restrictions generally, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 545.351 et seq.; prima facie speed limits, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 545.352; authority of municipalities to alter speed limits, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 545.356; conflicting designated speed limits, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 545.359; special speed limitations, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 545.361; temporary speed limits, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 545.362; minimum speed regulations, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 545.363; exception for emergency vehicles and authority of municipality to regulation speed of ambulances, emergency medical services vehicles, and blood or tissue bank vehicles, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 545.365. 

Sec. 44-141. - Basis for determination of city speed limits. 
    As the result of traffic and engineering surveys heretofore conducted by the city police department as to each of the streets and thoroughfares hereinafter referred to, the maximum prima facie safe, reasonable, and prudent speed limits for motor vehicles on all streets and thoroughfares within the corporate limits of the city except for interstate Highway 410 and Farm to Market Highway No. 1535, are determined to be as provided in this article. 
(Code 1982, § 25.801; Code 1995, § 25.801; Ord. No. 788, 5-14-1996) 
State Law reference- Authority of municipalities to alter speed limits, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 545.356. 
Sec. 44-142. - Speed limits applicable to all city streets and alleys. 
    Except as otherwise specifically provided in this article, the prima facie maximum reasonable or prudent speed limit on all streets and public thoroughfares in the city shall be 30 miles per hour and the prima facie maximum reasonable or prudent speed limits on any public alley or alleyway or utility easement or easement right-of-way within the city shall be 15 miles per hour. 
(Code 1982, §§ 25.801.2, 25.803; Code 1995, §§ 25.801.2, 25.803; Ord. No. 232, 8-11-1964; Ord. No. 243, 5-11-1965) 
Secs. 44-143-44-155. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - MOTORIZED CARTS 

Sec. 44-156. - Applicability. 
    The provisions of this division shall apply to all motorized carts operated upon public streets and rights-of-ways within the City of Castle Hills except that the operation of motorized carts is not subject to the provisions of this article on private property, with the consent of the owner, or within gated or limited access communities unless the streets of the community are dedicated for public use and maintained by the city, or in connection with a parade, a festival or other special event provided the consent of the sponsor is obtained and provided such motorized cart is only used during such event. 
    The use of UTVs by city officials and personnel for official business on city owned property and city leased property is authorized. 
( Ord. No. 2016-05-10A, § 2, 5-10-2016 ) 
Sec. 44-157. - Electric and gasoline motorized cart required equipment. 
(a)  Every motorized cart must be equipped, as mandated by the Texas Transportation Code, Section 547.703, Section 551.404(b) with the following: 
(1)  Operational headlamps; 
(2)  Operational tail lamps; 
(3)  Side reflectors; 
(4)  Operational parking brake; 
(5)  Rearview mirror(s); (capable of a clear unobstructed view of at least 200 feet to the rear); 
(6)  Slow-moving-vehicle emblem; and 
(7)  Horn (must be audible for a distance of 200 feet in compliance with Texas Transportation Code, Section 547.501). 
(b)  All required equipment shall meet Texas and federal motor vehicle safety standards. 
( Ord. No. 2016-05-10A, § 2, 5-10-2016 ) 
Sec. 44-158. - Gasoline carts. 
    Every motorized cart powered by gasoline shall at all times be equipped with an exhaust system in good working order and in constant operation and meeting the following specifications: 
(1)  The exhaust system shall include the piping leading from the flange of the exhaust manifold to and including the muffler and exhaust pipes or including any and all parts specified by the manufacturer. 
(2)  The exhaust system and its elements shall be securely fastened with brackets or hangers, which are designed for the particular purpose of fastening motorized cart exhaust systems 
(3)  The engine and powered mechanism of every motorized cart shall be so equipped, adjusted and tuned so that the exhaust is in good working order. 
(4)  It shall be unlawful for the owner of any motorized cart to operate or permit the operation of such cart on which any device controlling or abating atmospheric emissions which is placed on a cart by the manufacturer is rendered unserviceable by removal, alteration or which interferes with its operation. 
( Ord. No. 2016-05-10A, § 2, 5-10-2016 ) 
Sec. 44-159. - Operational regulations. 
(a)  All drivers of motorized carts shall hold a valid driver's license and shall abide by all traffic regulations applicable to vehicular traffic when using the authorized streets and parking areas of the city. 
(b)  Motorized carts shall not be operated on any sidewalk, pedestrian walkway, jogging path, park trail or any location normally used for pedestrian traffic except for official police business or by Castle Hills officials and personnel conducting official business. 
(c)  No person may operate a motorized cart upon any portion of a street or trafficway having a posted speed greater than 35 m.p.h. 
(d)  All motorized carts are entitled to a full use of a lane on the authorized streets and parking areas of the city and no motor vehicle shall be driven in such a manner as to deprive any motorized cart of the full use of a lane. 
(e)  The driver of a motorized cart shall not overtake and pass in the same lane occupied by the vehicle being overtaken. 
(f)  No driver shall operate a motorized cart between lanes of traffic or between adjacent lines or rows of vehicles. 
(g)  The number of occupants in a motorized cart shall be limited to the number of persons for whom factory seating is installed and provided on the motorized cart. The operator and all occupants shall be seated upon the seat of the motorized cart and no part of the body of the operator or occupant shall extend outside the perimeter of the motorized cart while the motorized cart is being operated. The operator shall not permit any occupant of the cart to ride in the lap of any occupant while the cart is in motion. 
(h)  Children must be properly seated while a cart is in motion and may not be transported in a reckless or negligent manner. No person younger than six years of age may be transported in a motorized cart unless restrained by a safety belt restraint. 
(i)  Motorized carts may only be parked in the same manner and at the same places designated for the parking of motor vehicles. The stopping, standing or parking of motorized carts in areas where parking is not allowed or in any place that impedes the flow of traffic, pedestrian walkways or a passageway is prohibited. Motorized carts shall not park within any space designated for disabled persons unless a current disabled parking placard is displayed and the person to whom the placard was issued is operating or being transported by the cart. 
(j)  Motorized carts may not be used to tow a person on roller skates, skateboard or bicycle. 
(k)  Motorized carts shall not be operated on NW Military Hwy and West Ave unless crossing the highway/roadway. 
(l)  Motorized carts shall not be operated on NW Loop 410 or frontage road. 
( Ord. No. 2016-05-10A, § 2, 5-10-2016 ) 
Sec. 44-160. - Liability. 
    Any owner of a motorized cart operated on public streets and rights-of-ways of the City of Castle Hills shall maintain liability insurance for any injuries or property damage caused by the use of such owner's motorized cart in the city. 
Nothing  in this section shall be construed as an assumption of liability by the City of Castle Hills for any injuries to persons, pets or property which may result from the operation of a motorized cart by an authorized driver. 
    Owners are fully liable and accountable for the actions of any individual that they provide permission to operate and drive said motorized cart, both on personal and/or city and public properties. This described liability responsibility especially applies to personal injuries or property damage resulting from motorized cart drivers who are minors under the age of 18 with or without a current and valid Texas driver's license. 
( Ord. No. 2016-05-10A, § 2, 5-10-2016 ) 
Sec. 44-161. - Penalties. 
    Any person who violates the provisions of this article shall upon conviction, be punished according to the general penalties described in section 1-17. 
Secs. 44-162-44-167. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - PARKING[5] 

Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
State Law reference- Stopping, standing and parking generally, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 545.301; parking, towing and storage of vehicles, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 681.001 et seq. 

Sec. 44-168. - Lights required for night parking. 
    It is unlawful for any person to park a motor vehicle on any street or alley within the limits of the city during the nighttime hours and remain in such vehicle without displaying parking lights on such motor vehicle. 
(Code 1982, § 25.1001; Code 1995, § 25.1001; Ord. No. 7, 11-1-1951) 
Sec. 44-169. - Direction; proximity to curbline. 
    No person shall stand or park a vehicle of any kind in a street or roadway in the city other than parallel with the edge of the roadway headed in the lane and direction of lawful traffic movement and with the wheels of the vehicle within 18 inches of the curb or edge of the roadway. 
(Code 1982, § 25.1004; Code 1995, § 25.1004; Ord. No. 125, 5-23-1961) 
Sec. 44-170. - Truck-tractor, semi-trailer, pole-trailer and trailer parking prohibited. 
    It is unlawful to park any truck-tractor, semi-trailer, pole-trailer, or trailer, either singularly or a combination of both, on any residential street for any length of time except when actually loading or unloading property. 
(Code 1982, § 25.1015; Code 1995, § 25.1015) 
State Law reference- Overnight parking of commercial motor vehicles in or near residential subdivisions, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 545.307. 
Sec. 44-171. - Alleys. 
    It is unlawful to park any automobile, vehicle, car, truck, motorcycle, motor scooter, or powered conveyance, or any kind of trailer, in any alley in the city at any time, or for any length of time, during the day or night. 
(Code 1982, § 25.1002; Code 1995, § 25.1002; Ord. No. 533, 8-11-1987) 
Sec. 44-172. - Driveways. 
    No person shall stand or park a vehicle in any manner which shall block or impede free vehicular ingress and egress to all public and private driveways lawfully opening into any city street, roadway, or alley. 
(Code 1982, § 25.1005; Code 1995, § 25.1005; Ord. No. 125, 5-23-1961) 
Sec. 44-173. - Expressways. 
    No person shall stand or park a motor vehicle on the roadway portion of the expressway located within the city limits. No person shall stand or park any motor vehicle on the untraveled portion of the expressway located within the city limits, except for repairs necessitated by an emergency, and in no event for a period in excess of two hours. Equipment owned by governmental agencies, or their contractors, while being used in the performance of authorized duties on the expressway with the city is exempted from the provisions of this section. 
(Code 1995, § 25.1016; Ord. No. 749, 11-8-1994; Ord. No. 1047, 1-12-2010) 
Sec. 44-174. - Frontage roads. 
    The frontage roads shall be signed as no parking areas at intervals, as indicated on state highway department map "I.H. 410 and Loop 410 Control: 521-4 from: Glencrest Drive To: Blanco Road," on file in the city office, which is incorporated herein by reference. 
(Code 1982, § 25.1007.1; Code 1995, § 25.1007.1) 
Sec. 44-175. - Overnight parking on paved streets. 
    The parking or storing of cars, trucks, tractors, or other vehicles on paved streets during the hours from 2:00 a.m. to 5:00 a.m., except temporarily disabled vehicles that are protected by flares or other approved signal devices, is prohibited. 
(Code 1982, § 25.1201; Code 1995, § 25.1203; Ord. No. 756, 3-14-1995) 
State Law reference- Overnight parking of commercial motor vehicles in or near residential subdivisions, V.T.C.A., Transportation Code § 545.307. 
Sec. 44-176. - Permits for temporary overnight parking. 
(a)  Any person owning or occupying residential premises may obtain a temporary overnight parking permit for visitors or persons temporarily staying in such premises upon written application made and filed with the chief of police prior to the time such automobiles or other vehicles are parked on the street. No such permit shall exceed 30 days, and no more than three such permits may by issued for any premises during any calendar year by the chief of police. 
(b)  To be effective, any such permit shall be in writing and displayed on the automobile at all times when parked on the streets of the city between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 5:00 a.m. 
(c)  Permits under this section shall be granted by the chief of police upon a showing that the premises do not have adequate space for the parking of automobiles of persons temporarily visiting or occupying such premises and the person making such application cannot without undue hardship obtain off-street parking within the vicinity of such property. 
(d)  In determining whether or not a hardship exists, the chief of police shall consider the cost of providing off-street parking on the premises so owned or occupied and the cost and availability for providing for such automobile or automobiles off-street parking on other premises and the proximity of other premises that might be available to such occupants for off-street parking. 
(Code 1982, § 25.1202; Code 1995, § 25.1204; Ord. No. 708, 5-14-1992; Ord. No. 709, 7-14-1992; Ord. No. 756, 3-14-1995) 
Sec. 44-177. - Parking of vehicles on vacant lots. 
(a)  No motor vehicles, trailers, semi-trailers, house trailers, commercial vehicles, trucks, busses, or boats of any type, operable or inoperable, may be parked on any vacant lot under any circumstances, except as follows: 
(1)  Such vehicles, trailers, or boats must be confined to the rear one-third of such vacant lot. 
(2)  Such vehicles, trailers or boats thus located on the rear of such lot must be completely screened from view on all four sides to a height of at least six feet but not more than eight feet, no more and no less, by permanent and attractive screening or fencing of a type and height to be approved by the city manager at the time of the issuance of the requisite fence permit. 
(b)  In the event of conflict between this section and the city zoning regulations, the zoning regulations shall be controlling. 
(Code 1982, § 28.107; Code 1995, § 28.107; Ord. No. 961, 11-8-2005) 
Sec. 44-178. - Parking restrictions on certain streets on school days only between 8:00 a.m. and 4:00 p.m. 
    It is unlawful to park any automobile, vehicle, truck, motorcycle or other powered conveyance, or any kind of trailer, on school days only between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and 4:00 p.m. in the locations listed in the table of traffic schedules maintained in the office of the city secretary as provided in section 44-2. No parking signs or red curbs designating the no parking locations shall be installed advising the public of the location of the no parking zones. Violations of this section shall be enforced by citations and/or by the towing of any vehicles or trailers found in violation of this section. 
( Ord. No. 2016-01-12, 1-12-2016 ) 
Secs. 44-179-44-207. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - HAZARDOUS MATERIALS TRANSPORT 

Sec. 44-208. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    County terminal means a business or other location within the boundaries of the county which business or location serves as a point of origination or receipt for shipments of NRHM. 
    Local delivery of regulated materials means transportation that originates in the county or is bound for delivery in the county or both. 
    Nonradioactive hazardous material (NRHM) means those nonradioactive materials classified as hazardous by the federal government through the secretary of transportation pursuant to his authority under 49 USC 1801 et seq. 
    Nonradioactive hazardous materials (NRHM) transportation means motor vehicle transportation or non-radioactive hazardous materials in such quantities that the vehicle is required to carry and exhibit placards pursuant to 49 CFR 172. 
    NRHM (nonradioactive hazardous materials) vehicle means a vehicle transporting regulated materials and subject to provisions and regulations of this article. 
    Prohibited nonradioactive hazardous materials local delivery route means all streets and public highways and segments of streets and public highways within the city except for IH-410 eastbound and westbound lanes between Jackson Keller and Blanco Roads and West Avenue and NW Military Highway. 
    Prohibited nonradioactive hazardous materials through transportation route means all streets and public highways and segments of streets and public highways within the city except for IH-410 eastbound and westbound lanes between Jackson Keller and Blanco Roads. 
    Requiring placards, when used to describe a vehicle, means any vehicle transporting hazardous materials in sufficient quantity to require placarding as set forth in the federal department of transportation hazardous materials regulations at 49 USC 1801 et seq. 
    Regulated materials means nonradioactive hazardous materials of the character regulated by this article and affected by this local nonradioactive hazardous materials route regulation. 
    Through traffic transportation means transportation of regulated materials that originates outside of the county and involves no deliveries or pickups in the county. 
(Code 1995, § 25.1501) 
Sec. 44-209. - Enforcement and penalties. 
(a)  Officers of the fire department having citation authority under state law and officers of the police department are expressly authorized to enforce the provisions of this article, as are other peace officers with jurisdiction to enforce the laws and ordinances of the city and state on public roadways within the city. 
(b)  Violation of any of the provisions of this article shall constitute an offense punishable by a fine of not less than $500.00 and not more than $2,000.00. 
(c)  The city shall be entitled to pursue all remedies, at law and in equity, including but not limited to injunctive relief, with attendant civil penalties as may be provided under state statute, which remedies shall be cumulative of the criminal laws, none of which shall be mutually exclusive of the other. 
(Code 1995, § 25.1511; Ord. No. 905, 11-13-2001) 
Sec. 44-210. - Routes restricted. 
(a)  No person shall transport, contract, or arrange, or participate in the transport, contract, or arrangement to transport nonradioactive hazardous materials within the corporate boundaries of the city unless his destination or point of departure is a county terminal. 
(b)  Local delivery transportation of nonradioactive hazardous material is permitted only on the eastbound and westbound lanes of IH-410 within the corporate limits of the city and on NW Military Highway and West Avenue within the city. 
(c)  Through transportation of nonradioactive hazardous material is permitted only on the eastbound and westbound lanes of IH-410 within the corporate limits of the city. 
(d)  Except for those routes for through transportation and local delivery permitted in this section, both through transportation or local delivery of nonradioactive hazardous material is prohibited within the city. 
(Code 1995, §§ 25.1502-25.1505) 
Sec. 44-211. - Placard requirements. 
    The operator of a vehicle used to transport hazardous materials requiring placards shall apply and display appropriate placards meeting federal department of transportation specifications on each end and each side of the vehicle. 
(Code 1995, § 25.1507(1)) 
Sec. 44-212. - Pre-operation inspection required. 
    Before operation the vehicle operator shall inspect the vehicle to determine that the brakes, tires and steering mechanism are in good working condition, the electrical wiring is well insulated and firmly secured, and the vehicle is in a condition adequate to safely transport hazardous materials. 
(Code 1995, § 25.1507(2)) 
Sec. 44-213. - Police department discretion and public safety. 
(a)  The police department may temporarily suspend the operation of some or any vehicles carrying regulated nonradioactive hazardous materials, without notice whenever road, weather, traffic, or other exigent circumstances warrant such action. 
(b)  The police department may redirect through traffic vehicles carrying regulated nonradioactive hazardous materials onto any highway or roadway, public or private, when the through traffic route is blocked for any reason, or in response to any exigent circumstance, which police direction for benefit of public safety shall have authority of law. 
(Code 1995, § 25.1508) 
Sec. 44-214. - Exception for emergency response vehicle carrying fuel. 
    It shall be permissible and an affirmative defense to violation of this article that the vehicle carrying a regulated material is carrying fuel directly to the scene of an emergency, or for a public emergency purpose, specific to the function of fueling equipment used to respond to or address the emergency. 
(Code 1995, § 25.1509) 
Sec. 44-215. - Exceptions applicable to empty vehicles. 
(a)  The routing and placarding requirements of this article shall not apply to an empty vehicle that has been used previously to transport regulated materials provided the vehicle meets the requirements of this section. 
(b)  A vehicle that has transported nonradioactive hazardous materials in bulk packaging or in any other type of container and is required to be placarded pursuant to 49 CFR 172 must and shall remain placarded when it is empty unless it is sufficiently cleaned of residue and purged of vapors to remove any potential hazard or refilled with a material requiring different placards or no placards, to such an extent that any residue remaining in the packaging is no longer hazardous. 
(Code 1995, § 25.1506) 
Sec. 44-216. - Parking and standing. 
    No vehicle transporting regulated nonradioactive hazardous materials may park or stand at any location with the city except for purposes of load or unloading except vehicles parked in designated truck parking areas of locations providing food, fuel, rest, safe haven, or repair and vehicles parked in the parking areas of businesses engaged in the transportation, storage or production of hazardous materials. 
(Code 1995, § 25.1510) 
Chapter 46 - UTILITIES[1] 
(RESERVED) 
Footnotes:
